**2026-07-18 — Two follow-up fixes from the same day's earlier audits, both now fully verified live end-to-end (Docker came up mid-session): (1) `sort_order` standardized to TINYINT schema-wide + GUI negative/overflow guard (V121) — took 4 live-DB iterations to get right, each one a real bug live verification actually caught. (2) Backend Java null-safety audit — clean, zero exploitable NPEs, full 194-test suite green against the migrated live DB.**
- **sort_order → TINYINT (V121), verified live — 4 real bugs caught by actually running it, not by review**:
  1. **DEFAULT constraint blocks ALTER COLUMN**: every `sort_order DEFAULT 0` backs an auto-generated unnamed SQL Server default constraint (e.g. `DF__connectio__sort___3AB788A8`); SQL Server refuses `ALTER COLUMN` on any column with a dependent default, named or not. First live attempt failed on the very first table; Flyway's whole-migration transaction rolled back cleanly, no partial damage. Fixed by finding each table's unnamed default dynamically via `sys.default_constraints` (name isn't predictable/portable), dropping it, then re-adding it afterward with an explicit name (`df_<table>_sort_order`) so this can't recur.
  2. **3 of the original 44 tables don't exist in the live DB at all**: `external_system_type`, `custom_config`, `commodity_instrument_map` were all found by the original audit's `sort_order` grep, but each was later `DROP TABLE`'d by a subsequent migration (V106, V17, V115 respectively — V115's drop was already documented in this doc's own V113-session entry). This was a mistake in the original 44-table list, not live drift — corrected by excluding all three, leaving 41 tables. Also added `DROP INDEX IF EXISTS` throughout as cheap insurance against the same class of mistake for indexes.
  3. **Real data exceeds TINYINT's 255 cap**: `screen_field_registry` (38 of 60 rows) and `object_lock_rule` use a deliberate "hundreds" gap-numbering scheme (900/910/920/930 for `TRADE_BLOTTER`'s `agriDetail` fields, 800s for `metalsDetail`, etc. — room to insert a field into a group later without renumbering everything) — populated by the application after the original seed, so the earlier "grepped all 120 migrations' INSERT literals, none approach 255" check was correct but insufficient (it only checked seed data, not live application data). **Asked the user rather than deciding silently** (`AskUserQuestion`: keep these two as SMALLINT vs. renumber to fit vs. leave untouched) — user chose to renumber and keep TINYINT uniform everywhere. Added a sequential per-`screen_code` renumbering step (`ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY screen_code ORDER BY sort_order, <pk>) - 1`) immediately before each table's `ALTER COLUMN`, deliberately giving up the gap-space design intent per the user's explicit choice.
  4. Final result: `V121__sort_order_tinyint_standardization.sql` (mirrored to `database/121_...sql`) narrows 41 `sort_order` columns (4 that were plain `INT`, 37 that were `SMALLINT`) to `TINYINT` — 30 of the 41 have a covering index (`DROP INDEX IF EXISTS` → `ALTER COLUMN` → `CREATE INDEX`), the other 11 are a direct `ALTER COLUMN`.
  - **Entity-side**: 4 dedicated JPA entities had `sortOrder` as `Integer` (`AppModule`, `AppFunction`, `ScreenFieldRegistry`, `ObjectLockRule`) — changed to `Short`, matching the convention `StorageFacilityType`/`CommodityInstrumentMapEntry` already used. The other 37 tables are Tier2-generic (`referencedata` package reads column types dynamically) — no Java change needed. Two response-DTO records (`EffectiveFieldPermissionsResponse`, `ProfileDetailResponse`) use primitive `int sortOrder` — left as-is, `Short` auto-widens to `int` safely.
  - **GUI-side**: `features/tier2/ReferenceDataTable.tsx`'s generic `fieldControl()` renderer (covers all 37 Tier2-generic tables) now special-cases `col.name === 'sortOrder'` to add `min={0} max={255}` on the `InputNumber`. No dedicated-entity table (the 4 above) has a live GUI edit form at all — RBAC/field-permission admin config is seed/migration-only — so the Tier2 fix is complete GUI-side coverage.
  - **Verified live, for real**: backend booted clean against the live DB (`Started EtrmBackendApplication`), `flyway_schema_history` confirms V121 `success=1`, spot-checked 7 tables' actual `sys.types` show `tinyint`, confirmed all 30 recreated indexes exist, confirmed `screen_field_registry` renumbered to a clean `MIN=0 MAX=59 DISTINCT=60` with no collisions, live `GET /api/v1/reference-data/deal_type` round-trip returns correct data with real JWT auth, and the **full 194-test suite passes clean** (silent success under `mvn -q`, zero `[ERROR]` lines — the many `Data integrity violation` WARN log lines during the run are `ReferenceDataCrudSmokeTest` intentionally exercising bad-input error paths, not failures) run against this same migrated live DB, not a separate test schema.
- **Null-safety audit (Java backend, per explicit user follow-up question "which layer" → "Backend Java NPE risks")**: methodically checked the highest-risk categories in a financial backend, each verified by reading actual code, not assumed:
  - `.equals()` null-safety (28 call sites, full manual review) — clean. Every risky-looking one (`ParentCompanyGuaranteeService`, `HolidayCalendarService`, `BookService`) is either protected by `@NotNull`+`@Valid` at the API boundary, guarded by a preceding null-check, or operating on a value that's structurally guaranteed non-null (e.g. a `while (x != null)` loop variable).
  - `Optional.get()` anti-pattern — zero occurrences anywhere in the codebase (everything correctly uses `.orElseThrow()`).
  - The historical `@NotNull`-on-`@JsonIgnore`'d-raw-FK-field bug (found and fixed for 6 entities + `GlAccount` earlier this project, per this doc's own V116-session entry) — re-checked all 7 files, confirmed the fix is still in place, no regression.
  - **All 18 `resolveForeignKeys()` implementations** (`PipelineTariffService`, `CreditLimitService`, `LetterOfCreditService`, `RinObligationService`, `LocationService`, `RinTransactionService`, `PeriodService`, `EmissionSchemeService`, `ProductService`, `EmissionObligationService`, `EnvironmentalProductService`, `TruckService`, `CarbonRegistryService`, `MarketService`, `GlAccountService`, `MarginAgreementService`, `PriceIndexService`, `PipelineSegmentService`) — every single one follows the identical safe `if (input.getXxxCode() != null) { ...resolve...} ` pattern. Zero exceptions found.
  - BigDecimal arithmetic chains in financial calculations (`CreditLimitService.hydrate()`'s `available`/`utilisationPct` computation, `LetterOfCreditService.hydrate()`'s `availableAmount`) — every operand (`limitAmount`, `usedAmount`, `collateralOffset`, `warningThresholdPct`, `criticalThresholdPct`, `lcAmount`, `drawdownAmount`) is `@NotNull` on the entity and both `create()`/`update()` controllers use `@Valid @RequestBody`, so Bean Validation rejects a null before this code ever runs. The one genuinely-optional operand (`tempUpliftAmount`, no `@NotNull`) is correctly null-guarded in code (`!= null ? ... : BigDecimal.ZERO`).
  - `RinInventoryController`'s live aggregate calculation (`avgCost`/`totalValue` from a JPQL `SUM(CASE...)` query) — the `pricedQuantitySum()`/`pricedValueSum() != null` checks are technically redundant (the JPQL uses `ELSE 0`, not `ELSE NULL`, so `SUM()` can never return null once `GROUP BY` guarantees ≥1 row) but not masking a real gap — over-defensive, not broken.
  - **Conclusion: zero exploitable NPE bugs found in any of the above.** This is a real, evidence-based negative result — not "didn't look hard enough." The backend's actual null-safety mechanism is consistent `@NotNull` + `@Valid` Bean Validation at the API boundary combined with defensive `if (x != null)` guards in every `resolveForeignKeys()`/`hydrate()` method — a real, working pattern, not luck.
- **Real secondary finding — NOT an NPE, a validation-timing gap, correctly categorized as distinct from what was asked**: 17 create/update endpoints across 12 controllers take a real entity/DTO `@RequestBody` **without `@Valid`**: `AddressContactController.updateEntityAddress`/`updateEntityContact`, `RbacController.createRole`/`updateRole`, `SystemUserController.createUser`/`updateUser`, `FieldPermissionController` (profile save), `LegalEntityController.bulkCreate`, `ProductReportingGroupController.assign`, `HolidayCalendarController.bulkCreateHolidays`, `IncotermController.update` (its own `create()` correctly has `@Valid` — `update()` was missed), `BookController.archive`/`move`/`addTrader`, `MarketProductController.create`/`update`, `MarketProductPeriodController.add`, `BookAccessGrantController.create`. Traced two of these (`SystemUserController`, `IncotermController`) all the way through to confirm the actual failure mode: a missing required field reaches `repository.save()` unvalidated, hits the DB's own `NOT NULL`/CHECK constraint, and `GlobalExceptionHandler`'s existing `DataIntegrityViolationException` handler turns it into a clean 400 — **not a 500, not an NPE**, just a less specific error message and a wasted DB round-trip versus catching it at the API boundary. Real gap, worth closing, but explicitly not part of this pass's "NPE risk" scope — flagged here as its own follow-up item, not fixed. **RESOLVED 2026-07-19** (see that date's entry at the top of this section) — closed for all endpoints except the two bulk-upload ones (`LegalEntityController.bulkCreate`, `HolidayCalendarController.bulkCreateHolidays`), where adding `@Valid` was determined to be the wrong fix (would break intentional per-row partial-success handling). Also turned out several of these (the `book`/`bookaccess` ones especially, built after this entry was written) were genuine unhandled NullPointerExceptions, not just the DB-constraint-catches-it case described above.
- **Not implemented this pass**: the 17-endpoint `@Valid` gap above (documented only, per the distinction above). Also not re-verified: this audit covered the highest-risk categories deeply, not all 516 backend `.java` files exhaustively — a reasonable, evidence-backed sample, not a claim of 100% file-by-file coverage.

**2026-07-18 — Book/EOD hierarchy gap analysis: reviewed how OpenLink Endur and industry-standard ETRM practice structure books against SmartETRM's current model, since EOD relies directly on it. Research + design proposal only, explicitly not implemented ("don't start implement just give me what is best I'll review and confirm").**
- **Trigger**: user asked for a review of the book setup against major trading-house platforms (OpenLink Endur named explicitly), framed by "EOD process relies on this," plus a direct question — "how will we see group of desks PL or submit the EOD process on higher level, what is the hierarchy model we implemented?"
- **What's already solid (V118–120 book redesign, confirmed correct against industry practice, no changes needed)**: `book_trader` (multi-trader ownership, PRIMARY/SECONDARY/BACKUP, exactly-one-active-PRIMARY enforced), `parent_book_id` (arbitrary-depth self-referencing hierarchy — matches Endur's internal-portfolio tree), `book_access_grant` (entity/desk/book-scoped row-level access, same `PENDING_APPROVAL → ACTIVE` workflow as `user_role_assignment`), full temporal audit history for free (`book_history`, `SYSTEM_VERSIONING`), and `position`/`position_eod_snapshot` both correctly keyed on `book_id` as the atomic P&L/position unit.
- **The hierarchy model as implemented, exactly**: two hierarchies that are only loosely related. (1) `legal_entity` — self-referencing `parent_entity_id`, models the corporate/legal group. (2) `desk` — flat, one `legal_entity_id` each, **not self-referencing** — no "desk group"/"trading group" layer exists between desk and entity today. (3) `book` is the only real rollup mechanism: self-referencing `parent_book_id` (arbitrary depth), `desk_id` **nullable** (confirmed via `V1__master_data_foundation.sql`'s original `book` table def), one `legal_entity_id`.
- **Real finding: "group of desks P&L" already half-works at the DB layer but is blocked in the GUI.** Because `book.desk_id` is nullable and `parent_book_id` carries no desk-consistency constraint, the schema already supports a desk-less "consolidation" book (e.g. `desk_id = NULL`, `book_name = 'Global Oil Trading'`) that every desk's book points at via `parentBookId` — `position`/`position_eod_snapshot` being keyed on `book_id` means a recursive rollup query would sum it automatically, no schema change needed. **But `organization/books/BookFormDrawer.tsx:230` has `deskId` as `rules={[{ required: true }]}`** — the GUI cannot create a desk-less book even though the DB column allows it. **Separately, `BookFormDrawer.tsx:127,133`'s parent-book picker filters options to `b.legalEntityId === legalEntityId`** — so a consolidation book spanning desks across *different legal entities* (e.g. a global commodity book over US/UK/SG entities) isn't reachable either, even though nothing in the DB schema forces that restriction (only the GUI does). Net: the rollup capability already exists in the schema, it's purely a GUI gap blocking it.
- **Gaps found, ranked by EOD-reliability impact (none implemented — this is the punch list):**
  1. **No EOD close/lock/sign-off state anywhere in the schema** (highest priority — the literal thing "EOD relies on this" is about). `position_eod_snapshot` stores the *numbers* for a book/date but nothing records the *state* of the close process — grepped the entire schema for `eod_status`/`eod_lock`/`close_status`/`book_close`, zero hits. There's no answer to "has EOD actually finished and been approved for Book X on date D, or is it provisional/re-run?" — downstream GL posting and regulatory reporting have no gate to check before trusting a day's numbers. Proposed: `book_eod_status`, one row per (book, business_date), state machine `OPEN → PRICING → CALCULATED → SIGNED_OFF ⟷ REOPENED`. **Applies to every node in the book tree, not just leaves** — a consolidation node is gated on all children reaching `SIGNED_OFF` but still needs its own explicit sign-off action (same approval-workflow convention as `book_access_grant`), giving a real "submit EOD" action at any level (desk, desk-group, entity) while guaranteeing a parent can't close before its children do.
  2. **No book lifecycle state machine** — only `is_active` BIT + `archived_at`/`archived_reason` + `go_live_date`, three independently-settable signals that can drift into invalid combinations (e.g. `is_active=true` with `archived_at` set), and no way to freeze a book (block new trades) without permanently archiving it. Proposed: `DRAFT → ACTIVE → SUSPENDED → CLOSED → ARCHIVED`.
  3. **Limits exist as fields but are never enforced or logged.** `position_limit`/`pnl_limit`/`var_limit` are plain nullable thresholds; grepped for `limit_breach`/`breach_log`/`LimitBreach` schema-wide, zero hits, no soft-warning-vs-hard-block tiers either. EOD risk reporting in every real trading house includes limit-utilization-vs-breach; there's currently nothing to report from. Proposed: `book_limit_breach` — timestamped breach events, WARN/BREACH severity, override sign-off (same approval pattern again).
  4. **No book- or desk-level timezone/EOD calendar.** `legal_entity.default_timezone` exists; `desk`/`book` don't have their own. `holiday_calendar` is wired only to `trade.payment_calendar_code` (settlement) and pipeline cycles (V96) — never to desk or book. For any entity spanning multiple trading timezones (a US entity with both a US desk and an APAC desk), there's no source of truth for *when* EOD should run for that book. Proposed: `desk.timezone` (or derive via the `location_id` already added in V118) + `desk.eod_calendar_id → holiday_calendar`.
  5. **No tradeable-vs-consolidation-only distinction in the book tree.** Any book can simultaneously hold direct trade bookings *and* have children, with nothing preventing double-counting on EOD rollup (parent's own positions + children's rolled-up positions — additive, or is the parent meant to be virtual-only?). Proposed: `book_role` (`TRADING` | `CONSOLIDATION`) — a `CONSOLIDATION` book can have children and the application layer rejects direct trade bookings against it. This is also the fix that makes the "group of desks P&L" gap above a first-class, intentional construct instead of an unmarked side effect of nullable `desk_id`.
  6. **Currency consolidation across the hierarchy is unmodeled.** Each book has one `base_currency_id`, but nothing specifies which FX rate/date convention is authoritative when a parent (potentially different currency) consolidates children's EOD P&L — that logic would live entirely in application code today with no schema anchor, a real "two people get different consolidated numbers" risk. Proposed: an explicit `fx_rate_type` reference on the consolidation step, or at minimum a documented convention (EOD official close rate, dated to the business date being closed).
  - **Lower priority, flag for Finance stakeholder input rather than treat as a settled gap**: whether `book` needs its own cost-center/profit-center concept distinct from the existing `gl_account.book_id` link (V50) — a common trading-book-vs-chart-of-accounts divergence in real trading houses, but not clearly needed here without Finance's input.
- **Suggested sequencing if/when this gets built** (not written as actual migrations — proposal only): (1) `book_eod_status` — highest value, purely additive, lowest risk. (2) Book lifecycle state machine — can coexist with `is_active` during transition. (3) `book_limit_breach` — additive. (4) Desk timezone/calendar — additive. (5) `book_role` — additive column, but needs an application-layer rule (reject direct booking on `CONSOLIDATION` books) plus the two `BookFormDrawer.tsx` GUI fixes (make `deskId` optional when `book_role=CONSOLIDATION`; relax or make explicit the cross-entity parent-book restriction). (6) FX consolidation convention — mostly a documented decision, smallest schema footprint.
- **Research method**: read `V1__master_data_foundation.sql`'s original `book`/`desk`/`legal_entity` table defs plus `V118`/`V119`/`V120` (the prior book-redesign migrations) directly; grepped the full 120-migration schema for EOD-status/limit-breach/timezone-calendar patterns to confirm gaps were real absences, not just unfound by search terms; read the live `BookFormDrawer.tsx`/`BooksPage.tsx`/`types.ts` frontend to confirm GUI-vs-DB capability gaps; web search on OpenLink Endur's internal-portfolio/book-hierarchy model and general ETRM EOD-close practice (results were mostly marketing-tier, not deep technical docs — grounded primarily in verified reads of this codebase's own schema plus established ETRM domain conventions, not vendor-proprietary specifics). **Nothing implemented this pass** — no migration, no entity change, no frontend change. This entry is the complete spec for whoever picks it up next, pending the user's review/confirmation.

**2026-07-18 — SQL Server data-type sizing audit across all 120 migrations (V1–V120). Research only, per explicit user instruction ("gather ... update handoff doc we'll correct it later") — nothing in this entry has been fixed yet.**
- **Trigger**: user asked for a project-wide review of "incorrectly using the data types like if int is enough but we use bigint or small int is enough but we still used int etc."
- **Method**: parsed every `CREATE TABLE` and every `FOREIGN KEY`/`REFERENCES` clause (including later `ALTER TABLE ADD CONSTRAINT`/`ALTER COLUMN`) across all 120 migration files, cross-checked PK vs FK types, then grepped targeted patterns for boolean/money/sequential-int columns. `etrm-backend/src/main/resources/db/migration` treated as authoritative (per this doc's own convention); the `database/*.sql` mirror not separately re-parsed.
- **Headline result: the schema is already disciplined, not the "guess wrong size everywhere" scenario the question implied.** Three of five checked categories came back with **zero findings**: (1) PK/FK type parity — 787 FK constraints checked, no INT-FK-into-BIGINT-PK (or reverse) mismatches anywhere; (2) boolean-semantics columns (`is_*`/`has_*`/`*_ind`/`*_flag`) — 100% already `BIT`, no stray `VARCHAR(1)`/`CHAR(1)`/`INT` flags; (3) money/quantity/rate columns — 100% already `DECIMAL`, `FLOAT`/`REAL` isn't used anywhere in the schema for anything. BIGINT itself is used sparingly and correctly (5 files: `snapshot_id`/`audit_id`/`file_size_bytes`/polymorphic `entity_id` — all genuinely high-volume or cross-table-polymorphic, not accidental oversizing).
- **Real findings — 11 columns with a self-evidently narrow, bounded domain still declared plain `INT`, TINYINT/SMALLINT candidates:**
  - `V108__voyage_charter_bunker_backbone.sql:392` `laytime_calculation.version_number` INT → TINYINT (recalc counter, `DEFAULT 1`)
  - `V108__voyage_charter_bunker_backbone.sql:394` `laytime_calculation.superseded_by_version` INT → TINYINT (must match the column above)
  - `V56__fx_period_rate_forward_curve.sql:39` `fx_period.days_offset` INT → SMALLINT (comment documents values like `1, 2, 45, 1032`; even a 30-yr daily curve fits SMALLINT's ±32767)
  - `V41__balmo.sql:55` `trade_order_balmo.elapsed_pricing_days` INT → TINYINT (bounded by days-in-a-month, max ~23)
  - `V41__balmo.sql:56` `trade_order_balmo.total_pricing_days` INT → TINYINT (same bound)
  - `V49__credit_limit_expansion.sql:24` `credit_limit.tenor_cap_months` INT → SMALLINT
  - `V49__credit_limit_expansion.sql:85` `credit_limit_line_item.tenor_cap_months` INT → SMALLINT (same field, line-item scope)
  - `V49__credit_limit_expansion.sql:28` `credit_limit.review_frequency_days` INT → **SMALLINT, not TINYINT** — seed data (`V49` lines 176/183) uses 365/180, which would overflow TINYINT's 255 max
  - `V32__broker_fee_agreement.sql:52` `broker_fee_agreement.payment_due_days` INT → SMALLINT (`DEFAULT 30`)
  - `V33__trade_order_item.sql:15` `trade_order.order_sequence` INT → SMALLINT (per-trade leg sequence, `UNIQUE(trade_id, order_sequence)`)
  - `V33__trade_order_item.sql:60` `trade_item.item_sequence` INT → SMALLINT (per-order line sequence, `UNIQUE(order_id, item_sequence)`)
- **Real findings — 4 columns that are outliers against this schema's own established convention**, not a fresh judgment call: 46 of 50 `sort_order` columns schema-wide already use SMALLINT (40) or TINYINT (6); these 4 use plain INT for the identical bounded field (small-list UI display ordering):
  - `V20__rbac_roles_functions.sql:33` `app_module.sort_order` INT → SMALLINT
  - `V20__rbac_roles_functions.sql:47` `app_function.sort_order` INT → SMALLINT
  - `V26__field_level_permissions.sql:34` `screen_field_registry.sort_order` INT → SMALLINT
  - `V26__field_level_permissions.sql:51` `object_lock_rule.sort_order` INT → SMALLINT
- **Category 5 (post-V95 currency_code/country_code regression check) — zero findings**: no migration after V95 reintroduces a raw currency/country code string column; the V95 FK-id conversion (see that entry's own §0/§13 history) holds cleanly everywhere sampled (`trade_order`, `trade_item`, `trade_order_cost`, `broker_fee_agreement`, etc.).
- **Not fixed — explicitly deferred per the user's own framing ("we'll correct it later")**: any actual `ALTER COLUMN` for the 15 columns above needs its own migration (`V121__...`), a matching entity-field type change (`Integer`/`Short` on the Java side — check `@Column` annotations for each), a live-DB verification pass (Hibernate `ddl-auto: validate` on boot, per this doc's own established verify pattern), and a check for any frontend `number` input that assumes no upper bound. None of that was attempted this pass — this entry is the complete punch list for whoever picks it up.
- **User-specified standard for the `sort_order` fix specifically (given after this audit, also not yet implemented) — revised to TINYINT, not SMALLINT**: initial ask was "`sort_order` must always be SMALLINT and never allow negative in GUI"; on discussing the tradeoff, settled on **TINYINT** as the better standard instead. Reasoning: TINYINT is SQL Server's unsigned 1-byte int (0–255) — it enforces "never negative" at the schema level itself, not just via GUI validation, which directly satisfies the "never allow negative" half of the requirement for free. The 255 cap is a non-issue for every `sort_order` column in this schema — all are small admin/reference-list display-ordering fields, never expected to exceed a few dozen rows. **Before executing**, worth a quick check that no `sort_order` column sits on a table that could ever realistically need more than 255 manually-ordered rows (not yet verified). Scope of the actual fix, once done: standardize **all ~50** `sort_order` columns on TINYINT — the 4 plain-`INT` outliers (`V20__rbac_roles_functions.sql:33,47`, `V26__field_level_permissions.sql:34,51`) need narrowing, the 40 currently `SMALLINT` need narrowing, the 6 already `TINYINT` need nothing. **Also required, GUI side**: even with TINYINT's DB-level non-negative guarantee, every `sort_order` numeric input should still reject negative values client-side for a good error message pre-submit — grep `sortOrder`/`sort_order` across `etrm-frontend/src` for `InputNumber`/`<Input type="number">` usage (not yet inventoried this pass) and add `min={0}` (antd `InputNumber`) or the equivalent. Nothing here has been implemented — this bullet is the spec for that follow-up, deliberately not executed this session per the user's explicit "don't change anything now, just add it to handoff doc."

**2026-07-18 — Raw-ID GUI sweep, round 2: fixed 4 more forms still showing bare numeric FKs instead of resolved names (the "1 / Trading Desk (ID)" pattern user reported on the Trader edit drawer). Verified live via Playwright against MSW. A real mock-data gap and a real pre-existing crash were found along the way — documented below, not both fixed.**
- **Trigger**: user reported the Trader edit drawer still showing raw IDs ("User Account (ID) 1", "Legal Entity (ID) 1", "Trading Desk (ID) 1", "Approver Trader (ID)") and asked "I thought we've fixed this earlier for all objects — it seems not fully implemented." Confirmed via `Explore` sweep: the earlier raw-ID fix passes (V118 book redesign, the type-safety sweep above) never touched `TradersPage.tsx`/`DeskFormDrawer.tsx`/`MarketsPage.tsx`/`PriceSourcesPage.tsx` — these were missed, not regressed.
- **Fixed — Group 1, Trading Desk & Trader Authorization** (the reported screen): `organization/traders/TradersPage.tsx` — `userId`/`legalEntityId`/`deskId`/`approverTraderId` all converted from raw `<InputNumber>` to `<Select>` with resolved labels, reusing existing hooks (`useSystemUsers`, `useLegalEntities`, `useDesks`, the page's own `useTraders`) rather than adding new lookup logic. `organization/desks/DeskFormDrawer.tsx` — same fix for `legalEntityId`/`headTraderId` (the sibling `locationId` field was already done correctly via `useTradingDeskLocations()` and served as the template).
- **Fixed — Group 2, Pricing/Market master data**: `markets/markets/MarketsPage.tsx` — `exchangeId` (had a hardcoded `"1 = ICE"` placeholder as a workaround) now a `Select` via `useExchanges()`. `pricing/price-sources/PriceSourcesPage.tsx` — the index-link sub-form's `priceIndexId` now a `Select` via `usePriceIndices()`.
- **Real mock-data bug found while verifying, not a UI bug**: `mocks/etrmHandlers.ts`'s `traderStore` referenced `userId: 101–106`, but `systemUsersStore` only ever seeded `userId: 1–9` (and only 2 of those — `j.doe`→trader 1, `a.smith`→trader 2 — actually linked back to a trader). So even with the `Select` fix in place, 4 of 6 traders' User Account field still rendered a raw, unresolvable ID because the referenced row genuinely didn't exist in mock data. Fixed by adding system-user rows 10–13 for the other 4 traders (Raj Patel, Maria Jensen, Pierre Lefebvre, Sarah Wong) and repointing the trader rows' `userId` at the real 2/3/10/11/12/13 range. This is the same "shadow store drifted from the real one" class of bug flagged elsewhere in this doc (§0's `legalEntityStore` vs `legalEntitiesRef` note), just for `system_users`/`traders` instead.
- **Real pre-existing crash found, NOT fixed (out of scope for this pass)**: `PriceSourcesPage.tsx`'s `IndexLinksDrawer.openAdd()` sets `effectiveFrom: dayjs().format('YYYY-MM-DD') as unknown as string` — a plain string cast to `Dayjs`, not an actual `Dayjs` object — which crashes `AppDatePicker` with `date.isValid is not a function` and white-screens the "Link Index" (add new) flow. Confirmed present on unmodified `main` too (verified by `git stash`-ing this session's changes and reproducing the same crash), so unrelated to the `priceIndexId` fix above — the *edit* path for an existing link (which does exercise the new `priceIndexId` Select) works fine and was used to verify the fix instead. Needs its own fix: `effectiveFrom: dayjs()` (no `.format()`/cast) in `openAdd()`.
- **Explicitly out of scope this pass, left as pending groups for a future session** (found during the initial `Explore` sweep, see full findings above the fix list in this session's transcript if resuming with it still in context):
  - **Group 3 — Voyage Ops optional trade links**: `voyage-ops/voyages/VoyageWorkspace.tsx` — `tradeOrderId`/`tradeItemId` ("Trade Order ID (optional link)" / "Trade Item ID (optional link)") are still raw `<InputNumber>`, the only two outliers in a form where every other FK field already resolves via `Select`. Needs a trade-order/trade-item search hook (check `features/trade/hooks.ts`) that doesn't currently exist — these are optional cross-links to trade blotter records, not simple single-table FKs, so it's more than a drop-in `Select` swap. Similarly `bolmo/BolmoAgreementsPage.tsx`'s `orderId` field.
  - **Polymorphic references, not a simple FK**: `credit/insurance-policies/InsurancePoliciesPage.tsx`'s `insuredEntityId` and `credit/collateral/CollateralPage.tsx`'s `securedEntityId` can point at a trade, account, vessel, or credit line depending on a type discriminator — a single `useXxx()` → `Select` doesn't apply; would need a type-aware resolver.
  - **Not investigated this pass**: this sweep was scoped to Descriptions/Form fields with an explicit "(ID)" label or an obvious raw-FK `<InputNumber>`/`<Input type="number">`. It did not check ag-grid **column** renderers for the same pattern (only the Trader/Desk/Market/PriceSource *forms* were in scope) — worth a follow-up grep for grid columns rendering a raw numeric FK with no `valueFormatter`/`cellRenderer` name lookup.
- **Verified for real, live in the browser** (MSW mocks, not the real backend — this machine's `.env.development.local` points at the real backend by default; overrode with `VITE_USE_MOCKS=true` on the dev-server env for this session only, file left untouched): `npx tsc -b` clean throughout. Playwright (installed ad hoc via `npm install --no-save`, not a project dependency — same gap noted in the previous session's entry) drove the actual Master Data Hub → Traders/Desks/Markets/Price-Sources edit drawers and confirmed every fixed field renders a real resolved name, not a raw number — screenshotted at each step. Confirmed specifically: Trader JDO's Legal Entity/Trading Desk/User Account all resolve; Trader RKP's Approver Trader resolves to "JDO — John Doe"; Desk OIL-CRUDE's Legal Entity/Head Trader resolve; Market ICE_BRENT's Exchange resolves to "ICE — Intercontinental Exchange"; the Price Index Link edit form resolves to "DTBRT — Platts Dated Brent". **2026-07-18 — Frontend type-safety sweep: made `useTableRows` generic to kill ~90 unsafe casts, and fixed a real stale-type bug (`Counterparty`/`LegalEntity`/`BrokerRef`) that was rendering broken dropdown labels on ~12 pages. Frontend-only, no migration/backend touched.**
- **Trigger**: user asked to "fix all the type safety issues" in the project. `npx tsc -b --noEmit` was already fully clean (strict mode, no errors) and `as any`/`@ts-ignore` were essentially absent — the real issue was pervasive `as unknown as X[]` / `as X[]` double-casting (238 occurrences project-wide) used to narrow the generic Tier2 `useTableRows()` return type (`ReferenceDataRow[]`, a deliberately dynamic `Record<string, string|number|boolean|null>`) down to a page's locally-known row shape.
- **`features/tier2/hooks.ts`**: `useTableRows<T = ReferenceDataRow>(tableName)` is now generic — `queryFn` casts once, internally, to `Promise<T[]>`, so callers write `useTableRows<{ productId: number; productCode: string; productName: string }>('product')` and get a real typed array back instead of casting at every call site. (Constraining `T extends ReferenceDataRow` was tried first and rejected — TS's structural check requires an explicit index signature for that constraint, which rejects named interfaces like `ReportingGroup`/`TemplateRow` even though they're perfectly compatible; an unconstrained default type param avoids the false rejection.)
- **Updated ~40 files** across contracts/, credit/, environmental/, finance/, logistics/, markets/, reference/, voyage-ops/, and `trade/TradeBlotter.tsx` to pass the type argument and drop the local `as unknown as {...}[]` / `type LR = {...}` casts — purely mechanical, one call site at a time, verified with `tsc -b` after each batch.
- **Real bug found along the way, not just a type-cleanliness issue**: `features/trade/api.ts`'s `Counterparty`/`LegalEntity` interfaces had stale field names (`counterpartyCode`/`name`, `entityCode`/`name`) that never matched what the tier1 backend handlers actually serve (`cpCode`/`legalName`, `entityCode`/`entityName`) — this exact gap was already flagged in a prior session's memory note ([[project_blotter_workspace]]) as "~12 consuming pages cast to this stale shape, so labels render undefined at runtime" but not yet fixed. Fixed by having `trade/api.ts` import and re-export the real `Counterparty`/`LegalEntity` types from `tier1/counterparty/types.ts` / `tier1/legal-entity/types.ts` instead of maintaining a second, drifted copy. Every consumer that was casting around the mismatch (`CreditLimitsPage`, `CollateralPage`, `MarginAccountsPage`, `BankGuaranteesPage`, `LettersOfCreditPage`, `NettingAgreementsPage`, `GtcAgreementsPage`, `CommercialTermsPage`, `BolmoAgreementsPage`, `RinTransactionsPage`, `EmissionObligationsPage`, `RinAccountsPage`, `RinObligationsPage`) updated to the real field names — several of these were rendering `"CODE — undefined"` in dropdown labels at runtime, now fixed as a side effect of the type fix, not just a cast cleanup.
- **`BrokerRef`** was also missing `commodityType` (present in both mock data and the real MSW broker store) — `TradeBlotter.tsx`'s broker-filter-by-commodity logic was casting around this gap too; added the field to the type instead.
- **`CreditLimitsPage`'s counterparty→country autofill was silently dead code**: `onCpChange` read `cp.jurisdiction` (a field that never existed on the real type) and looked it up through a country-code map, so `countryId` was always `undefined` and the field never auto-filled. Real `Counterparty.jurisdictionId` is already the country id directly — simplified to use it directly, deleted the now-dead `countryIdByCode` map.
- **Also fixed the 20 pre-existing `eslint` errors** (unrelated to the type-safety ask but caught while running the full check suite): 3× `no-undef` on `React.ReactNode`/`React.ComponentType` in files using the new JSX transform (fixed via named `type` imports instead of the `React.` namespace); 8× `react-hooks/immutability` — all the same false-positive shape, mutating `skipDraftReset.current` (a real `useRef()` returned from the shared `useDraftValues` hook) which the new React-Compiler-powered `eslint-plugin-react-hooks@7` can't see through a custom-hook boundary; 6× `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` — all genuine sync-state-with-external-query-data effects (seed local state when a TanStack Query result arrives), not derivable during render. Both classes fixed with scoped, commented `eslint-disable` blocks rather than forcing a key-remount refactor of working code — same judgment call as this doc's own precedent for `exhaustive-deps`.
- **Verified**: `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean, `npx eslint .` 0 errors (was 20), `npm run build` succeeds. **Not verified via live browser click-through** — Playwright isn't installed as a project dependency in this environment (`ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND: playwright` when importing from a throwaway script), so the field-name fixes were cross-checked directly against the real backend-serving type definitions (`tier1/counterparty/types.ts`, `tier1/legal-entity/types.ts`) rather than confirmed visually in the running app. Flagged as a good follow-up spot-check next session, especially for the pages whose dropdown labels were silently broken (`CreditLimitsPage`, `CollateralPage`, `MarginAccountsPage`, `BankGuaranteesPage`, `LettersOfCreditPage`, `NettingAgreementsPage`, `GtcAgreementsPage`, `CommercialTermsPage`, `BolmoAgreementsPage`, `RinTransactionsPage`).

**2026-07-18 — Trading book redesign (V118-V120): multi-trader books, flexible book hierarchy, entity/desk-scoped access control, verified end-to-end against the real backend + live DB.**
- **Why**: existing `dbo.book` had `deskId`/`legalEntityId` as raw `<InputNumber>` fields in the UI (user had to type a PK, guided only by a hardcoded hint comment), a single required `responsible_trader_id` (no way to share a book across traders), and no way to scope data access below the RBAC action-permission level (any user with `TRADE_VIEW` could see every legal entity's books).
- **V118** — reused the existing `dbo.location` table (previously logistics-only: ports/hubs/storage) for desk offices instead of a new table: added `office_loc_ind`/`trading_desk_ind` BIT flags (both default 0, ~1,000 existing logistics rows untouched) + `desk.location_id` FK. New `GET /api/v1/locations/trading-desks` filters to the picker's actual candidates.
- **V119** — `dbo.book_trader` join table (book_id, trader_id, role PRIMARY/SECONDARY/BACKUP, filtered unique index enforcing one active PRIMARY per book) replaces the old single `responsible_trader_id` column (backfilled then dropped — clean break, no live trading data yet). Added `book.parent_book_id` (self-FK, nullable, arbitrary depth — not a fixed-depth chain, matching how OpenLink Endur's portfolio tree actually works per a research pass this session) with cycle-prevention + depth-cap enforced at the service layer (SQL Server can't express recursive integrity in a CHECK). Added `book.archived_at`/`archived_reason` for a self-documenting year-end archive sweep (reuses the existing `is_active` flag as the switch, no new status enum, no per-year book duplication).
- **V120** — `dbo.book_access_grant`: legal-entity/desk/book-scoped access, `READ`/`READ_WRITE` (reusing `role_function`'s existing vocabulary, not a new one), built as a sibling to `dbo.user_role_assignment` with the identical `PENDING_APPROVAL → ACTIVE | REJECTED → EXPIRED` workflow so it slots into the existing Roles & Permissions admin page as one more tab ("Book Access") rather than a new screen. Resolution rule (entity grant → access to every desk/book under it; desk grant → that desk's books only; book grant or `book_trader` row → that one book) is documented in the migration header; actual query-time filtering of book-listing endpoints by this resolution is **not yet wired up** — this pass is CRUD + approval workflow for issuing grants only.
- `dbo.book` is a SQL Server temporal table (`book_history`, since V1) — every move between desk/entity/parent and every archive/unarchive is audited for free, no separate audit table needed. New `PATCH /api/v1/books/{id}/move` and `/archive` endpoints exploit this.
- **Fully verified against the live DB and real GUI, not spot-checked**: migrations applied clean (`flyway_schema_history` confirms v120, Hibernate `ddl-auto: validate` passed — no column-type mismatches), real JWT login (`admin`/`DevPassword123!`) + full curl round-trip on every new endpoint (`GET /books` confirms `responsibleTraderId` gone and `parentBookId`/`archivedAt`/`traders[]` present and correctly denormalized; `PATCH .../move` confirmed cycle-rejection returns 409 with a clear message; `PATCH .../archive` sets `archivedAt`/`archivedReason`/`isActive=false`; `POST .../traders` confirmed duplicate-PRIMARY rejection; full grant request→approve→duplicate-reject→revoke cycle on `book-access-grant` all correct) — all test mutations cleaned up afterward. Real Playwright pass against the live backend (not MSW) confirmed `BookFormDrawer` renders cascading Legal Entity/Desk `Select`s (no more raw-ID hint text), a working Parent Book picker, and an inline Book Traders section (add/remove with role); confirmed the new "Book Access" tab on `RolesPage.tsx` renders with a working Request Access flow. Noted for whoever picks this up next: a handful of unrelated 403s appeared in the browser console during this pass (not from any of the endpoints tested directly via curl, which all returned correct 2xx/4xx) — worth a quick look but didn't block verification of the actual feature.
- Note: this machine's `etrm-frontend/.env.development.local` points the dev server at the real backend (`VITE_USE_MOCKS=false`) rather than MSW — and the backend's CORS `allowed-origins` only permits `http://localhost:5173`, so a verify session must run on port 5173 specifically, not an arbitrary alternate port, when this override file is present.

**2026-07-17 — Added road/truck tariff + transport-mode links (V117), closed the "no JUnit for the new entities" gap for all ~26 dedicated entities built this session, and along the way found and fixed 10 more real bugs (2 self-introduced, 8 found by the test-writing agents) — full project-wide `mvn test` clean, backend boots clean at V117.**
- **V117** — gap check on "tariff/freight cost for distribution, linked to truck or pipeline": pipeline was already fully covered (`pipeline_tariff`, pre-existing); vessel freight already covered (`freight_rate_index`/`demurrage_dispatch_rate`); **truck/road had no tariff table at all** — built `dbo.road_tariff` (route-based via the existing MOT-agnostic `transport_route`, mirrors `pipeline_tariff`'s shape: rate/currency/UoM/fuel-surcharge/min-charge/effective dates). Also added `mot_type_id` (nullable FK) to `loading_rack` and `throughput_agreement` (V116) since neither had any way to say which transport mode they serve. All Tier2-generic — zero new Java code needed, the generic mechanism picked up the new table/columns automatically.
- **JUnit coverage** — dispatched 3 parallel background agents (Environmental/RIN: 8 entities; Finance/Pricing: 10 entities; Operations/Logistics: 6 entities) plus wrote `TransportRouteControllerTest`/`RegulatoryObligationControllerTest` myself, covering all ~26 dedicated entities built earlier this session that previously had zero test coverage (Tier2-generic tables like `loading_rack`/`road_tariff` don't need dedicated tests — they're already covered by the existing `ReferenceDataCrudSmokeTest` 154-table sweep).
- **10 more real bugs found — this is the actual value of writing these tests, not the coverage number**:
  1. **My own bug** (found by my own new test): `TransportRouteService.create()` never set `created_by` (NOT NULL live column) — every POST failed. Fixed with `AuditorAware`, matching the established pattern (`LocationService`).
  2. **My own bug, worse**: `RegulatoryObligation.java` never mapped `created_by` **at all** (not even a field) despite the live column being NOT NULL — every POST failed unconditionally. Fixed by adding the field + wiring `AuditorAware`.
  3–8. **Six entities** (`CarbonRegistry`, `EmissionScheme`, `EnvironmentalProduct`, `EmissionObligation`, `RinObligation`, `RinTransaction`, found by the Environmental/RIN agent) had `@NotNull` directly on a raw FK `Integer` field whose getter/setter were `@JsonIgnore`'d — only the denormalized `String` sibling (aliased to the same JSON key) was reachable from JSON. Bean Validation ran on the deserialized entity *before* `resolveForeignKeys()` ever populated the int field, so **every real POST/PUT 400'd unconditionally, for every real caller, since the frontend only ever sends the string code** — these 6 endpoints have been completely non-functional for create/update since they were built earlier this session, undetected until a test tried a real round-trip. Fixed by dropping `@NotNull` from all 6 raw FK fields (enforcement belongs in `resolveForeignKeys`/the DB's own `NOT NULL`).
  9. **`RailcarProductApproval.assetType`** (found by the Operations/Logistics agent) carried `@NotBlank`, but `RailcarController.addProductApproval()` always sets it server-side *after* `@Valid` already ran — the frontend's own `RailcarProductApprovalInput` type correctly omits `assetType` from the payload (it's meant to be server-assigned), so every real request from the actual UI 400'd. Fixed by dropping `@NotBlank`.
  10. **`RinFuelCategory.dCode`** (and the same field on `RinObligation`/`RinTransaction`) declared `@Size(max=10)`/`length=10`, but the live column is `NVARCHAR(5)` — `sys.columns.max_length` is in *bytes* for `NVARCHAR` (2 bytes/char), so the real char limit is 5. A 6-10 char value would pass Bean Validation only to fail with an unhandled-looking truncation error at the DB. Fixed all 3 occurrences.
  11. **`GlAccount`** (found live via curl after fixing the above pattern, not by the agent's own test — the agent correctly documented a 500 it couldn't fix, but the *underlying* fix exposed a second, deeper bug): had two getters bound to the same JSON key `"accountType"` (raw `Integer` field, no `@JsonIgnore`, plus the denormalized `String` sibling) — Jackson refused to build any (de)serializer for the class at all, so `InvalidDefinitionException` 500'd every POST/PUT **and any GET that returned a `GlAccount`** (list included, once a row existed). Fixed by `@JsonIgnore`-ing the raw getter/setter. That then surfaced bug 3–8's exact pattern again (`@NotNull` on the now-ignored field) — fixed the same way. That *then* surfaced a third, independent gap: `GlAccountService.create()`/`update()` never actually called `resolveForeignKeys()` at all — the incoming `accountTypeCode` string was silently dropped, `accountType` stayed `NULL`, and the DB's own `NOT NULL` constraint was the only thing stopping a silently-broken row from being written. Fixed by wiring `resolveForeignKeys()` into both methods. **Three independently-fixed bugs in one entity, each one only surfacing once the previous one was fixed** — a good illustration of why "does it compile" and even "does GET work" are not the same as "does create actually work."
- **Two of my own tests initially collided with themselves** on re-run: `RegulatoryObligationControllerTest` and `RinObligationControllerTest` both used a JVM-local `AtomicInteger` to vary a field inside a composite UNIQUE constraint, which resets to 0 on every JVM run and collided with leftover rows from a *previous* run (since `deactivate` is a soft flag, not a delete — the old UNIQUE key stays taken). Fixed both by deriving the varying value from `unique()`'s own counter (seeded from `System.currentTimeMillis()`, so it's collision-free across runs, not just within one) instead of a fresh per-JVM counter.
- **Verified for real, multiple times**: full project-wide `mvn test` clean (not just the new classes in isolation — this matters, since fixing bug 11 above required editing `main/` source after tests were "passing" against the old, broken behavior). Backend restarted from a fresh boot after every batch of fixes; final boot at V117 confirmed clean via `flyway_schema_history` and zero Hibernate schema-validation errors. A live curl round-trip against `/api/v1/gl-accounts` confirmed the full three-bug fix chain works end-to-end, not just that the test passes.
- **Still open**: leftover deactivated test rows from this session's test runs remain in the live DB (`carbon_registry`, `gtc`, `bolmo_agreement`, etc. all have extra rows beyond original seed data) — matches this codebase's own established convention (`LegalEntityControllerTest` and others do the same, `unique()` codes prevent any real collision), not cleaned up further. `<AuditInfo>` component still not rolled out to any of these ~26 pages' Drawers (flagged two sessions ago, still pending).

**2026-07-17 — Closed the entire 27-endpoint backend backlog from the previous entry, plus built the net-new "Supply & Distribution" master-data domain (migration frontier now V116). All 29 previously-orphaned dedicated endpoints verified 200 live; full JUnit suite (170+ tests) clean; backend boots clean from a fresh Flyway run.**
- **Built via 4 parallel background agents** (Environmental/RIN: 8 tables; Finance: `gl_account`/`gtc`/`uom_conversion`/top-level `bank-accounts`; Pricing: `price_source`/`price_index_source`/`formula_template`/`settlement_price`/`pricing_rule`; Operations/Logistics: `nomination`/`delivery_instruction`/`railcar`+product-approvals/`bolmo_agreement`+legs/`position`) plus my own direct work (`incoterms-ref`/`payment-methods` — small ALTERs, V114; `transport_route`/`regulatory_obligation`/`rin_inventory`/`tas_position` stub). Two agents (Operations/Logistics, Pricing) hit the session's usage limit mid-task but had already written their code — picked back up and verified once the limit reset, per the user's "finish now" → later "build the missing pieces" instructions across two turns.
- **A real, self-caused bug found and fixed**: `commodity_instrument_map` (V113, built earlier this session for the Trade Blotter fix) turned out to be a **duplicate** of `commodity_instrument_type_config` — a table already built in a much earlier session (V45) for the exact same purpose, already seeded with the identical 77 rows, whose own migration comment explicitly said "the authoritative DB-side config" for this exact endpoint. Missed because the search was by guessed table name, not by function. Fixed via `V115__drop_duplicate_commodity_instrument_map.sql` and repointed the `commodityinstrumentmap` package at the real table (which turned out to have a simpler design too — plain `commodity_type` VARCHAR, no FK, composite-keyed on `(commodity_type, instrument_type)` via `@EmbeddedId`). **Lesson applied**: before building a new table, check whether the *data* already exists under a different name, not just whether the exact guessed name exists.
- **Three more real bugs caught by actually running things, not just compiling**: (1) `MotType.java` (built for `transport_route`) guessed `type_code`/`type_name` columns; the real table uses `mot_code`/`mot_name` — caught by Hibernate schema validation on a live boot, fixed in one pass. (2) `RegulatoryReportType.java` guessed PK column `regulatory_report_type_id`; the real column is `report_type_id` — same live-boot catch, and confirmed `regulatory_obligation`'s own FK column names (`legal_entity_id`/`report_type_id`/`reporting_entity_id`) were all guessed correctly by cross-referencing an unrelated part of this same handoff doc (§ "Final group of the four approved backlog groups" from an earlier session, which had already built the frontend for `regulatory_obligation` against the real schema). (3) `RinFuelCategoryRepository.findByDCodeIgnoreCase()` (RIN agent) — a genuinely subtle Spring Data gotcha: the entity field is `dCode` (lowercase d, matching the frontend's camelCase), but Spring Data's method-name-derived-query parser looks for a property literally named `DCode` and throws `PathElementException` at repository-bean-creation time — not caught by `mvn compile`, only by actually booting/testing the app. Fixed with an explicit `@Query` JPQL annotation; this one repository method was shared by 4 other packages (`RinObligationService`, `RinTransactionService`, `RinInventoryController`), so the one fix resolved all call sites.
- **`rin_inventory`** (genuinely missing table, per the backlog) was deliberately built as a **read-only live aggregation over `rin_transaction`** (JPQL `GROUP BY account/d_code/vintage_year`, quantity-weighted average cost) rather than a second, separately-maintained balance table — avoids a two-sources-of-truth problem since no batch/position-calc job exists in this codebase to keep a stored balance table in sync with the ledger.
- **`tas_position`** (`pricing/tas-positions`) deliberately stubbed as `GET → []`, no `PATCH .../lock-price` — the real feature is a live view over trade order legs with an active TAS pricing rule, but this codebase has never modeled `trade`/`trade_order` as a JPA entity at all (a repeatedly-confirmed scope boundary from multiple earlier sessions). An unmapped `PATCH` now correctly 405s (this session's earlier `GlobalExceptionHandler` fix) rather than crashing.
- **New "Supply & Distribution" master-data domain** (`V116__supply_distribution_master_data.sql`) — the 6 items flagged as "genuinely missing, not yet designed in any detail" in the previous session's §11a, built as Tier2-generic reference tables per the user's own "ref data" framing (no dedicated backend/frontend code needed): `loading_rack` (custody-transfer measurement points — rack number, meter type, prover cert/calibration dates), `movement_type` (RECEIPT/DELIVERY/INTERNAL_TRANSFER/BLEND/LOSS_GAIN, seeded), `inventory_ownership_type` (COMPANY_OWNED/CONSIGNMENT/EXCHANGE_BORROW/EXCHANGE_LOAN/THIRD_PARTY_HELD, seeded), `blend_recipe` + `blend_recipe_component` (terminal splash-blending recipes), `throughput_agreement` (third-party storage/throughput rights — the storage-side analogue of `pipeline_tariff`), `product_interface_rule` (line-changeover/flush-volume rules). Registered in `master_data_table_registry` under a new module_group.
- **A second, previously-invisible Hub bug found while adding these**: `MasterDataHub.tsx` filters/counts every registered table via a flat `ALL_ENTRIES` array, but *groups* them into sidebar sections via a **separate, hardcoded `GROUPS` array** (icon/color/label per module_group) — adding entries with `group: 'Supply & Distribution'` to `ALL_ENTRIES` without also adding `'Supply & Distribution'` to `GROUPS` made the new tables count correctly in the page header ("174 tables total") but silently vanish from every grouped view (`map.get(e.group)` returns `undefined` for an unregistered group key, and `?.push()` on `undefined` no-ops) — reproduced live via Playwright ("1 result in 0 groups" search state) before being traced to its exact cause and fixed. `theme/tokens.ts`'s `moduleColor()` also extended to route `supply`/`distribution` substrings.
- **Verified for real, multiple times**: `mvn compile`/full `mvn test` (170+ tests) clean after every fix, not just at the end. Backend restarted from a fresh boot multiple times against the live DB — `flyway_schema_history` confirms V112 through V116 all applied successfully, in order, with zero schema-validation errors on the final boot. A live sweep of all 29 previously-orphaned endpoints (`curl` with a real JWT) confirmed every one now returns `200`, not `404`. A real Playwright pass confirmed a genuine `POST /reference-data/loading_rack` round-trip through the actual Static Data GUI (not just the API) renders correctly and the new "Supply & Distribution" Hub group is now visible and searchable; test row cleaned up via direct `DELETE` afterward.

**2026-07-17 — Found and fixed the Trade Blotter's two live-breaking gaps (`commodity-instrument-map`, `pricing-rules`), then discovered this is a systemic pattern: 27 frontend features total exist with zero backend at all (migration frontier now V113). Full list documented below as backlog — user chose to stop after the Trade Blotter fix rather than build out all 27 this pass.**
- **Trigger**: user pasted a live error — `NoResourceFoundException: No static resource api/v1/commodity-instrument-map` — hit while using the app against the real backend. Confirmed the *error handling* was already fixed by this session's earlier `GlobalExceptionHandler` work (clean 404, not 500), but the underlying cause was new: `commodity-instrument-map` is a real, actively-used feature (`TradeBlotter.tsx` calls `useCommodityInstrumentMap()` to restrict which instrument types are selectable per commodity) that only ever existed as an MSW mock (`etrmHandlers.ts`) — no real DB table, no real backend endpoint, ever.
- **`V113__commodity_instrument_map.sql`** (mirrored to `database/113_...sql`): new `dbo.commodity_instrument_map` table (`commodity_type_id` FK → `dbo.commodity_type`, `instrument_type` VARCHAR CHECK-constrained to the same 12 values as `INSTRUMENT_TYPES` in `trade/types.ts`, `sort_order`, `is_active`), seeded with the exact same commodity→instrument-type mapping the mock had (9 commodities, ~85 rows). New `commodityinstrumentmap` package: a plain reader entity (no create/update/delete — matches the mock's own "read-only; only changed via DB migration" comment) + a small controller that groups rows by resolved commodity `type_code` into the `Record<CommodityType, InstrumentType[]>` shape the frontend already expected. No frontend change needed at all — `api.ts` was already calling the right path, it just had nothing to call.
- **User then asked to "fix all similar bugs"** — prompted a systematic sweep rather than guessing at more one at a time: extracted all 265 unique API paths the frontend actually calls (regex over every `apiClient.*` call, excluding mocks) via a throwaway script, then live-probed all 88 static (non-`{id}`) ones against the real backend. Found **29 paths 404ing with the exact "No endpoint matches this request" shape** — i.e. 29 frontend features, each with its own dedicated `api.ts`/`hooks.ts`/Page, calling a REST path with genuinely zero backend behind it. Cross-referencing each against the live DB (`OBJECT_ID('dbo.<table>')`) and `master_data_table_registry` split them into three groups:
  1. **`pricing-rules` and `commodity-instrument-map`** — used directly by `TradeBlotter.tsx`, fixed this session. `pricing-rules`: `dbo.pricing_rule` table already exists with real data but was never registered in Tier2 *and* never got a dedicated controller — same shape as this session's earlier `payment_term`/`uom` discovery, a pre-existing gap, not new. **Deferred, not fixed** (table exists, needs either a dedicated `PricingRuleController` mirroring `PaymentTermController`'s shape, or a Tier2 registry row + Hub entry, since the frontend's dedicated page currently expects the former).
  2. **2 quick path-mismatch cases**: `incoterms-ref` and `payment-methods` — both tables (`incoterm`, `payment_method`) exist *and are already Tier2-registered*, but the frontend's dedicated pages (`features/reference/incoterms`, `features/contracts/payment-methods`) call bespoke paths (`/incoterms-ref`, `/payment-methods`) instead of the generic `/reference-data/{table}` mechanism that would actually work today. Smallest fix of the whole list — a thin dedicated controller (or repointing the frontend) — **not done this pass**.
  3. **20 more tables that exist but have no backend at all** (same shape as `pricing_rule`): `bank_account`, `bolmo_agreement`, `carbon_registry`, `emission_obligation`, `emission_scheme`, `environmental_product`, `gl_account`, `gtc`, `railcar` (logistics), `delivery_instruction`, `nomination` (operations), `positions`, `price_index_source`, `price_source`, `formula_template`, `rin_account`, `rin_fuel_category`, `rin_obligation`, `rin_transaction`, `settlement_price`, `uom_conversion`.
  4. **5 where the table doesn't exist in the DB at all yet** — a deeper gap than the rest, needs schema design too, not just a controller: `compliance_obligation`, `freight_route`, `trade_order_option`, `tas_position`, `rin_inventory`.
- **Explicit user decision** (via `AskUserQuestion`, options were "stop here" / "fix the 2 quick ones" / "keep going through all 27"): **stop here**. Building real backends (business logic, validation, likely more real bugs like the `period` one) for ~25 features this session risked rushed, under-verified code for domains (RIN compliance, environmental credits, positions/settlement, BOLMO) this session has zero prior context on. This full list is the actionable backlog for whoever picks it up next — every one of these 27 (minus the 2 fixed) will 404 with a clean, correctly-coded message (not a 500) if a user reaches them, per this session's earlier `GlobalExceptionHandler` fix, but will not function.
- **Verified for real**: `mvn compile`, full `mvn test` (161 tests, clean) both re-run and green after V113. Live API round-trip on `GET /api/v1/commodity-instrument-map` confirmed byte-identical to the old mock's data, resolved through real FKs (not hardcoded).
