  - `dbo.holiday_calendar` was missing `calendar_type` (BANKING/COMMODITY/EXCHANGE/CUSTOM — a real, currently-used field, distinct from the existing *unused* legacy `commodity_type VARCHAR` column, left unmapped), `currency_id` (added as an id FK per the app's surrogate-key convention — `HolidayCalendar.currencyCode: string` → `currencyId: number` on the frontend, same fix already applied to `Currency.countryId`/`Book.bookType`), and `created_at`.
  - `dbo.calendar_holiday` (the actual list of holiday dates per calendar) didn't exist at all — new child table, same V100 migration.
  - `period.commodity_type` FKs the dedicated `dbo.commodity_type` table (V85), same as `desk`/`book` in batch 1 — reused `CommodityTypeRepository`. `period.load_type_lookup_id`/`gas_day_type_lookup_id` genuinely DO FK `dbo.lookup_value` (V57, never redirected by V85 — only `book_type`/`commodity_type` were "the exception") — first real use of the shared `LookupResolutionService` built in batch 1.
  - Two more `SMALLINT`/`TINYINT`-vs-`Integer` Hibernate mismatches caught before shipping (`period.roll_offset` is `SMALLINT`, `period.crop_year_offset_months` is `TINYINT` — both need `Short`, not `Integer`, per the major session's own JPA-audit finding below) — mapped correctly from the start this time instead of finding it via a failed `ddl-auto=validate` boot.
  - Not yet verified against a live DB (none reachable here) — compile/typecheck clean only.
- **Batch 3 — Counterparties & Agreements (commercial-terms/netting-agreements/gtc-agreements/broker-fee-agreements/entity-tax-registrations) — done, no new migration needed (all five tables' real schema already matched their frontend types almost exactly — first batch with zero schema gaps).** Built `CpCommercialTerms`, `NettingAgreement`, `CpGtcAgreement`, `BrokerFeeAgreement`, `TaxRegistration` entities + repositories + services + controllers (`/api/v1/counterparties/commercial-terms`, `/netting-agreements`, `/gtc-agreements`, `/api/v1/broker-fee-agreements`, `/api/v1/entity-tax-registrations`).
  - Added small **read-only** reference entities purely so these services can resolve denormalized display names, without yet building the full controller each one will eventually need: `CreditTerm`/`PaymentTerm` (`credit_term` is already generic-Tier2-registered via V72 — this doesn't compete with that; `payment_term` is NOT registered, still owed a real dedicated controller in the future Contract & Legal batch), `Gtc`/`GtcVersion`, `Product`, `UnitOfMeasure` (both `product`/`unit_of_measure` still owed full controllers in the future Products & Markets batch — `Product` in particular is large, ~8 sub-resource paths per the original audit, deliberately deferred).
  - `cp_gtc_agreement` FKs `gtc_version_id`, but the frontend's own `Gtc` type already flattens `gtc`(1)→`gtc_version`(N) into one row with a plain `version: string` — `CpGtcAgreementService` resolves the frontend's `gtcId` to "the current version" via `gtc_version.is_current`, matching that existing simplification rather than exposing the version table to this batch's frontend.
  - `TaxRegistration` reuses the existing polymorphic `EntityType` enum (`LEGAL_ENTITY`/`COUNTERPARTY`/`BROKER`) and `?entityType=&entityId=` filter convention already established by `AddressContactController`/`EntityAddress`/`EntityContact` — same pattern, new table. Note: `EntityAddress.entityId` is `Long` but `tax_registration.entity_id` is genuinely `INT` in the real schema — `TaxRegistration.entityId` is `Integer`, correctly not unified with the other two.
  - Not yet verified against a live DB (none reachable here) — compile/typecheck clean only.
- **Batches 6+ (Logistics & Delivery, Freight & Shipping, Contract & Legal, Pricing & Rates, Finance & Settlement, Carbon & Environmental, RIN & Renewable Fuels) — not started yet.** `PaymentTerm`/`UnitOfMeasure` already have a minimal read-only entity from batch 3 (see above) — their future batches should extend those, not create competing ones. Two smaller bugs also flagged by the original audit, not yet fixed: an unscoped `apiClient.get('/bank-accounts')` call in `tier1/counterparty/api.ts` with no matching endpoint (the scoped `/counterparties/:id/bank-accounts` version works fine), and `pricing/balmo-products/api.ts` bypassing the shared `apiClient` entirely (raw `fetch('/api/balmo-products')`, missing the `/api/v1` prefix) — BOLMO is out of Master Data scope anyway (see above) so this one can wait longer than the others.

**Major session — chased "backend won't start" all the way through a full JPA-entity-vs-schema audit, several genuine backend bugs, a Vite env-precedence bug, and ended with a 142-test JUnit/MockMvc regression suite. Root cause of everything: the ~130-table JPA entity layer and the generic Tier 2 CRUD service had literally never been exercised against a live, fully-migrated schema before this session — every bug below was latent, not newly introduced.**

- **Credentials**: `db-init`'s `etrm_app` login creation was create-only — if the login already existed with an older password (e.g. after `.env`'s `ETRM_APP_DB_PASSWORD` was changed), it silently no-opped instead of syncing, so the backend failed with "Login failed for user 'etrm_app'". Fixed `docker/db-init/init-db.sh` to `ALTER LOGIN ... WITH PASSWORD` on every run when the login already exists, not just create it once.
- **JPA entity layer — systematic type-mismatch sweep**, found by actually letting `ddl-auto: validate` run to completion for the first time (previously died earlier in the chain). Every mismatch below was found by restarting, reading the exact column Hibernate complained about, fixing it, and repeating until boot succeeded — not a guess-and-check pass:
  - `INT` vs `BIGINT` PK/FK mismatches: `Address`, `EntityAddress`, `Contact`, `EntityContact`, `BankAccount`, `LegalEntity`, `Counterparty`, `MasterDataTableRegistry`, `ParentCompanyGuarantee`, and the whole RBAC family (`AppFunction`, `AppModule`, `UserRole`, `RoleFunction`, `UserRoleAssignment`, `AppUser`) and field-permission family (`ObjectLockRule`, `FieldPermissionProfile`, `FieldPermissionRule`, `RoleFieldProfile`, `ScreenFieldRegistry`) — all mapped `Long` in Java against `INT IDENTITY` in the DB.
  - `Instant` vs `DATETIME2`: `AuditableEntity`'s shared `createdAt`/`updatedAt` (and a few classes with their own copies) were mapped as `java.time.Instant`, which Hibernate maps to `datetimeoffset`, but every audit column in the schema is plain `DATETIME2`. Fixed once at the shared base class, which fixed it for every entity extending it.
  - `TINYINT`/`SMALLINT` vs `Integer`: `AppUser.failedLoginCount` and `Counterparty.settlementDays` are `TINYINT`, `MasterDataTableRegistry.displayOrder` is `SMALLINT` — Hibernate maps `Short`, not `Integer`, to these. Confirmed via a schema-wide grep that no other JPA-mapped column hits this (154-table schema has ~19 `TINYINT` columns total; only these 3 are actually entity-mapped, the rest are only reachable via the schema-driven generic API, which has no such assumption).
  - Several stale VARCHAR-code fields that earlier migrations (V86/V87/V94/V95) had already converted to numeric FK ids in the DB, but the Java entities were never updated to match: `LegalEntity`/`Counterparty`'s `jurisdiction`/`baseCurrency`/`cpType`/`kycStatus` etc. Cross-checked the frontend's `types.ts` for the same three Tier1 features afterward — already correct, confirming it was only the backend layer that drifted.
- **`ReferenceDataCrudService` (the generic Tier 2 CRUD behind ~150 registered reference tables) — four real bugs**, found via a purpose-built `@TestFactory` sweep (`ReferenceDataCrudSmokeTest`) that exercises create/update/delete against every registered table with a metadata-derived payload:
  1. Unconditionally appended `created_by`/`updated_by` to every INSERT/UPDATE — but 48 of 154 registered tables don't have those columns (`incoterm`, `currency`, `credit_rating`, ...), so create/update 500'd on all of them. Fixed to check the table's live metadata first.
  2. New-row identity retrieval via a separate `SELECT SCOPE_IDENTITY()` call came back `NULL` even inside `@Transactional` (root cause not fully pinned down — not a simple connection-pooling issue). Replaced with `Statement.RETURN_GENERATED_KEYS`, reading the id off the INSERT's own execution instead of a second round trip.
  3. A registry-level `allow_delete=0` (etc.) denial threw `IllegalStateException`, which had no specific handler and fell through to a generic 500 instead of a `403`.
  4. **The big one**: never excluded `createdBy`/`createdAt`/`updatedBy`/`updatedAt` from client-supplied payload fields (only the PK was excluded that way) — so any caller that included those fields (the smoke test does, deliberately, to test this exact boundary) crashed every create/update on every table with SQL Server error 264, "column specified more than once". Never surfaced before because the current frontend form just happens not to send them. Fixed the same way the PK already was: explicitly skip audit columns from client input.
  - Also added: **server-side uppercase normalization** for every `*_code`/`short_name`/`code`-named column across the generic API (matched by naming convention, not per-table config) plus the three Tier1 dedicated entities (`LegalEntity`, `Counterparty`, `UserRole`) — a lowercase value typed anywhere now always lands uppercase in the DB.
  - Also added: `GlobalExceptionHandler`'s catch-all was silently swallowing every 500 with zero server-side logging — every bug above was invisible in the logs until this was fixed first.
- **Schema bug, not just a Java bug — `V97__nullable_unique_constraint_fix.sql`**: `legal_entity.lei_code`, `counterparty.lei_code`, and `vessel.mmsi` were plain (non-filtered) `UNIQUE` constraints on nullable columns — SQL Server treats every `NULL` as equal, so at most one row in each table could ever have no LEI/MMSI (the normal case — LEI is only mandatory for certain regulated entity types). Found by the very first `LegalEntityControllerTest` test (a plain create with no LEI code) failing against a completely fresh dev DB. Fixed the same way `exchange.uq_exchange_mic`/`market.ix_market_exchange` already handle this elsewhere in the schema: replaced with a filtered unique index (`WHERE col IS NOT NULL`).
- **Frontend — two real, separate bugs, neither about the backend at all**:
  1. `VITE_USE_MOCKS=true` in `.env.development` meant the whole frontend was running against in-memory MSW mock data the entire time, never touching the real backend — explains "UI changes don't save to DB" reports. Once MSW's service worker is ever started in a browser tab it stays registered at the browser/origin level across reloads and dev-server restarts until explicitly unregistered — `main.tsx` now self-heals this (unregisters any stale worker whenever mocks are off).
  2. The override file meant to flip that flag was initially named `.env.local` — **wrong filename**: Vite's env-file precedence is `.env < .env.local < .env.[mode] < .env.[mode].local`, so a plain `.env.local` is actually *overridden* by `.env.development`, not the other way around. However many hard-refreshes were tried, the server itself never picked up the override. Renamed to `.env.development.local` (verified this time by curling the actual served bundle and checking the inlined `import.meta.env` value, not just inferring from HTTP status codes).
- **New: `etrm-backend/src/test/java/...` — 142 JUnit/MockMvc integration tests against the real DB** (`cd etrm-backend && set -a && source .env && set +a && mvn test`), covering CRUD + 400/404/409/403 paths for all 9 dedicated controllers (`LegalEntity`, `Counterparty` incl. nested contacts/bank-accounts/addresses, `ParentCompanyGuarantee`, `Address`/`Contact` pool+links, `Rbac` incl. full role-approval lifecycle, `FieldPermission`, `SystemUser`, `Auth`) plus `ReferenceDataCrudSmokeTest`'s per-table sweep of all 81 create-enabled generic tables. Every bug listed above was found *by* writing and running this suite, not before it.
  - **Meta-lesson from the suite itself**: `SystemUserController` and `RbacController`'s role endpoints have no hard-delete (only deactivate/reject) — two test classes (`SystemUserControllerTest`, `RbacControllerTest`) had no way to clean up their created rows through the API and left 15 junk `app_user` rows and 28 junk `user_role` rows in the real dev DB across repeated runs before this was caught. Fixed by adding `@AfterEach` JDBC-based cleanup to both. **Not yet audited**: `LegalEntityControllerTest`/`CounterpartyControllerTest`/`ParentCompanyGuaranteeControllerTest`/`FieldPermissionControllerTest` likely have the same lower-severity issue (their entities support deactivate but not hard delete either) — flagged, not yet fixed.
- **Created a real `admin` / `ADMIN`-role login** (`admin` / `AdminDev2026!`, `userId=25`) via the actual API + real role-assignment approval workflow (not a SQL shortcut), for whenever real permission enforcement lands — per `SecurityConfig`'s own note, every authenticated endpoint is currently unrestricted regardless of role, so this account has no different *effective* access yet than any other logged-in user.

**Added `etrm-system/database/test-data/` — hand-authored sample business data for the "entity" tables `database/consolidated/` deliberately leaves empty.** User asked whether test data existed for anything beyond reference/lookup rows — it didn't: querying the live DB found ~68 entity tables (`legal_entity`, `counterparty`, `trader`, `book`, `vessel`, `pipeline`, `location`, etc.) with zero rows anywhere. Since these tables had never held real data, there was nothing to extract with `mssql-scripter` — the file (`database/test-data/snapshots/2026-07-12/01_core_tier1_test_data.sql`) is hand-authored instead, one consistent fictional trading group ("Meridian Trading": 3 legal entities across UK/US/Singapore) across 24 core Tier 1 tables (deferring niche commodity-specific ones like `metal_warrant`/`lng_boil_off_rule`/`power_pnode`). Follows the same dated-snapshot convention as `consolidated/` (own top-level `README.md` + per-snapshot `README.md`), with an explicit prerequisite on `consolidated/snapshots/2026-07-12/` being applied first. Verification against a from-scratch throwaway DB (schema → seed → this file) caught two bugs before landing: (1) `vessel.mmsi` is a plain (non-filtered) `UNIQUE` constraint, which rejects multiple `NULL`s — all 3 vessel rows needed real MMSI values; (2) `vessel`/`vessel_certificate`/`market` all carry filtered indexes (`ix_vessel_vetting`, `ix_vc_expiry`, `ix_market_exchange`), which need `SET QUOTED_IDENTIFIER ON` at insert time — a `SET ANSI_NULLS ON`/`SET QUOTED_IDENTIFIER ON` preamble had been intended for the file's header but was silently dropped during a header+body concatenation step; re-added and re-verified 0 errors, all 24 tables confirmed populated.

**Follow-up — made the test-data file idempotent and applied it to the real local dev `ETRM_DB` (not just the throwaway verification DB).** User asked to actually load the data (not just leave it as a verified-but-unapplied file) and wanted `IF NOT EXISTS` guards added so the script is safe to re-run in future without erroring or duplicating rows. Wrapped every `INSERT` with `IF NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM dbo.<table> WHERE <pk> = <id>)` keyed off the explicit id being inserted (the one `UPDATE` — the `desk.head_trader_id` backfill — needed no guard, since re-setting the same value is naturally idempotent). Verified the guard actually works, not just that it looks right: ran the file twice in a row against a fresh throwaway DB, 0 errors both times, row counts unchanged between runs (no duplicates). First confirmed `ETRM_DB` itself wasn't accidentally about to receive a duplicate load of `database/consolidated/`'s reference seed data — checked `flyway_schema_history` (frontier already at V96, matching the consolidated snapshot) and spot-checked `currency`/`country`/`lookup_value` row counts (already non-zero, since `01_master_data_seed.sql` was originally extracted FROM this exact live database) — so only the test-data file, not the consolidated seed file, needed to be applied. Ran it against `ETRM_DB`: 0 errors, all 24 tables confirmed populated (`legal_entity`=3, `counterparty`=6, `vessel`=3, etc., matching the throwaway-DB verification exactly).

**Migration frontier: V97.** Next migration is **V98**. Every SQL change must be written to BOTH `etrm-system/database/NN_name.sql` (no V prefix) AND `etrm-backend/src/main/resources/db/migration/VNN__name.sql` (V prefix) — keep them byte-identical.

**Added `etrm-system/database/consolidated/` — a generated, flattened master-data schema+seed snapshot, not part of the Flyway chain.** User asked for one consolidated schema file plus seed-data files split by Master Data Hub group. Generated via `mssql-scripter` (`pip install mssql-scripter`, run as `python3 -m mssqlscripter` — its CLI shim's shebang is broken on a `python3`-only machine) against the live, fully-migrated `ETRM_DB`, not hand-assembled from the 96 migration files — far more reliable given how much the schema changed shape across migrations (columns renamed/converted/dropped repeatedly). Table scope: the 81 tables in `master_data_table_registry` + Tier 1 Hub entities (`MasterDataHub.tsx`) + 8 supporting tables the Hub references but doesn't card (`address`, `document_store`, `field_permission_profile`, `gtc_version`, `pipeline_point`, `pricing_trigger_event_type`, `pricing_window_rule`, `screen_field_registry`) = **154 tables**, explicitly excluding trade/position/nomination/delivery_instruction (operational, stays migration-only). Verified by actually applying both files to a throwaway database on the same container until 0 errors and row counts matched the source exactly (1385 rows) — this caught two real `mssql-scripter` quirks: system-versioned tables need `SYSTEM_VERSIONING=ON` deferred until after the PK exists (tool's default ordering doesn't satisfy SQL Server's requirement), and `pricing_rule`'s non-standard-named temporal columns (`valid_from_sys`/`valid_to_sys`) get wrongly included in data `INSERT`s. **Real finding along the way**: computed the Hub's 16 groups' FK dependency graph and found it's densely cyclic — there is no group-by-group load order that satisfies every FK (Products & Markets needs Finance & Settlement's currency; Finance & Settlement's bank_account needs Counterparties & Agreements; that needs Organization & Users; which needs Products & Markets back again). So the per-group files (`02`–`18`) are reference-only for browsing a specific group's data, clearly labeled as such; `01_master_data_seed.sql` is the one actually-runnable file, using a computed per-*table* topological order instead.

**Follow-up — moved into a dated, immutable snapshot structure per user request.** Files now live at `database/consolidated/snapshots/2026-07-12/` (migration frontier V96), not directly under `consolidated/`. `database/consolidated/README.md` is now an index documenting the release rule: snapshot folders are named `YYYY-MM-DD`, never edited in place once created, and a new dated folder is added (not overwritten) whenever the migration frontier moves, the Hub/registry table scope changes, or seed data changes meaningfully enough to warrant a fresh point-in-time record. Next person cutting a snapshot should copy `snapshots/2026-07-12/README.md` as a starting template and follow the numbered process in the top-level `database/consolidated/README.md`.

**Free local Docker setup added (`docker-compose.yml` + `docker/db-init/`) — and along the way, the full 96-migration Flyway chain got its first-ever real-SQL-Server run, surfacing and fixing ~40 real bugs.** User asked how to run SQL Server locally for free; built a one-command `docker compose up -d sqlserver && docker compose up db-init` setup (SQL Server 2022 Developer edition — free for dev/test, full feature set) plus `docs/RUNNING_LOCALLY.md` confirming every layer of the stack (DB, Spring Boot, Maven, React, AG Grid Community, npm packages) has a genuinely free tier. Verifying the setup meant actually running Flyway against a real container for the first time ever (previously only hand-reviewed, per the backend README's own "not compile-verified" disclaimer) — it failed at V1 and kept failing, one bug at a time, all the way to V96. Fixed every one in place (both `etrm-backend/.../db/migration/VNN__*.sql` and the mirrored `database/NN_*.sql`), re-running `flyway migrate` against a freshly wiped DB after each fix until `flyway info` showed all 96 as `Success`, then confirmed a second `migrate` run is a clean no-op. Recurring bug categories (full detail in `docs/RUNNING_LOCALLY.md`):
  - **Temporal table setup** (V1/V6/V7): `PERIOD FOR SYSTEM_TIME` must be declared in the same `ALTER TABLE ADD` as the generated columns, not a separate statement.
  - **Batch-compile-time column resolution**: a `CHECK` constraint, index, or second `ALTER TABLE` can't reference a column added earlier in the *same unbatched script* — needs `GO` between them. The single most common bug, hit in a dozen files with zero `GO` statements.
  - **Dropping a column requires dropping every dependent object first** (indexes, `CHECK`/`UNIQUE` constraints, and for temporal tables, the matching `_history` table column with matching nullability) — SQL Server doesn't cascade this.
  - **Unnamed inline `DEFAULT` constraints** block `DROP COLUMN` until dynamically looked up via `sys.default_constraints` and dropped by generated name — recurred across a dozen currency/status/type-code conversions (V55/V78/V81/V82/V83/V95).
  - **FK requires exact type match including length** — several `VARCHAR(10)` columns meant to reference a `VARCHAR(20)` code column; SQL Server rejects rather than truncates. Also CHAR vs NCHAR/VARCHAR mismatches on ~8 currency columns.
  - **Demo seed data assuming trade/order/counterparty rows that no migration ever actually inserts** (mirroring frontend MSW mock IDs) — now guarded to no-op on a fresh DB instead of throwing FK violations (V33/V40/V41/V88/V89).
  - **A few genuinely missing tables/products** referenced by later migrations but never created by any earlier one — `trade_lng_detail`/`trade_metals_detail`/`trade_agri_detail` (added to V9) and benchmark products `BRENT-CRUDE`/`WTI-CRUDE`/`TTF-GAS`/`LME-COPPER`/`CBOT-CORN`/`HENRY-HUB-GAS`/`HEATING-OIL` (added to V24/V39/V69).
  - One `(x IS NULL) = (y IS NULL)` — not valid T-SQL, boolean predicates aren't comparable values (V51).
  - `dbo.period.commodity_type` was converted to an INT FK by V85 but V93 (which runs after) still assumed the old VARCHAR shape for a composite FK to it — rewired V93's `trade_order.commodity_type` to match.
  - Known pre-existing gap, not fixed this pass: `V14`/`V16`/`V18` have minor drift between the backend migration folder (what Flyway actually reads) and the `database/` mirror — doesn't affect the migration run but worth reconciling for the byte-identical convention.

**Follow-up — fixed both items flagged above, plus got the backend fully booting against real SQL Server for the first time.** User asked to fix the `mvn spring-boot:run` failure and the `V14`/`V16`/`V18` drift, then how to connect via SSMS/a VS Code extension.
  - **`V14`/`V16`/`V18` drift**: `database/` was missing `16_custom_config.sql` entirely and had stale content for `14`/`18`. Copied the backend versions over (backend is the one Flyway actually reads, so it's the source of truth) — all 96 files now confirmed byte-identical via a full diff sweep.
  - **`spring-boot:run` ASM failure — root cause was not the Maven plugin.** It's Spring Framework's own bundled ASM (`spring-core-6.1.14.jar`, used at runtime for `@ComponentScan` classpath scanning), which doesn't parse Java 25 bytecode (class file major version 69) yet. Proven by testing three escape routes in order: `mvn package` (same failure, in `repackage`), running the compiled classes directly via `java -cp` with a Maven-built classpath (same failure, this time explicitly from `org.springframework.asm.ClassReader` during component-scan, confirming it's Spring's ASM not the Maven plugin's) — at which point installing an older JDK was ruled out too, since `javac --release 25` requires a JDK ≥25 to even compile, so swapping the *runtime* JDK down doesn't help. The actual fix: audited `src/main/java` for anything requiring Java >21 — only `record` (Java 16+) is used, nothing sealed-class/pattern-matching/25-specific — so lowered `pom.xml`'s `<java.version>` from `25` to `21` (LTS). Recompiled clean, then verified a full `mvn spring-boot:run` startup against the real Dockerized SQL Server: it got past the ASM issue entirely, connected over SSL, and Flyway ran.
  - **Found and fixed a second, unrelated bug while verifying the above**: `.env`'s `DB_URL` contains `;` (`databaseName=...;encrypt=true;trustServerCertificate=true`) — bash's `source .env` (used by the "run from terminal" instructions) treats unquoted `;` as a command separator and silently truncates the value at the first one, losing everything after `localhost:1433`. This surfaced as an SSL trust error ("trustServerCertificate property is set to false") that looked unrelated until traced back. Fixed by quoting the value in both `.env` and `.env.example` (`DB_URL="jdbc:sqlserver://..."`) — VS Code's `envFile` parser handles either form, but a bare terminal `source` needs the quotes.
  - **New, separate issue surfaced once the backend actually booted**: Hibernate's schema validation (`ddl-auto: validate`) now fails on `Address.addressId` — mapped `Long`/`BIGINT` in the JPA entity, but `address.address_id` is `INT IDENTITY` per `V1`. This is a genuine JPA-entity-vs-schema mismatch, not a migration bug — the backend README already disclosed the ~130-table entity layer was never run against a live schema before. Documented in `docs/RUNNING_LOCALLY.md` as a known follow-up (likely more entities affected, same `INT` vs `BIGINT` PK pattern) rather than fixed unprompted, since the scope (auditing every entity against every table) is a distinct body of work from what was asked.

**V96 — reviewed a user-supplied 10-table wishlist of commodity-specific master data (Metals/Oil&LNG/Power/Agri/Intercompany) against the live schema before building anything, per the "research before schema" rule.** Findings: 8 of the 10 were missing entirely (new tables); 1 (`tank_heel`) was a near-duplicate of `dbo.tank.heel_volume_m3` (V4) — fixed via `ALTER TABLE tank` adding only the 3 genuinely missing columns (`heel_product_id`, `min_operating_level_m3`, `max_safe_fill_level_m3`) instead of a redundant 1:1 table; 1 (`lng_boil_off_rule`) complements rather than duplicates `dbo.vessel.guaranteed_boil_off_rate_pct_per_day` (V53) — that's a single nameplate spec, this is a real rule set scoped to vessel and/or storage_facility. New tables (`96_commodity_specific_master_data.sql`): `metal_warrant`, `metal_assay_component_rule`, `lng_boil_off_rule`, `power_pnode`, `power_ancillary_service_type` (the exact follow-up V11's own header flagged as not-yet-built), `agri_moisture_discount_scale`, `agri_crop_year_lifecycle`, `intercompany_transfer_rule`, `payment_calendar_assignment` — all registered in `master_data_table_registry`. Every code-shaped field the user proposed (geography_country_id, currency amounts, etc.) was built as a surrogate `*_id` FK to a real table (`country`, `currency`, `unit_of_measure`...) rather than a bare code column, matching the V86/V87/V95 convention; the user's literal `mst_` table-name prefix was dropped since this schema has never used it. One field was corrected outright: `metal_warrant.is_rent_paid_to_date BIT` → `rent_paid_through_date DATE`, since "paid to date" means a date, not a flag. SQL only in this pass — no frontend/TypeScript wiring done yet (registry rows make the tables visible on the generic Static Data screen with no code, but any dedicated forms/pages are still open work).

**V96 follow-up — frontend + API wiring for the 9 new tables, plus a hardcoded-unit-column review the user asked for.** Two separate asks:
  - **API**: confirmed (not built — it already exists) that `/api/v1/reference-data/{table}` (`ReferenceDataController`/`ReferenceDataCrudService`/`ReferenceDataMetadataService`) is a fully generic, SQL-Server-catalog-driven CRUD API — adding a table is a `master_data_table_registry` row, not new Java code (per the Master Data Entry Technical Design doc). The V96 registry inserts already wire all 9 tables into the real API with zero backend changes needed.
  - **Frontend**: the generic mechanism only reached MSW (dev-mode mock) once `etrm-frontend/src/mocks/referenceData.ts` got per-table `registrySeed`/`metadataSeed`/`rowSeed` entries — MSW can't introspect a live DB schema the way the real backend does. Added those for all 9 tables, plus 5 new lightweight FK-mirror entries (`vessel`, `unit_of_measure`, `legal_entity`, `payment_term`, `location` — reusing real ids from their dedicated stores/pages, e.g. `vesselId 1 = NORDIC LUNA`) so foreign keys resolve to real labels instead of raw ids, matching the existing `product`/`storage_facility`/`counterparty`/`holiday_calendar` mirror pattern. `unit_of_measure` closes a pre-existing gap flagged in a comment next to `freight_rate_index.uomId` (no `uom` mock table existed at all before this). Verified live via Playwright against the running dev app (not just `tsc -b --noEmit`, which was also clean): all 9 tables render with resolved FK labels, Add/Edit modal opens with the right control per column kind, no console errors.
  - **Hardcoded-unit-column review**: user asked whether fields like `net_weight_mt`/`heel_volume_m3` should instead be a generic `value` + `uom_id` pair. Audited the whole schema (`grep` across every `database/*.sql`) rather than guessing. Finding: this codebase deliberately runs **two coexisting patterns**, not one inconsistency — (1) a fixed-unit-suffix column (`_mt`, `_cbm`, `_kg`) on `vessel`/`tank`/`truck`/`railcar`/`container`/`storage_facility` physical dimension fields, used because the real-world unit for that specific field is fixed by industry convention (a tanker's cargo capacity is always quoted in cbm/mt, never barrels) — matching real shipping/ETRM systems, not an oversight; and (2) a generic `value` + `*_uom_id` FK pair (`location.capacity`+`capacity_uom_id`, `pipeline.capacity`+`capacity_uom_id`, `commodity_grade_standard.price_adjustment_per_uom`+`adjustment_uom_id`) used only where the same field genuinely varies in unit row-to-row. Checked V96's own new fields against this: all of them already use whichever pattern actually fits (`net_weight_mt` fixed per LME convention; the two new `tank` heel columns match their existing `_m3` siblings on the same table; `metal_assay_component_rule`/`agri_moisture_discount_scale` already used the generic `*_currency_id`/`*_uom_id` pattern). Recommended against a blanket schema-wide conversion — it would be pure churn across ~15 already-shipped tables (schema + frontend types + MSW mocks) for no functional gain, not a bug fix. Flagged as available if the user wants specific tables changed, but not done unprompted.

**V96 real bug found: the 9 new tables were invisible on `MasterDataHub.tsx`, the actual page the user was looking at.** User reported "I still don't see new master data items" after the frontend-wiring pass above claimed completion. Root cause: this app has **two separate, independently-maintained catalogs** of Static Data tables — (1) `master_data_table_registry` (DB) / `registrySeed` (mock), which drives the registry-generic Tier2 sidebar at `/static-data` and *did* already list all 9 new tables correctly (confirmed via Playwright — this is why my earlier verification pass reported success), and (2) `MasterDataHub.tsx`'s own hardcoded `Entry[]` array powering the card-based `/master-data` landing page, which is a curated catalog that nothing auto-populates from the registry. My earlier pass only touched (1); the user was on (2). Added all 9 entries there (same `live: true`, `db`, `group`, `label`, `path: '/static-data/{table}'`, `description`, `tags` shape as every existing entry), placed in their matching existing group sections (`Products & Markets`, `Freight & Shipping`, `Power & Energy`, `Counterparties & Agreements`, `Calendar & Periods`). Verified live via Playwright: all 9 labels now render on `/master-data`, and clicking a card navigates to the correct populated `/static-data/{table}` page. **Lesson for next time a Tier2 table is added: it needs BOTH the registry row AND a `MasterDataHub.tsx` entry — the registry alone is not sufficient for a table to be discoverable from the main Master Data landing page.**

**V95 — converted `currency_code`/`country_code`/`jurisdiction` natural-key FKs to surrogate `currency_id`/`country_id` FKs, closing the largest remaining code-based-FK family flagged in V94's future-work list.** User asked to work on this specifically (of the two families V94 listed — location/uom already done, currency/country was the much bigger one at ~30+~19 raw grep hits).
  - **SQL** (`95_currency_country_code_to_id_conversion.sql`): converted **32 currency columns** across ~25 tables and **21 existing country/jurisdiction FK columns + 3 genuine gaps** (`insurance_provider.country_code`, `regulatory_report_type.jurisdiction`, `trade_repository.jurisdiction` had no FK constraint at all before this — added fresh). Same ADD-nullable/backfill/DROP-old/restore-NOT-NULL/ADD-FK pattern as V94. Two structural findings verified directly against the live schema before writing any ALTER (same discipline as the V30/V91 precedent):
    1. **V87's `fk_pipeline_country` targeted a column that doesn't exist** — `04_product_spec_mot_pipeline.sql` drops and recreates `dbo.pipeline` with only a CSV `country_codes VARCHAR(100)` column, no singular `country_code`. Fixed in place in `87_currency_country_reference_integrity.sql` (`IF EXISTS(sys.columns)` guard, mirroring V91's fix to V30's dead CREATE) rather than worked around in V95 — `dbo.pipeline` is excluded from the country conversion entirely, there's nothing single-valued to convert.
    2. **`dbo.legal_entity.base_currency`** was code-based since V1 (`fk_le_currency`) and never appeared in V87's own currency sweep despite V87's header comment citing it as the pattern to match — included as the 32nd currency column.
  - **Frontend, ~25 tables across the whole app** — split into 5 pieces to manage risk and enable parallelism: Trade Blotter (`features/trade/types.ts` + `TradeBlotter.tsx` + trade order/item/cost mock data) done directly for tight control, matching V94's approach for its highest-risk file; the other ~20 tables split into 4 parallel background-agent briefs by cohesive area (Organization/Counterparty/Legal-Entity; Credit & Risk; Markets & Logistics — 12 sub-areas; Pricing/BOLMO/BALMO/generic-lookup), each given the exact column list up front so no agent had to make a scope judgment call, all briefed to re-read `mocks/etrmHandlers.ts` fresh before editing since they were touching the same file concurrently.
  - **Foundational gap fixed first**: the frontend's `Country` type had **no `countryId` at all** — every consumer keyed off `countryCode` as if it were the identity. Added `countryId: number` (V86's real seed order, GB=1...QA=18) before any other conversion could start, since every other agent's work depended on it existing.
  - **A real bug the conversion itself would have introduced, caught and fixed before it shipped**: `AgriDetail.originCountry` (a frontend-only enrichment field, no backing DB column at all) shared the same `countryOpts` variable as the real `trade_order.originCountryId` field in `TradeBlotter.tsx` — once `countryOpts` was repointed to emit numeric ids, this unrelated field would have silently stored a number in a `string | null` slot. Renamed it to `originCountryId` too, even though there was no SQL column to convert, specifically to avoid that regression.
  - **Concurrent-agent gap found independently by two agents, self-reconciled**: `countriesStore` (21 rows) was missing several countries actually referenced in seed data — Switzerland (needed by 4+ Swiss-domiciled counterparties/tax registrations) was added as `countryId: 22` by the Organization/Counterparty agent; the Markets & Logistics agent, running concurrently, found the same table needed 6 more (Denmark, Marshall Islands, Liberia, Cyprus, Panama, Malaysia for vessel flags/transport operators) plus Italy for a truck fleet — added as `23-29`, correctly noticing CH was already there and continuing the sequence rather than colliding. Verified afterward: ids 1-29 sequential, no duplicates, no two agents assigned the same id to different countries.
  - **`ReferenceDataTable.tsx`** (the generic component behind ~120 Tier-2 Static Data tables) gained a genuinely new capability during this pass: generic `foreign_key`/`foreignKeyTable: 'country'` resolution (it previously only knew how to resolve FK columns keyed by *code* for ISO sets, not a numeric id-based country FK) — needed by `regulatory_report_type`/`insurance_provider`'s fresh gap-closing FKs and reused by several Tier-2 tables in the Markets & Logistics batch (`transport_operator`, `balancing_authority`, `metal_brand`). Built once by the Pricing/BOLMO agent, independently duplicated by two other agents who then found the first agent's version mid-edit and reverted their own to reuse it rather than leaving three competing implementations — confirmed via each agent's own report, not just assumed.
  - **Verified, not just typechecked**: full `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean across the whole frontend (0 errors) after all 4 agents + the direct Trade Blotter work landed; `mvn -q -o compile` clean in `etrm-backend`. Live Playwright pass across 23 touched routes (Trade Blotter, Counterparties, Legal Entities, Margin Agreements, Brokers, Vessels, GL Accounts, and more) — zero console/page errors; screenshots confirmed real resolved values everywhere a currency/country field appears (Legal Entities' "Jur."/"Ccy" columns show `GB`/`GBP` etc., not raw ids; Vessels' "Flag" column shows `"MH — Marshall Islands"`; Counterparties' "Jur." column shows `CH` for the Swiss entities specifically, confirming the id-22 fix actually took effect end-to-end, not just in the seed data).

**V94 — converted `location_code`/`uom_code` natural-key FKs to surrogate `location_id`/`uom_id` FKs, end to end (SQL + every frontend consumer), keeping the GUI showing only resolved names/short codes, never a raw id or bare code.** User asked to cross-check the whole project for this pattern rather than assume V93's two brand-new tables were the only offenders.
  - **SQL** (`94_location_uom_code_to_id_conversion.sql`): both `dbo.location` and `dbo.unit_of_measure` already carried a surrogate IDENTITY PK (`location_id`/`uom_id`) alongside their natural code column — V90/V91/V93 had wired the child-table FKs onto the code column instead of the id, the wrong pattern relative to how most of this schema already does it (e.g. `dbo.trade.uom_id`, `dbo.product.default_uom_id`). Converted 9 location columns across 6 tables (`trade_transport_agreement_detail` load/discharge, `trade_oil/lng/metals_detail` title-transfer, `bolmo_agreement`/`trade_order` delivery, `nomination`/`delivery_instruction` location) and ~19 uom columns across 13 tables (`trade_order`, `trade_item`, `bolmo_agreement`, `bolmo_leg`, `balmo_product`, `settlement_price`, `broker.commission_uom`, `broker_fee_agreement`, `trade_option_detail.strike_uom`, `trade_storage_agreement_detail` capacity/tariff, `trade_swap_detail` fixed/notional, `trade_transport_agreement_detail.capacity_uom`, `trade_order_price_adjustment.adjustment_uom`, `commodity_grade_standard.adjustment_uom`, `nomination`/`delivery_instruction` uom). Pattern per column: add the new `*_id` nullable, backfill by joining the old code to the master table, drop the old FK + code column, restore `NOT NULL` where the original was, add the real FK on the id. Deliberately out of scope (separate families, not requested): `pipeline_code`, `route_code`.
  - **Frontend, split three ways to manage risk**: (1) `features/trade/types.ts` + `features/trade/TradeBlotter.tsx` — the highest-risk file (2500+ lines, this doc's own prior CRITICAL notes on it) — done directly rather than delegated, for tight control. Renamed every in-scope field, repointed `locationOptionsFor`/`uomOptionsFor` to emit `value: locationId`/`value: uomId` while keeping the label as `"CODE — Name"` (location) or the bare `uomCode` (UoM, per explicit user decision — UoM codes like BBL/MT are already short, trader-standard labels, no separate "full name" concept wanted). `TradeOrder`/`TradeItem` kept a denormalized `uomCode`/`deliveryLocationName` display field alongside the new real `uomId`/`deliveryLocationId`, matching the codebase's established denormalization convention. `SwapDetail`/`OptionDetail`/`StorageAgreementDetail`/`TransportAgreementDetail` have no frontend form UI at all yet (confirmed via grep before assuming) — only their `types.ts` shapes needed renaming, no `TradeBlotter.tsx` form changes. `FreightDetail`'s own `loadLocationCode`/`dischargeLocationCode` deliberately left untouched — different table (`trade_freight_detail`, not `trade_transport_agreement_detail`) and out of V94's SQL scope entirely. (2) Two parallel background agents handled the mechanical mock-data layer (`mocks/etrmHandlers.ts` seed rows + `compute*`/`denormalize*` helpers) and the 8 smaller independent feature areas (BOLMO, Brokers, Broker Fee Agreements, BALMO Products, Settlement Prices, Nominations, Delivery Instructions, and `commodity_grade_standard`'s generic Tier-2 mock row) — both briefed with an exact, unambiguous field-rename table since all judgment calls (which fields are in/out of scope, the UoM display decision) were already resolved before delegating.
  - **Verified, not just typechecked**: `tradeOrdersStore`/`tradeItemsStore` in `etrmHandlers.ts` are typed `unknown[]`, so `tsc` cannot catch a field-name mismatch there — live Playwright verification was load-bearing, not optional, for this change. Confirmed via screenshots: Trade Blotter grid still shows `"500,000 BBL"` (resolved via the new `uomId`), BOLMO grid resolves `deliveryLocationId` to real names ("Sullom Voe Terminal", "Port of Rotterdam"), Nominations/Settlement Prices still show short UoM codes directly — no raw ids, no `undefined` leaks, zero console/page errors across every touched route. One good catch from the mock-data agent: the field-permission map and field-registry array in `etrmHandlers.ts` had matching string-literal keys (e.g. `'oilDetail.loadLocationCode'`) that `tsc` couldn't have caught since they're untyped strings — renamed to avoid a silent metadata-drift bug.
  - `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean; `mvn -q -o compile` clean in `etrm-backend` (no new errors from V94).

**Future-work reference: remaining code-based FK families, inventoried but NOT converted this session** (user asked for this list specifically, to decide later which if any to tackle next). Two buckets:
  - **Bucket 1 — cheap conversions (master table already has a surrogate id sitting unused for this exact FK):** `currency_code` (~30 FK columns, mostly from `87_currency_country_reference_integrity.sql` plus `trade_cost`/`trade_order_cost` V88 and `trade_order.broker_fee_currency_code` V89 — by far the largest single family), `country_code` (~19 FK columns, V86/V87), `pipeline_code` (`nomination`, `trade_transport_agreement_detail`), `route_code`/`transport_route` (`trade_transport_agreement_detail`, 1 column), `credit_term_code`/`credit_term` (`trade.credit_term_code` only — `counterparty.credit_term_id` already correctly id-based, a mixed-pattern family like location/uom were), `payment_calendar_code`/`holiday_calendar` (`trade.payment_calendar_code` only), `storage_facility_code`/`storage_facility` (`trade_storage_agreement_detail` only).
  - **Bucket 2 — no surrogate id exists to convert onto:** none found — `product`, `broker`, `commodity`, `exchange` all turned out to already be fully id-based everywhere (no `*_code` FK exists for them at all), so there's currently no real Bucket 2 case in this schema.
  - **Composite-key, structurally different problem (not a bucket 1/2 case):** `period_code`→`period(period_code, commodity_type)` and `incoterm_code`→`incoterm(code, version_year)` on `trade_order` — already solved in V93 by adding a second matching column and building a composite FK against the master table's existing composite unique key, not by swapping to a surrogate id (neither `period` nor `incoterm` has a spare single-column id that fits this specific FK shape). One related gap surfaced during this inventory: `trade_order_item.incoterm_code` (V33) has no FK constraint at all — bare column, not yet touched by any migration.

**V93 — closed the master-data FK/UI backlog from the "what master data is still pending" review.** User asked to fix two items from that review: (1) the "~12 known missing FK constraints" backlog item, and (2) the 9 `live: false` Master Data Hub placeholders with no real page (`product_spec_template`, `nomination`, `delivery_instruction`, `transport_route`, `price_index_source`, `bank_account`, `parent_company_guarantee`, `tax_registration`, `contact`).
  - **The FK backlog turned out mostly already fixed** — re-reading the handoff doc's own session history in order found that V91 (a *later* migration than the V90 entry that first listed the "~12 findings") had already added all of them: `location_code` family, `pipeline_code`/`route_code`/`storage_facility_code`, `trade.credit_term_code`/`payment_calendar_code`. Verified directly against the SQL (not just doc text) before treating it as done — a stale-memory trap worth flagging: the handoff doc's session-recap entries are chronological but a later entry can supersede an earlier one's "deferred" note without the earlier note ever being marked resolved.
  - **What was genuinely still open**: `trade_order.period_code` → `period(period_code, commodity_type)` and `trade_order.incoterm_code` → `incoterm(code, version_year)` — both deferred in V91 because the target tables use composite unique keys `trade_order` didn't mirror. Asked the user via `AskUserQuestion`; chose to add the missing columns properly rather than pin to a filtered-index shortcut. **V93** adds `trade_order.commodity_type` (mirrors `period`'s `OIL/POWER/GAS/AGRICULTURAL/METALS/NULL` CHECK — a FREIGHT trade order backfills to `NULL`, i.e. matches only commodity-agnostic period rows, since `period.commodity_type`'s CHECK has no FREIGHT value at all) and `incoterm_version_year` (backfilled to the max active version for the code), then adds both composite FKs. Documented caveat in the migration comment: SQL Server multi-column FKs use MATCH SIMPLE, so a NULL in either new column skips validation for that row — not a regression vs. today's total absence of a constraint, just not airtight for FREIGHT legs.
  - **New tables**: `dbo.nomination` (physical scheduling nomination against a `trade_order` leg — pipeline/vessel/terminal/rail/truck, status lifecycle DRAFT→SUBMITTED→ACCEPTED/REJECTED→COMPLETED) and `dbo.delivery_instruction` (formal load/discharge/receipt/delivery instruction, optionally referencing a nomination) — the two Hub placeholders that had no SQL at all before this.
  - **Frontend build, parallelized across 4 background agents** (each independently briefed off the exact same template — `features/logistics/vessel-certificates/` — and told not to touch the two shared files `AppRouter.tsx`/`MasterDataHub.tsx`, wired centrally afterward to avoid concurrent-edit collisions on those two): Nominations + Delivery Instructions (`features/operations/`); Product Spec Templates (`features/markets/spec-templates/` — reused the existing `productSpecTemplateStore` rather than duplicating it, since it already backed a nested `/products/:id/spec-templates` endpoint) + Transport Routes (`features/logistics/transport-routes/`, new store); Price Index ↔ Source Mapping (`features/pricing/price-index-sources/` — the mock CRUD already existed from V90, only the page was missing); and four cross-entity "directory" pages for `contact`/`tax_registration`/`bank_account`/`parent_company_guarantee` (`features/organization/contacts/`, `features/credit/tax-registrations/`, `features/finance/bank-accounts/`, `features/credit/pcg/`) — a genuinely different use case from the existing inline per-entity tabs on `CounterpartyFormPage`/`LegalEntityFormDrawer` (e.g. "every bank account in the system" vs. "this one counterparty's accounts"). PCG's directory page was near-trivial (`useGuarantees()`/`GuaranteeFormDrawer`/`useEntityResolver` already existed unscoped); Contacts/Tax/Bank Accounts needed three new thin drawers since their existing `*Section.tsx` components only edit a locally-staged array committed on the parent form's save, with no standalone per-record persistence path — new unscoped `GET /bank-accounts` and unscoped-mode additions to the existing `GET /entity-contacts`/`GET /entity-tax-registrations` handlers were added in `mocks/counterpartyHandlers.ts` to back them.
  - **Verified, not just built**: all 4 agents' concurrent edits to the shared `mocks/etrmHandlers.ts`/`mocks/counterpartyHandlers.ts` cross-checked afterward for duplicate `crudHandlers(...)` path registrations or clobbered sections (none found) before wiring routes — a real risk with 4 parallel agents touching the same mock file, called out explicitly since it's the kind of thing that can silently corrupt a shared file if not checked. Every grid column resolves FK-shaped fields to human labels (order→reference, location_code→name, vessel_id→name, counterparty_id→name, etc.) — checked live via Playwright screenshots, not just `tsc`, per the standing "verify correctness not just rendering" rule; one apparent bug (PCG grid showing "CounterpartySHELLPLC" with no space) turned out to be an `innerText`-scraping artifact of an antd `Tag` sitting next to text, not a real rendering bug — confirmed via screenshot before ruling it out. Full `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean after all 4 agents' edits + the central routing/Hub wiring; `mvn -q -o compile` clean in `etrm-backend` (no new errors from V93). Master Data Hub coverage: all 9 target entities now `live: true` with working routes.


**Fixed: Trade Blotter showed a raw `counterpartyId` number instead of a name after saving/reopening a trade** ("when you save the deal and open it in gui we show Counterparty id which is not correct should show the short name or full name"). Same shadow-vs-real mock-store trap as the CRITICAL legal-entity note above, just for counterparties, and only partially fixed previously (the netting-agreements handler already avoided it; `denormalizeTrade`/`computeCreditLimit` didn't). Root cause: `mocks/etrmHandlers.ts` had its own local `counterpartiesRef` array (10 entries) plus a dead duplicate `GET /counterparties` handler returning it — shadowed at runtime by the real `counterpartyHandlers.ts`/`cpStore` (registered earlier in `browser.ts`, only 3 entries: Shell Trading, Glencore International AG, Shell plc). `denormalizeTrade` (POST/PUT `/trades`) resolved names against the disconnected `counterpartiesRef`, and the 15 seed trades' `counterpartyId` values didn't consistently point at either list (4 ids were even reused for two different companies across different trades — e.g. id 2 meant both "BP Oil Trading" and "BP Energy Europe" depending on which trade row). Net effect: the real counterparty Select (built from the 3-row `cpStore`) had no matching option for most seed trades, so antd fell back to rendering the bare id.
  - Fix: expanded `counterpartySeed`/`cpStore` (`mocks/counterpartyData.ts`) from 3 to 13 counterparties, adding the 11 distinct companies actually referenced across the seed trades (BP Oil Trading, BP Energy Europe, Equinor Energy AS, Trafigura Group, Glencore Metals, RWE Supply & Trading, ExxonMobil Global Trading, Centrica Energy Trading, Glencore Energy UK, Vitol SA, Cargill International SA — ids 10-20, `nextCpId` bumped to 21). Corrected all 15 seed trades' `counterpartyId` to point at the matching real `cpStore` row (was internally inconsistent — same id, different companies, across different trade rows). `denormalizeTrade` and `computeCreditLimit` now resolve against `cpStore`/`legalName` instead of `counterpartiesRef`; deleted the dead `counterpartiesRef` array and its dead duplicate `/counterparties` handler entirely.
  - **Deliberately left alone**: the credit/collateral feature pages (margin agreements, netting agreements, CP GTC, collateral, credit limits, LCs) have their own static seed rows with `counterpartyId`/`counterpartyName` pairs that are *also* internally inconsistent with each other (e.g. id 2 = "Glencore International AG" in netting/GTC but "BP Oil Trading" in margin agreements/credit limits) — but those pages render pre-baked static strings directly, never re-resolving through a Select, so they don't exhibit the raw-id-display bug. Cosmetic flavor-text inconsistency only; flagging so it isn't mistaken for the same class of bug if it resurfaces.
  - Verified live via Playwright: opened TRD-2026-00004 (Glencore Metals) — grid, header, and the edit-form Select all show "Glencore Metals & Minerals AG" / "GLEN-METALS — Glencore Metals & Minerals AG", not a raw id. Created a brand-new trade end-to-end (New Trade → picked "VITOL — Vitol SA" from the now-13-row dropdown → Save) — reopened trade `TRD-2026-00016` correctly shows "Vitol SA" in both the title bar and the Counterparty field. `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean.

**V92 — fixed the credit_term_code/payment_calendar_code mock-vs-backend data-parity gap V91 surfaced but didn't fix.** Investigating turned up a THREE-way mismatch, not two: the backend SQL seed, the frontend's live Static Data "Credit Terms" page (`referenceData.ts`'s `credit_term` mock — `STANDARD_30`/`ISDA_CSA_STD`/`LC_BACKED`/`PARENT_GUAR`), and the Trade Blotter's own hardcoded `CREDIT_TERM_CODES` dropdown + mock trade seed data (`NET_30`/`NET_14`/...) all used different, non-overlapping vocabularies — same shape of problem independently existed for holiday calendars (backend `UK_BANK`/`US_FEDERAL`/... vs. the frontend's *own two separate* mocks: the live dedicated Holiday Calendars page's `holidayCalendarsStore`, `LON`/`NYC`/`NYMEX`/`LME`/`ECB`/`ICE-EU`, and `referenceData.ts`'s FK-label-resolution mirror of the same). Fixed by picking one canonical set per table and converging everything onto it, rather than picking a winner and discarding data:
  - **`credit_term`**: canonical = union of what the Trade Blotter already offered (`NET_7`..`NET_90`, `PREPAY`, `CASH_ON_DELIVERY`) and what the Static Data page already offered (`LC_BACKED`, `PARENT_GUAR`, `ISDA_CSA_STD`) — 11 codes. `92_credit_term_holiday_calendar_data_parity.sql` (mirrored to `V92__...sql`) deletes the backend's old 8 mismatched rows and inserts the 11; `referenceData.ts`'s `credit_term` array updated to the same 11 (kept `creditTermId` 2/3/4 stable since `cp_commercial_terms` mock rows reference them by ID; `id 1` repurposed `STANDARD_30`→`NET_30`, with the one `cpCommercialTermsStore` row denormalizing that ID's name updated to match). The Trade Blotter's own `CREDIT_TERM_CODES` const and its 15 seed trades' `creditTermCode` values needed **no changes** — they already used the right vocabulary; the other two sources needed to catch up to them.
  - **`holiday_calendar`**: canonical = the backend's existing codes (already richer — includes commodity-specific calendars like `TTF_GAS`/`EPEX_POWER` the frontend never had), plus one legitimately missing addition, `ECB_TARGET` (EUR TARGET2 — the frontend already assumed a EUR calendar existed under the name `ECB`; backend had none). Frontend's `holidayCalendarsStore` (the live `/calendar/holiday-calendars` page) renamed `LON`→`UK_BANK`, `NYC`→`US_FEDERAL`, `NYMEX`→`NYMEX_WTI`, `LME`→`LME_METALS`, `ECB`→`ECB_TARGET`, `ICE-EU`→`ICE_BRENT`; `referenceData.ts`'s FK-mirror copy updated to match (calendarIds 1-6 kept stable). The 15 mock trades' `paymentCalendarCode` values (previously invented composite strings like `'LON-USD'`/`'FRA-EUR'`/`'NY-USD'` that didn't match *any* real table) were remapped to the real single-calendar codes (`UK_BANK`/`ECB_TARGET`/`US_FEDERAL`) by currency/region.
  - **Deliberately left alone**: `period.pricingCalendarCode`/`settlementCalendarCode` and `pricing_rule.pricingCalendarCode` still use the old short-form codes (`'LON'`/`'NYC'`/`'CBOT'`) in `etrmHandlers.ts` and `PeriodsPage.tsx`'s hint text — these are a separate field not backed by any FK added in V91, so reconciling them was out of scope here; flagging so a future FK-integrity pass on `period`/`pricing_rule` doesn't rediscover this from scratch.
  - Verified: `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean in `etrm-frontend/`.

**V91 — FK integrity sweep batch 2 (location/pipeline/route/storage_facility/credit_term/payment_calendar/price_index code families), plus a latent V30 migration bug fix.** Re-verified V90's leftover "~12 findings" backlog item-by-item against the live SQL before touching anything (an Explore agent traced every column across all 90 migration files) — two of the original claims turned out stale (`trade_freight_detail` has no `location_code`-style column at all, it already uses FK'd `load_location_id`/`discharge_location_id`; `transport_route` is a fully schema-complete table, not merely stubbed). The other 8 sub-claims were confirmed and fixed in `91_location_pipeline_credit_term_fk_gaps.sql`: added 14 FK constraints — `trade_transport_agreement_detail`(load/discharge_location_code, pipeline_code, route_code), `trade_oil_detail`/`trade_lng_detail`/`trade_metals_detail`.title_transfer_location_code, `bolmo_agreement`/`trade_order`.delivery_location_code (all → `location.location_code`), `trade_storage_agreement_detail.storage_facility_code` → `storage_facility.facility_code`, `trade.credit_term_code` → `credit_term.term_code`, `trade.payment_calendar_code` → `holiday_calendar.calendar_code`, `trade_swap_detail.floating_index_code`/`floating_index2_code` → `price_index.index_code`. Also normalized 9 columns' VARCHAR lengths to exactly match their FK target (previously legal-but-inconsistent, e.g. VARCHAR(50) referencing a VARCHAR(30) unique key) — safe because none of `location`/`pipeline`/`transport_route`/`storage_facility` have real seed rows yet, so no truncation risk. **Found and fixed a second latent bug while tracing history**: `30_freight_trade_detail.sql` issued a bare, unguarded `CREATE TABLE dbo.trade_freight_detail` with a completely different (incompatible) column set from the one `09_trade_schema.sql` already created — on any real sequential migration run this would fail with "object already exists"; it never actually took effect (confirmed by `53_freight_demurrage_master_data_enhancement.sql`'s `IF NOT EXISTS ... ALTER TABLE ADD` assuming 09's column set is live). Fixed by wrapping V30's CREATE in `IF OBJECT_ID(...) IS NULL`, turning it into a documented no-op instead of dead/broken SQL — **note this edits a historical migration file's body, not just future ones; if V30 was ever already applied against a real Flyway-tracked DB, this will trigger a checksum mismatch requiring `flyway repair`.**

**Also surfaced, not yet fixed**: the frontend MSW mock trades' `creditTermCode` ('NET_30', 'NET_14', ...) and `paymentCalendarCode` ('LON-USD', 'FRA-EUR', ...) values don't match the real backend seed codes in `dbo.credit_term` ('OPEN_30', 'SECURED_LC', ...) / `dbo.holiday_calendar` ('UK_BANK', 'US_FEDERAL', ...) — a pre-existing mock/backend data-parity gap (frontend and backend seed data evolved independently), logged here since it would matter the moment trade data is ever persisted through the real backend instead of MSW.

**Still deferred**: `trade_order.period_code`/`incoterm_code` — both need a real design decision, not just an `ADD CONSTRAINT`, since their master tables (`period`, `incoterm`) use composite unique keys (`period_code`+`commodity_type`, `code`+`version_year`) that `trade_order` doesn't fully mirror.

**CRITICAL — antd `Form.Item` gotcha, cost a full debugging session this time: a custom wrapper component used as a `Form.Item`'s child MUST forward `value`/`onChange` (or `checked`/`onChange`) through to the real underlying control, or the form's internal store silently desyncs from what's on screen.** `Form.Item` injects those props onto its direct child; if that child is your own component (not a bare antd `<Input>`/`<Select>`/etc.) and it doesn't accept-and-spread them, `form.setFieldsValue()`/`initialValues` populate the store correctly (`form.getFieldsValue()` proves it) while the rendered input stays visibly empty — there's no error, no warning, just a silent visual desync. Hit this building `CustomFieldInput` in `TradeBlotter.tsx` (V89's custom-fields feature): it destructured only `{ dataType, selectOptions }` and dropped everything else, so the injected `value`/`onChange` never reached the real `<InputNumber>`/`<Input>`/`<Switch>`/`<Select>` it rendered. Fix: destructure `{ dataType, selectOptions, ...rest }` and spread `{...rest}` onto the real control. Any future custom Form.Item child in this codebase needs the same treatment.

**CRITICAL — verification checklist: two "basics" got missed twice in the same session before the user had to point them out. Check for both, every time, as part of testing/verification — not just "does it render / does tsc pass."**
1. **Every displayed ID-typed column resolves to a human name/label, not a raw numeric ID.** `RolesPage.tsx`'s "User Assignments" tab shipped showing a bare `User ID` column — it rendered fine, `tsc` was clean, headless Chrome screenshots even confirmed rows populated correctly, but nobody checked whether a human could actually read who the row was about. When reviewing or building any grid/table/detail view, explicitly ask: is there a raw `xxxId` on screen that should be a resolved name instead? Don't just confirm the screen renders without errors — look at what it says.
2. **Every column that looks like a foreign key has an actual `FOREIGN KEY` constraint, not just a comment claiming one.** `dbo.user_role_assignment.user_id` had `-- FK → system_user.user_id` as a comment (and `system_user` isn't even a real table — `dbo.app_user` is) with no real constraint, found only on a third pass over the exact same table. When reviewing or touching any `CREATE TABLE`, read the full constraint block, not just the columns being changed — check every `xxx_id` column against the `CONSTRAINT ... FOREIGN KEY` list, and check every FK-shaped comment actually names a real table.

Both gaps passed multiple review/rebuild/verification passes this session before surfacing — verification that only confirms "it works" (renders, compiles, screenshot looks populated) is not the same as verification that confirms "it's correct" (readable, referentially sound). Do the second kind.

**`etrm-backend` now compiles 100% cleanly (`mvn clean compile` — 0 errors)** — this was broken all session (and evidently for a while before it) until fixed in the entry below. If a future session sees compile errors again, don't assume they're "pre-existing and unrelated" without checking — that assumption was wrong twice this session already.

**CRITICAL — do not add Lombok to this backend, and don't reach for `--release`/`-source`/`-target` version flags on the compiler.** This environment's JDK (26.x, `java -version`) cannot run Lombok's annotation processor reliably under ANY explicit compiler version flag (`--release N`, or `-source N -target N`, for any N including N matching the JDK's own native version) — confirmed by direct `javac` reproduction, not guessed. Every other JPA entity in this backend already uses plain hand-written getters/setters (`AppUser`, `UserRole`, `UserRoleAssignment`, `RoleFunction`, …) — that's the established, working convention; match it, don't introduce Lombok. `java.version`/`maven.compiler.*` in `pom.xml` should stay untouched (currently 25, matching the JDK actually running this build) — Spring Boot's own `--release` derivation from `java.version` works fine as long as nothing in the compile depends on Lombok.

**CRITICAL — typecheck command:** `npx tsc --noEmit` in `etrm-frontend/` is **vacuous** — the root `tsconfig.json` is solution-style (`"files": []`, references only) and exits clean without checking anything. Always use `npx tsc -b --noEmit` (matches the real build script `tsc -b && vite build`). This bit us once this session — 24 real errors were hiding behind a false-clean `tsc --noEmit`.

**CRITICAL — there are two separate, non-interchangeable "legal entity" mock stores in the frontend.** `src/mocks/handlers.ts` exports `legalEntityStore` (seeded from `src/mocks/data.ts`: ACME-UK / ACME-US / GLOBEX-SG) — this is the **real, canonical, CRUD-backed** one, registered first in `browser.ts` so it's what `GET /legal-entities` actually returns and what `useLegalEntities()` shows everywhere. `src/mocks/etrmHandlers.ts` separately has an internal `legalEntitiesRef` shadow array (SETRM-LTD / SETRM-NL / SETRM-SG) used only to denormalize desk/book/trader seed rows — it is dead code as far as the `/legal-entities` endpoint goes (shadowed by registration order) and must never be used for anything a user can look up by legal entity id, or the displayed code won't match any real, editable record. Desk/book/trader `legalEntityCode` values were found stale (pointing at the shadow codes) this session and corrected to the real ones — if you add a new master-data entity that references `legalEntityId`, denormalize against `legalEntityStore`, not `legalEntitiesRef`.

**What changed this session, most recent first:**
- **Trade Blotter: Special Contract field shrunk + its length limit made unambiguous** ("reduce Special Contract length" / "hints or validation should [be] clear on length of the field") — the `specialReference` `Input` sat in a `Col span={24}`, stretching the box across the entire header width for what's normally a short reference string (maxLength 180, typical content ~40-90 chars); shrunk to `span={12}`. Since a narrower box could read as a shorter limit than it actually is, also moved the "Max 180 characters" note out of the hint tooltip's prose into the dedicated `format` slot of the `hint()` helper (renders as a distinct monospace "Format:" line) — combined with the input's existing always-visible `showCount` "0 / 180" counter, the 180-char ceiling is now unambiguous regardless of the field's on-screen width. Verified live: tooltip shows the format line distinctly; counter still visible at the new width.
- **Trade Blotter: second, more thorough field-alignment pass** ("field alignment still below par") — the first pass (below) fixed the two worst offenders but the user correctly flagged more remained. Used the Explore agent to systematically scan the entire ~2560-line file for the same root-cause pattern (a `<Row>` whose `<Col span>`s sum well under 24, leaving dead horizontal space — either one lonely field alone in its row, or two/three fields at a width sized for a since-removed sibling) rather than continuing to fix them one complaint at a time. Found and fixed 11 more instances: `OilSection`'s Title Transfer/Vessel/Pipeline row (conditional span `motType==='PIPELINE' ? 8 : 12`, was a fixed 8/8/8 that left a third of the row empty for TANKER/BARGE/TRUCK legs, i.e. most of them); `GasSection`'s Delivery Start/End/Gas Day Type row (6/6/6→18/24, widened to 8/8/8); `LngSection`'s lonely Price Basis field (span 12 alone → 24, matching how `Special Contract`/`Notes` already use full-width for a single field); `MetalsSection`'s lonely Title Transfer field (12→24); `BalmoSection`'s Running Avg/Final Settled Price pair (8/8→12/12); `RinSection`'s EPA Batch/EMTS Ref pair (8/8→12/12); `DeliveryFields`'s Risk Period (Risk Start/End, 8/8→12/12) and Delivery section (Incoterm/Delivery Location, conditional span `hasVesselPhysical ? 8 : 12` — was a fixed 8/8 that left a third of the row empty for GAS/POWER/FREIGHT/RINS/ENVIRONMENTAL and non-physical legs, i.e. most of them); the RFP Parameters card's Start/End Date pair (8/8→12/12); the Leg drawer's Leg Identity row (Leg Status/Template Leg, 8/8→12/12); and the Item drawer's lonely Product field (removed the unnecessary `Row/Col span={12}` wrapper entirely, matching the bare full-width `Form.Item` pattern already used by the very next field, `description`). Also merged the Leg (Order) drawer's Quantity & Pricing section's orphaned `settlementType` (previously alone in its own `Row` at `span={8}`, 16/24 blank) into the row above, redistributing all 5 fields (Quantity/UoM/Price/Currency/Settlement) across one row at 5/4/5/5/5. Verified live via Playwright: opened the Oil leg on TRD-2026-00001 (vessel/physical, MOT=TANKER — confirmed Title Transfer/Vessel now fill their row, Risk Period and the merged Quantity & Pricing row both fill cleanly) and the Power leg on TRD-2026-00005 (financial, non-vessel — confirmed Incoterm/Delivery Location now correctly widen to fill the row when Origin Country doesn't apply). `tsc -b --noEmit` clean throughout.
- **Trade Blotter: made "add legs/costs/etc for a new trade" actually discoverable** ("not just the trade lets allow to add other details legs costs etc for new trade") — the capability already existed technically (`submitTrade()` always calls `setSelectedTradeId(saved.tradeId)` regardless of `closeAfter`, so clicking the header's plain "Save" button during creation already unlocks the Delivery Legs/Items/Secondary Costs/Custom Fields/Specifications/Assay tabs, confirmed live via Playwright — a real trade row must exist first since legs/costs/items are separate FK-linked tables, not part of the trade form submit), but it was undiscoverable: the only signal was a small passive `Alert` ("Save the trade first...") sitting below a long, multi-section form, with the actual "Save" button all the way back up in the title bar — easy to miss, and easy to confuse with the adjacent "Create & Close" button which does the opposite (saves and hides the workspace). Fixed by turning that Alert into an actionable inline prompt with its own "Save Trade to Continue" primary button (calls the same `submitTrade(false)`) right where the sub-entity tabs will appear — so the two-step "fill header → save → tabs unlock in place" flow is now a single obvious action instead of a scavenger hunt. Verified live end-to-end: New Trade → fill required fields (counterparty/date/trader) → click "Save Trade to Continue" → all 6 tabs unlock in place with the trade's real reference (e.g. `TRD-2026-00016`) → Add Leg opens a fully-populated commodity-specific leg drawer immediately, no page reload or re-navigation needed.
- **Trade Blotter header/field alignment fix** ("still clumsy, fields are everywhere... check alignment of the fields width and length of the fields - some are really bad") — visually audited the workspace via Playwright screenshots in view/edit/create modes and found the layout bugs were real, not the whole page: (1) the Commodity Type / Direction / Term Type row (`TradeBlotter.tsx` ~line 1951) used column spans (14/4/6) sized for the Segmented pickers shown only while **creating** a new trade; once a trade exists those two fields collapse into small Tags but the wide columns stayed, leaving a large dead gap between the Tag and the next field. Fixed by making the spans conditional on `selectedTrade` (14/4/6 unchanged for create-mode Segmented; even 8/8/8 thirds for existing-trade Tag mode). While there, also fixed a visual inconsistency this exposed: `direction` always rendered as a full-width `<Select>` (just disabled/grayed in view mode) sitting next to two compact Tags — added a `watchedDirection` watch and now render it as a matching colored `Tag` (reusing the existing `DIRECTION_COLOR` map already used in the grid and title bar) whenever purely viewing (`selectedTrade && !tradeOpen`), reverting to the real `<Select>` during actual create/edit. (2) The "Deal Classification" Collapse section's Instrument Type field sat in a `Col span={16}` (very wide for a single dropdown) next to a `Col span={8}` that only ever shows an `Alert` for SWAP/OPTION/STORAGE/TRANSPORT instrument types — for the common case (PHYSICAL, or no selection yet) that entire right two-thirds of the row was permanently blank. Replaced the Row/Col with a flex layout: Instrument Type gets a fixed, content-appropriate `width: 380`, and the (now single, deduped) conditional `Alert` sits inline and only occupies space when actually rendered. Verified both cases live (no alert for PHYSICAL; alert renders inline immediately next to the field for e.g. Swap — Fixed/Float) — no more reserved empty column. Scanned the rest of the file (Credit & Legal, Contract Controls, Leg Identity/Entity & Book/Broker/Tolerance in the Order drawer, Secondary Costs tab) for the same "oversized column reserved for rarely-shown content" pattern — those were already reasonably balanced (spans sum sensibly to actual content, e.g. `12/12`, `10/5/4/5`, `6/6/6/6`), so left unchanged rather than churning working layout. Verified: `tsc -b --noEmit` clean; Playwright screenshots confirmed the fix in view mode (compact aligned tags, no gap), edit mode (Direction correctly reverts to an editable dropdown), and create mode (Segmented pickers unaffected, still full-width and usable).
- **Master Data Hub naming/grouping pass** ("rename the master data items in ui if required similar for static data items as well... best industry standards for top companies") — audited `MasterDataHub.tsx`'s ~90 card labels against two sources of truth: (a) real ETRM/CTRM industry terminology (Endur/Allegro-style — already well-matched from prior sessions' research, e.g. `Book`/`Broker`/`Legal Entity`/`Incoterms`/`Worldscale`/D-codes/REMIT-EMIR-CFTC are all correct as-is, no churn needed there), and (b) internal consistency against `dbo.master_data_table_registry` — the backend table that actually drives the **Static Data (Tier 2)** hub's (`Tier2HomePage.tsx`) card labels via `useRegisteredTables()`. Found and fixed real drift where the Hub's copy of a label had gone stale vs. the registry's canonical `display_name` (both should say the same thing since a Hub card is just a shortcut into that same page): `demurrage_dispatch_rate` ("Demurrage & Dispatch" → **"Demurrage & Dispatch Rates"**), `regulatory_report_type` ("Report Types" → **"Regulatory Report Types"**, was ambiguous next to `credit_limit_type`/`environmental_product_type` etc. all also called "... Types"). Also fixed inconsistent abbreviation: `cp_commercial_terms`/`cp_gtc_agreement` labels said "CP Commercial Terms"/"CP GTC Agreements" while every sibling card in the same group spells out "Counterparty" — renamed to **"Counterparty Commercial Terms"**/**"Counterparty GTC Agreements"**. Renamed the **"Trade Operations"** group (only ever held 3 items: `bolmo_agreement`/`nomination`/`delivery_instruction`, all physical-delivery-execution concepts, not trade capture) to **"Physical Operations"** — clearer and matches the common ETRM/CTRM term for this domain (distinct from trade capture and from "Logistics & Delivery" master data) — and reordered the `GROUPS` array so it sits between `Contract & Legal` and `Logistics & Delivery` (Products → Contract → Physical Ops → Logistics → Freight reads as a coherent execution pipeline instead of being sandwiched between Products & Markets and Contract & Legal). No DB/registry changes needed — the registry's own `display_name` values were already correct; only the Hub's stale copies needed fixing. `Tier2HomePage.tsx`'s `GROUP_ORDER` array needed no change (it never listed "Trade Operations" — those 3 tables are dedicated-page entities, not generic `/static-data/*` rows). Verified: `tsc -b --noEmit` clean; Playwright against the live dev server (signed in via the mock `dev.admin` button) confirmed all 6 renames render and the old "Trade Operations" string is gone.
