Master-data audit's other findings: registering the `product_spec_template`/`spec_parameter`/`spec_override` group and `bank_account` (both already have `live: false` Hub placeholders) generically ahead of bespoke pages; and — genuinely absent, not just unregistered — UN/LOCODE port codes (the mock already invents `unlocode` fields per location but `dbo.location` has no such column), HS/Harmonized Tariff codes (nothing to calculate the app's own `CUSTOMS_DUTY` trade-cost type against), ASTM D1250/API MPMS Ch.11.1 volume correction factor tables (temperature/pressure-dependent, vs. today's flat `uom_conversion` factors), a real denied-party/sanctions entity list (today only a country-level flag exists), and counterparty industry classification (NAICS/SIC/GICS, for concentration-risk reporting). UI-hint audit's other ~5 candidates not yet added: `railcars` `dotClass`/`aarClass`, `pipeline-cycles` nomination/confirmation/scheduling deadline trio, `pipeline-segments.tariffZone`.
  - Verified: `tsc -b --noEmit` clean after all edits.
- **V89 — Legal Entity/Book/Broker moved from trade header to leg (`trade_order`) level, Book/Broker gained commodity scoping, and a governed Custom Fields registry replaced the "move Deal Classification fields to leg level" ask.** User asked to move Entity & Book/Broker (and impliedly other header sections) to leg level, requested research into how Endur/Aspect model this, commodity-correct implementation, and a client-extensible custom-fields section — explicitly asking to fix whatever's wrong with Endur/OpenLink's own version of that last one.
  - **Researched + confirmed via `AskUserQuestion` before touching schema**: real ETRM practice keeps Legal Entity at deal-header level (one contracting entity per deal) but Broker and Book **do** legitimately vary per leg (a multi-leg strip can be executed via different IDBs on different days, and legs can post to different books). User's explicit choice was still the maximal one — all three (Legal Entity, Book, Broker) move to leg level, **independent per leg with no fallback/inheritance from the trade** (deliberately more data entry than defaulting, per user's pick).
  - **V89 (both copies, byte-identical)**: added `legal_entity_id`/`book_id`/`broker_id`/`broker_fee_type`/`broker_fee`/`broker_fee_currency_code` to `dbo.trade_order` (backfilled from the parent `trade` row, then `legal_entity_id`/`book_id` set `NOT NULL`, FKs added); dropped the same six columns (+ their FKs/index) from `dbo.trade`. Added `dbo.broker.commodity_type` (nullable — `NULL` = generalist IDB offered for every commodity, matches how `dbo.unit_of_measure`/`dbo.book` already model cross-commodity rows). New governed **Custom Fields registry**: `dbo.custom_field_definition` (field name, `data_type` CHECK TEXT/NUMBER/DATE/BOOLEAN/SELECT, `applies_to` CHECK TRADE/LEG, optional `commodity_type` scope, `select_options` JSON for SELECT), plus `dbo.trade_custom_field_value` / `dbo.trade_order_custom_field_value` (one row per (trade-or-order, definition), `UNIQUE` constraint enforces upsert semantics) — deliberately **two separate value tables**, not one polymorphic table, matching the same choice already made for `trade_cost`/`trade_order_cost` in V88.
  - **Why a governed registry, not Endur/OpenLink's "User Defined Fields"**: researched Endur's own docs/Capco's "Implementation Pitfalls" — UDFs there are untyped, single-value, no validation, and (per Endur's own governance guidance) need active "governance and controls" specifically *because* nothing stops sprawl or enforces consistency. Here, an admin defines each field once (name/type/scope/commodity) via a **Manage Custom Fields modal** (`ManageCustomFieldsModal` — add + activate/deactivate, no code required), and every trade/leg gets a typed, validated input for each active definition instead of a free-text box. Deliberately did *not* wire this into the generic Tier2/`master_data_table_registry` col()-schema machinery — that system's per-column schema declarations would have added real complexity for no benefit here; a small bespoke modal was simpler and sufficient.
  - **`TradeBlotter.tsx`**: removed the "Entity & Book" and "Broker" Collapse sections from the Trade Details tab entirely; added them to the Leg (Order) Drawer instead, right after Leg Identity — `legalEntityOpts` (unfiltered, entities aren't commodity-scoped), `bookOptionsFor(commodityType)` (dbo.commodity_type ids 1–9 line up 1:1 with `COMMODITY_TYPES_TRADE`'s array order, so filtering is a simple index+1 lookup — no resolver table needed), `brokerOptionsFor(commodityType)` (Broker.commodityType is a direct string match, `null` = shown for every commodity). New **Custom Fields** tab in the trade workspace, styled like Secondary Costs (two Collapse sections: Trade-Level Fields / Leg Fields with the same leg-selector), each backed by a new `CustomFieldsForm` that renders one input per active definition and a single "Save Custom Fields" button.
  - **Data layer**: `TradeOrder`/`TradeOrderInput` gained the six moved fields (removed from `Trade`/`TradeInput`); `Broker.commodityType` added; new `CustomFieldDefinition(Input)`, `TradeCustomFieldValue(Input)`, `TradeOrderCustomFieldValue(Input)` types, `CUSTOM_FIELD_DATA_TYPES`/`CUSTOM_FIELD_APPLIES_TO` consts. `api.ts`/`hooks.ts` got matching fetch/save/delete functions and hooks (`useCustomFieldDefinitions`, `useSaveCustomFieldDefinition`, `useTradeCustomFieldValues`/`useSaveTradeCustomFieldValue`, `useLegCustomFieldValues`/`useSaveLegCustomFieldValue`) mirroring the existing Items/Costs hook pattern, with the two value-save functions using **upsert semantics** (POST always; the mock handler finds-or-creates by (tradeId-or-orderId, definitionId) since a value row is 1:1 with its definition).
  - **MSW mock reshaping (`etrmHandlers.ts`)**: all 15 seed trades' `bookId`/`bookCode`/`legalEntityId`/`legalEntityName`/`brokerId`/`brokerCode`/`brokerName`/`brokerFeeType`/`brokerFee`/`brokerFeeCurrencyCode` fields extracted programmatically (Python regex pass, not hand-edited — 17 order rows across 15 trades) and moved onto each trade's order row(s); `denormalizeTrade()` split into a slimmer version (counterparty/trader only) plus a new `denormalizeOrder()` handling the moved fields, wired into the `/trade-orders` POST/PUT handlers. **Caught and fixed a self-inflicted regex bug during this pass**: an overly broad find/replace meant to add `commodityType` to the 7 `brokersStore` rows also matched `brokerCode`/`brokerName` pairs inside 8 unrelated `broker_fee_agreement` seed rows (creating duplicate `commodityType` keys) and 12 `tradeOrdersStore` rows (adding a bogus field that doesn't exist on `TradeOrder`) — caught by inspecting the diff before running `tsc`, fixed with a second targeted regex scoped to lines containing `agreementId:`/`orderId:`. Added `customFieldDefinitionStore`/`tradeCustomFieldValueStore`/`legCustomFieldValueStore` with 4 demo definitions (one per data type: ESG Score/NUMBER/TRADE, Vessel Class/SELECT/LEG/OIL-only, Broker Desk/TEXT/LEG, Middle Office Reviewed/BOOLEAN/TRADE) and matching demo values against trade 1/order 1, plus GET/POST/PUT/DELETE handlers for all three new endpoint groups.
  - **Real bug found and fixed during verification (see the new antd `Form.Item` CRITICAL note above)**: the Custom Fields tab's inputs rendered empty despite `form.getFieldsValue()` proving the store held the right data — root cause was `CustomFieldInput` (the per-data-type input picker) not forwarding the `value`/`onChange` Form.Item injects onto custom wrapper components. Fixed by spreading `...rest` onto the real control.
  - Verified: `tsc -b --noEmit` clean; Playwright against the actual running dev server (not just a throwaway instance) — Leg Drawer for order 1 shows Entity & Book (Legal Entity="ACME-UK...", Book="CRUDE-PROP...") and Broker sections with all other leg fields (Oil Cargo Details, Price Adjustments, etc.) intact; Custom Fields tab shows all 4 seeded values correctly pre-filled after the Form.Item fix, Manage Custom Fields modal lists all 4 definitions with working Active toggles and an Add Field form.
- **V88 + Trade Blotter redesigned into a single on-page workspace (no more Trade Drawer), with new Secondary Costs and Assay capture.** User asked for: the 9 key header fields (CP, contract date, CIN, special contract, trade status, trade type, trader, execution date, term type) always visible; everything else in clearly separated sections on the *same page*; Items visible without the extra leg-click; and new expandable sections for secondary costs (trade- and leg-level) plus physical-only Specifications/Assay tabs. Confirmed with user via AskUserQuestion: full on-page workspace (option A) and **two separate cost lists** (not one polymorphic table).
  - **V88 (both copies, byte-identical)**: `dbo.trade_cost` (trade-level, FK->trade CASCADE), `dbo.trade_order_cost` (leg-level, FK->trade_order CASCADE) — both with CHECK-constrained `cost_type` (FREIGHT/INSURANCE/STORAGE/PORT_DUES/CUSTOMS_DUTY/INSPECTION_SURVEY/BANK_CHARGES/LEGAL_DOCUMENTATION/AGENCY_FEES/OTHER), `is_estimated` BIT, real currency FK from day one (V87 pattern); and `dbo.trade_order_assay_result` — actual quality results per physical leg, FK-> `product_spec_value(spec_value_id)` (that one FK already carries template+parameter+bounds, so no duplicated template/parameter columns), `sample_point` CHECK (LOAD/DISCHARGE/SHORE_TANK/OTHER). Pass/fail vs. bounds is computed client-side at render. Shape mirrors `trade_order_price_adjustment` (V46) — small fixed enums stay CHECK constraints, not lookup_category. Seeded demo rows against trade 1 / order 1, reusing spec_value_id 1/2 (Brent API gravity + sulphur, matching the order's own oilDetail values).   - **`TradeBlotter.tsx` restructure**: Trade Drawer deleted entirely. New workspace `Card` below the trades grid (shown when a trade is selected or New Trade clicked): pinned header strip with the 9 fields + commodity/direction as live `Form.Item`s on the same always-mounted `tradeForm` (fields `disabled` in view mode, "Edit Trade" toggles edit; `useFormDraft`/`submitTrade` logic unchanged, only where fields render moved); Details as `<Collapse>` sections (Deal Classification + RFP, Entity & Book, Broker, Credit & Legal, Contract Controls, Notes — all `forceRender: true` so hidden panels' values survive submit); below the Form, `<Tabs>` for Delivery Legs (grid + Add Leg), Items (always visible, leg-selector Select defaulting to first leg via a new auto-select effect), Secondary Costs (two Collapse lists: `TradeCostsSection` + `LegCostsSection` with the shared leg selector; rows persist immediately per-row like Items, not on form submit), and — physical trades only, gated on the resolved trade-type label — Specifications (read-only, reuses `useProductSpecTemplates`/`useSpecValues` from products feature, grouped by the legs' distinct products) and Assay/Quality (`AssayResultsSection`: actuals vs. spec bounds with computed Within Spec/Out of Spec tags). Tabs sit *outside* the `<Form>` element on purpose — avoids nested `<form>` DOM (CostsEditor/Assay have their own inline Forms) and keeps their buttons enabled while the trade form is view-mode disabled. New-trade mode shows an Alert in place of the tabs until first save. Leg (Order) and Item drawers intentionally unchanged.
  - **Data layer**: `TradeCost`/`TradeOrderCost`/`TradeAssayResult` (+Inputs, `TRADE_COST_TYPES`) in `types.ts`; fetch/create/update/delete for `/trade-costs`, `/trade-order-costs`, `/trade-order-assay-results` in `api.ts`; `useTradeCosts`/`useLegCosts`/`useAssayResults` (+save/delete) in `hooks.ts` mirroring the Items hooks; MSW stores/handlers/seeds in `etrmHandlers.ts` (assay GET/POST/PUT join spec bounds via `joinAssayResult` against `productSpecValueStore`).
  - **Fixed while verifying (the §0 "look at what's displayed" checklist caught it)**: the blotter's Counterparty/Legal Entity selects rendered "undefined — undefined" — `/counterparties` and `/legal-entities` are actually served by the tier1 handlers (registered before `etrmHandlers` in `browser.ts`), whose rows are `cpCode`/`legalName` and `entityCode`/`entityName`, not the `counterpartyCode`/`name` shape declared in `features/trade/api.ts`. Fixed the two TradeBlotter labels to read the real fields. **Surfaced, not fixed (pre-existing, app-wide)**: ~12 other pages (`credit/*`, `counterparties/*`, `operations/*` etc.) cast `useCounterparties()`/`useLegalEntities()` results to the same stale `counterpartyCode`/`name` shape and so presumably render the same "undefined" labels — the stale interfaces in `features/trade/api.ts` are kept (with a warning comment) to avoid a mass ripple; fix consumers to `cpCode`/`legalName` as they're touched. Related pre-existing mismatch: trades seed references counterpartyId up to 10 but the real tier1 `cpStore` has only 3 CPs, so the trade rows' denormalized names come from `etrmHandlers`' shadow array while the picker only offers 3 real rows.
  - Verified: `tsc -b --noEmit` clean; Playwright drive of the real app — trade 1 (physical): header strip values resolved (CIN via `inputValue`, counterparty "SHELLTR — Shell Trading International Ltd"), all Collapse panels present, legs/items/costs/specs/assay tabs populated from seeds, added a trade-level cost through the UI and it persisted, assay shows correct Within Spec badges; trade 2 (financial): Specifications/Assay correctly hidden; New Trade → create flow works end-to-end (created TRD-2026-00016, workspace opens with tabs); Add Leg drawer still opens. Only console noise is the known pre-existing antd deprecation warnings.
  - **Follow-up fix, same session: Commodity Type / Term Type were still showing the full `Segmented` picker (all 9 commodity options) for existing trades.** First pass only swapped `Segmented`→`Tag` when `!tradeOpen` (pure view), so clicking "Edit Trade" on an *existing* trade brought the full picker straight back — user correctly reported "still not working" against this. Root cause of the miss: gating on `tradeOpen`/`editingTrade` conflates "is the form editable" with "does this trade already exist"; `editingTrade` in particular is only set inside `openEditTrade()`, so it's still `null` during plain row-selection view too. Real fix: gate on `selectedTrade` (an existing, persisted trade) instead — `!selectedTrade` shows the editable picker (new-trade creation only), any existing trade shows a fixed, non-interactive `Tag` in **both** view and edit mode, with a hint explaining it's locked because legs/products (Commodity Type) and leg-generation (Term Type) already depend on it. Verified against the user's actual running dev server (`localhost:5173`, not just my own throwaway instance) in all three states: view/edit of an existing trade → tag only; New Trade → picker still works.
- **Backend API audit for V87, prompted by the user asking "all api logic also changed for same" — found and fixed one real gap.** Delegated a research pass (not guessed) over every one of the ~37 tables V87 touched: only `counterparty` and `legal_entity` (from V86) have full bespoke Java CRUD modules; `credit_term`/`commodity_grade_standard`/`transport_operator`/`balancing_authority`/`metal_brand` are served through the generic `ReferenceDataController` (derives FK/CHECK metadata from SQL catalogs at request time — already covers the new FKs with zero Java changes, the established Tier 2 pattern); every other touched table (`trader`, `book`, `trade_order`, `trade_item`, `margin_agreement`, `credit_limit`, `letter_of_credit`, `gtc`, `broker`, etc.) has **no Java backend code at all** — mock-only in this dev environment, so there's no API logic to update yet. `GlobalExceptionHandler` already had a `DataIntegrityViolationException` → clean `409 CONFLICT` `ProblemDetail` handler (no stack-trace leak) — confirmed sufficient as-is, no change needed for single-row create/update paths.
  - **The one real gap**: `LegalEntityService.bulkCreate()` only guarded against duplicate `entity_code` per row; a bad `jurisdiction`/`incorporation_country`/`base_currency` value in one row of a bulk Excel upload would now hit the new V87 FKs, throw `DataIntegrityViolationException` mid-`@Transactional` batch, and roll back the *entire* batch — silently breaking the method's own documented promise ("a partial batch still commits everything that DID pass"). Root cause: a plain `try/catch` around `repository.save()` isn't sufficient in JPA/Hibernate — once a flush throws, the shared persistence context/transaction is left rollback-only, so every row after the bad one would fail too even if valid.
  - **Fix**: new `LegalEntityRowInserter` (`legalentity/LegalEntityRowInserter.java`), a separate `@Service` with a `@Transactional(propagation = REQUIRES_NEW)` `insert()` method — each bulk row now commits (or rolls back) in its own independent transaction. `LegalEntityService.bulkCreate()` calls it per row inside a `try/catch (DataIntegrityViolationException)`, rejecting just that row with a reason (same pattern as the existing duplicate-code rejection) instead of losing the whole batch.
  - Verified via `mvn -q -o compile` (clean, exit 0 — no pre-existing compile errors surfaced in this pass, contrary to the `verify` skill's older note about `CounterpartyController`/`ReferenceDataController`; worth re-checking that skill note next time it's consulted).
- **V87 — full currency/country FK sweep, closing out every gap V86's audit had flagged-but-not-fixed.** User said "do it now" after reviewing the V86 flag list. This is the full remediation of `[[project_currency_country_fk_gap]]`-class findings — after this entry, that memory file is stale and should be treated as historical, not current state.
  - **28 currency-code columns** (`CHAR(3)`/`VARCHAR(3)`/`VARCHAR(5)`/`NCHAR(3)`, storing an ISO code directly rather than a `currency_id` surrogate) got a real FK -> `dbo.currency(currency_code)`, matching the pattern `legal_entity.base_currency` already had: `trader.limit_currency`, `book.base_currency`, `counterparty.credit_limit_currency`, `cp_legal_entity_link.limit_currency`, `credit_term.margin_call_currency`, `trade.broker_fee_currency_code` (not `broker` — corrected a wrong table guess from the V86 audit), `broker_fee_agreement.fee_currency_code`, all 4 currency columns on `margin_agreement`, `credit_limit.limit_currency`, `letter_of_credit.lc_currency`, `trade_order.currency_code`, `trade_item.currency_code`, `settlement_price.tick_currency`, `bolmo_agreement.currency_code`, `balmo_product.tick_currency`, `trader_commodity_limit.limit_currency`, `trade_swap_detail.fixed_currency_code`, `trade_option_detail`'s strike/premium currency, `trade_storage_agreement_detail.tariff_currency_code`, `trade_transport_agreement_detail.freight_currency_code`, `trade_order.demurrage_currency`, `trade_order_price_adjustment.adjustment_currency`, `gl_account.currency_code`, `commodity_grade_standard.adjustment_currency_code`.
  - **20 country-code columns** (`CHAR(2)`) got a real FK -> `dbo.country(country_code)` (the table V86 created): `holiday_calendar`, `address`, `location`, `pipeline`, `exchange`, `market`, `transport_operator`, `vessel` (both `flag_country` and `build_country`), `truck`, `railcar`, `balancing_authority`, `metal_brand.country_of_origin`, `broker.country_code`, `credit_limit.cp_country_code`, `trade_order.origin_country_code`, `trade_storage_agreement_detail.storage_country_code`, `counterparty.jurisdiction`, `tax_registration.jurisdiction`, `gtc.jurisdiction` — the last 3 weren't in the original V86 flag list, found during this pass's own re-audit.
  - **Deliberately excluded, and this is a real distinction, not a miss**: `emission_scheme.jurisdiction` is `NVARCHAR(200)` free text (e.g. 'European Union', 'California'), NOT a `CHAR(2)` code — emission trading schemes routinely span multiple countries or are sub-national. Forcing it into a country picker would have been a regression, not a fix. Don't "complete" this one later without re-checking this reasoning.
  - **Seed-data compatibility, checked before every ADD CONSTRAINT**: `dbo.country` needed 3 more rows beyond V86's 18 — `CL` (Chile, used by `metal_brand`'s Codelco row and `trade_order`'s LME copper demo order), `PL` (Poland, `metal_brand`'s KGHM row), `NG` (Nigeria — not in any seed row, but named as a live example in `TradeBlotter.tsx`'s origin-country hint text, added so that hint doesn't start silently lying once the field becomes a real picker). All 3 also added to the frontend's `countriesStore` mock. Everything else across all ~48 touched tables had zero seed rows in SQL — the app's demo data mostly lives only in the frontend MSW mock — so those FKs are pure forward-guards with no backfill risk.
  - **Frontend, matching pattern used for Legal Entity (V86)** — free-text `<Input>` → searchable `<Select>` sourced from `useCountries()`/`useCurrencies()`, for: `CounterpartyFormPage.tsx` (`jurisdiction`, `creditLimitCurrency`), `TaxRegistrationsSection.tsx` (`jurisdiction`), `AddressesSection.tsx` (`countryCode`), `BrokersPage.tsx` (`countryCode`), `GtcsPage.tsx` (`jurisdiction` — also fixed a mislabeled hint that said "ISO 3166-2" and a placeholder of "England & Wales" when the real column is `CHAR(2)`; `governingLaw` is the separate free-text field that already correctly captures "English Law"/"New York Law"), `TradeBlotter.tsx` (`originCountryCode` on the physical-leg section, `agriDetail.originCountry` inside `AgriSection`).
  - **Found and fixed one more real bug while wiring Counterparty**: `CounterpartyFormPage.tsx`'s `defaultCurrencyId` Select, and `BankAccountsSection.tsx`/`GuaranteeTable.tsx`/`GuaranteeFormDrawer.tsx`'s currency pickers, were all sourced from a hardcoded `CURRENCY_LOOKUP` stopgap array in `staticLookups.ts` — explicitly self-documented in a comment as temporary with ids that "will NOT match whatever the real currency table assigns." Replaced all 4 call sites with the real `useCurrencies()` hook and deleted `CURRENCY_LOOKUP` (kept `CREDIT_RATING_LOOKUP` in the same file — genuinely still a stopgap, different concern, not touched).
  - **Mock data correction found while fixing GTCS**: the frontend's 6 seeded `gtc` rows had `jurisdiction` values of `'England & Wales'`, `'New York'`, `'Texas'` — not ISO2 codes at all, even though the real DB column is `CHAR(2)`. Once `jurisdiction` became a real country `<Select>`, these would have been unselectable. Corrected to `'GB'`/`'US'`/`'US'` — no information lost, since `governingLaw` already separately captures the "New York Law"/"Texas Law" distinction these values were really encoding.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean throughout) and headless Chrome across every touched bespoke page: Counterparty (jurisdiction → "GB — United Kingdom", credit currency + default currency both → real Selects with correct seeded values), Brokers (ICAP → "GB — United Kingdom"), GTCS (→ "GB — United Kingdom"), Trade Blotter's TRD-2026-00008 agri order (both origin-country fields → "FR — France", matching seed). SQL verified structurally (full re-read, byte-diffed both migration copies) — no live SQL Server in this environment to actually run Flyway against.
- **V86 — `dbo.country` created + `legal_entity.jurisdiction`/`incorporation_country` FK'd to it, after a full currency/country field audit found the concept didn't exist in SQL at all.** User asked to review every currency/country field across master data and user data for real FK linkage (example given: Legal Entity's Base Currency/Incorporation Country/Jurisdiction), then scoped the fix to Legal Entity only.
  - **Audit findings** (full sweep across all 85 prior migrations + frontend): `legal_entity.base_currency` already had a real FK to `dbo.currency(currency_code)` — fine. But **no `dbo.country` table exists anywhere in SQL, and no `Country` JPA entity exists in the backend** — `useCountries()`/`CountriesPage.tsx`/the `/countries` endpoint the frontend already has (with region/phoneCode/fatfStatus/sanctionStatus) is served purely by an MSW mock (`countriesStore` in `etrmHandlers.ts`), never backed by a real table. Every country/jurisdiction-shaped column across the schema (~15+: `legal_entity.jurisdiction`/`incorporation_country`, `counterparty.jurisdiction`/`cp_country_code`, `trade_order.origin_country_code`, `vessel.flag_country`, `metal_brand.country_of_origin`, etc.) is a bare unvalidated `CHAR(2)`. Separately, ~24 `CHAR(3)`/`VARCHAR(3)`/`NCHAR(3)` currency-code columns (`trader.limit_currency`, `book.base_currency`, `counterparty.credit_limit_currency`, all 6 in `35_credit_margin_lc.sql`, the 5 instrument-detail currency columns in `44_instrument_types...sql`, etc.) also have zero FK/CHECK, alongside the ~30 `currency_id INT` columns that ARE properly FK'd. **Both of these broader gaps are flagged, not fixed — out of the scope the user chose.**
  - **Frontend confirmed the same gap on the exact page the user named**: `LegalEntityFormDrawer.tsx` rendered `jurisdiction`/`incorporationCountry`/`baseCurrency` all as free-text `<Input>` (maxLength 2/2/3, uppercase CSS) — `baseCurrency` had a real DB FK the whole time but the form never called the existing `useCurrencies()` hook. Same free-text pattern also found (not fixed, flagged) in Counterparty/Brokers/GTCS/Emission Schemes/Trade Blotter's `originCountry(Code)`, and Counterparty's `defaultCurrencyId` Select was found sourced from a hardcoded stopgap array in `staticLookups.ts` explicitly commented "TEMPORARY... ids will NOT match the real table."
  - **V86 fix**: `database/86_legal_entity_country_fk.sql` (+ byte-identical `V86__legal_entity_country_fk.sql`) creates `dbo.country` (`country_id` surrogate PK, `country_code CHAR(2)` UNIQUE natural key — same dual-key shape as `dbo.currency` — plus `region`/`phone_code`/`fatf_status`/`sanction_status` to match the frontend's already-committed `Country` type), seeded with the exact same 18 rows already used by the frontend mock (reused, not reinvented). `legal_entity.jurisdiction`/`incorporation_country` get real `FOREIGN KEY ... REFERENCES dbo.country(country_code)` — direct `ADD CONSTRAINT`, no staging column needed since no `legal_entity` rows are seeded in SQL at all (data only ever lived in the frontend mock). `dbo.country` is deliberately **not** registered in `master_data_table_registry` / given a `MasterDataHub.tsx` card this pass — that's a separate Tier 2 discoverability task, not required for the Legal Entity FK fix (would need both together or neither, per the V80 lesson about registered-but-invisible tables).
  - **Frontend**: `LegalEntityFormDrawer.tsx`'s three fields converted from free-text `<Input>` to searchable `<Select>` (`"GB — United Kingdom"` / `"USD — US Dollar"` style labels) sourced from the real `useCountries()`/`useCurrencies()` hooks. `types.ts` comments updated to note the FK.

- **Shared field-validation framework built — `components/smart/fieldValidation.ts` (frontend) + `com.etrm.system.common.FieldValidation` (backend) — full design in §5 "Field-level input validation."** User asked for numbers-only/text-only/no-dangerous-special-chars validation across every GUI field and API endpoint, app-wide. Built as one shared module each side (not duplicated per-page), wired into the generic Tier 2 system (`ReferenceDataTable.tsx` + `ReferenceDataCrudService`, covering ~100+ tables from one call site), and piloted on one bespoke page (`DeskFormDrawer.tsx`) to prove it works wired into a hand-written form. **Every other bespoke feature page still needs this wired in — read §5 before adding or touching any form.** Also: `lookup_category` codes (V85, entry below) standardized to `UPPER_SNAKE_CASE` — a loose end from earlier in the session, finally closed out.
- **V85 — `dbo.lookup_category`: `lookup_value.category` upgraded from a free-text VARCHAR to a real FK, after researching how other ETRM providers avoid the OTLT (One True Lookup Table) anti-pattern. Then, in the same migration, `book_type` and `commodity_type` both got pulled entirely out of the generic system — one onto a real pre-existing dedicated table, one onto a brand-new one.**
  - **The ask, and the research behind it**: user wanted a review of how other ETRM platforms handle category/lookup reference data before anything got built. Landed on the two-tier `reference_type`/`reference_value` pattern used by mature platforms (Endur/Allegro-style): a `lookup_category` master table (so the category axis is itself managed, not a typo-able string) plus the existing flat `lookup_value` table now properly FK'd to it. Dedicated tables (V17 shape) remain the right call whenever a value drives real code logic. V82/V83/V84's 13 dedicated tables are explicitly, completely untouched by this — user was emphatic on this point after an earlier draft plan of mine tried to fold some of them into `lookup_value` and got immediately, correctly rejected ("why are you removing pure dedicated tables?").
  - **`database/85_lookup_category.sql`** (byte-identical backend copy, steps in file order):
    - **Step 0a — `book_type`**: while reviewing the binding list with the user, found a real, pre-existing dedicated `dbo.book_type` table (V17) sitting orphaned — `book.book_type` had been wired to `lookup_value` instead back in V55, and V78's own header comment already flagged this as the one exception among V17's 13 pairs (the other 12 got cut over to their dedicated tables properly). Redirected `book.book_type` onto the real `dbo.book_type` table via the standard staging-column pattern (including dropping `df_book_book_type`, a DEFAULT constraint V55 had left on the column that would otherwise block the `DROP COLUMN`), then deleted the now-orphaned `book_type` `lookup_value` rows before the `lookup_category` backfill runs, so `book_type` never becomes a category at all.
    - **Step 0b — `commodity_type`**: user then asked why `commodity_type` (11 consuming tables: `desk`, `book`, `gl_account`, `period`, `period_mapping`, `unit_of_measure`, `location_type`, `trader_commodity_limit`, `freight_rate_index`, `laytime_term_template`, `demurrage_dispatch_rate`) wasn't also pulled out the same way, reversing V58's prior explicit decision to leave it in `lookup_value` ("heavy reuse across many tables" turned out not to be the deciding factor for the user — a dedicated table was preferred regardless). Built a new `dbo.commodity_type` table (V17 shape, 11 rows: OIL/GAS/POWER/LNG/AGRICULTURAL/METALS/FREIGHT/RINS/ENVIRONMENTAL/MULTI/OTHER, same order/ids `lookup_value` used) and redirected all 11 consuming columns onto it — each via the same staging pattern, joining through the old `lookup_value` row to match on `code` = the new table's `type_code`. `book`/`period`/`period_mapping`/`trader_commodity_limit` needed extra care: dropped/recreated `ix_book_entity`, `period`'s 5 indexes + `uq_period_code_comm`, `period_mapping`'s `ix_pm_parent` + `uq_period_mapping`, and `trader_commodity_limit`'s `uq_tcl_trader_commodity`, since none of those can survive a `DROP COLUMN` while still referencing it. `dbo.commodity.commodity_type` itself is correctly **not** among the 11 — V58 dropped that column entirely back then as a redundant 1:1 self-tag (a stale binding row I'd initially written for it, based only on V55's text without checking V58's later reversal, caught and removed before this). Both new tables registered in `master_data_table_registry` (`Products & Markets`).
    - **Step 1–2 — the generic conversion**: `dbo.lookup_category` (`category_id`, `category_code` UNIQUE, `category_name`, `description`, `sort_order`, `is_active`, audit cols) backfilled from every distinct `lookup_value.category` string remaining *after* steps 0a/0b removed `book_type`/`commodity_type`'s rows — so neither ever becomes a `lookup_category` row. `lookup_value.category` converted via the established staging-column pattern to `category_id INT NOT NULL FK -> lookup_category`.
    - **Step 3 — dead-row cleanup** (explicitly approved): `36_carbon_environmental.sql` had seeded real `lookup_value` rows for `emission_scheme_type`/`carbon_registry_type`/`environmental_product_type`/`emission_obligation_status` *before* V83 built dedicated tables for those same 4 concepts and rewired the real columns to point at the new tables — those 4 categories' `lookup_value` rows (and their now-empty `lookup_category` headers) had had nothing referencing them since V83 ran, so they're deleted here. V83 itself is not touched.
    - **Step 4 — `dbo.lookup_category_binding`**: records which `table_name`/`column_name` consumes which `category_id` (one category can bind to many tables; a given column binds to exactly one category) — seeded with the 11 columns still genuinely FK'd to `lookup_value` after `book_type`/`commodity_type` moved off it (`REPORTING_CLASSIFICATION_TYPE`×2, `operator_type`, `instrument_type`, `storage_agreement_type`, `transport_agreement_type`, `price_adjustment_type`, `demurrage_basis`, `rin_transaction_type`, `rin_obligation_status`, `gl_account_type`). Categories seeded in V49/V50 (`breach_action`, `country_risk_rating`, `credit_alert_type`, `instrument_class`, `limit_basis`, `review_outcome`, `gl_normal_balance`) get a `lookup_category` row but zero bindings — those columns were never converted from free text to FK in the first place, part of the pre-existing, deliberately-deferred CHECK-constraint backlog, not touched here. `lookup_category_binding` itself is deliberately **not** registered in `master_data_table_registry` — it's plumbing for the reference-data GUI to resolve dropdown sources, not something an admin browses/edits directly.
  - **Frontend gap found and fixed while wiring the mock, not a pre-planned task**: `ReferenceDataTable.tsx`'s generic FK-dropdown logic (`fkOptions`) filtered lookup_value rows by `r['category'] === category` — a direct string-field read that would have silently broken (empty dropdowns, no error) the moment `lookup_value.category` stopped being a plain string in the mock. Fixed by resolving `foreignKeyCategory`'s code (e.g. `'operator_type'`) through a new conditional `lookup_category` fetch into a `category_id`, then filtering on `r['categoryId']`. Same bug, same fix pattern, in `ProductsPage.tsx`'s `ReportingGroupsTab` (`l.category === 'REPORTING_CLASSIFICATION_TYPE'` → resolves via a `lookup_category` lookup now). Also confirmed via `grep` that no other frontend file reads `.category` off a `lookup_value`-shaped row.
  - **Hint-clarity pass** (user asked explicitly, after the book_type/commodity_type rework): every remaining `lookup_value`-backed FK column's `foreignKeyCategory` audited for accuracy against the real `lookup_category` codes, not just assumed correct. Found `reporting_group.classificationTypeId` had never had `foreignKeyCategory` set at all (a pre-existing gap, silently mixing all 11 categories' rows into one dropdown) — fixed to `'REPORTING_CLASSIFICATION_TYPE'`. `freight_rate_index`/`laytime_term_template`/`demurrage_dispatch_rate`'s `commodityType` columns were still pointing `foreignKeyTable` at `'lookup_value'` from before this session's rework — repointed to `'commodity_type'` (no category needed now, it's a normal dedicated-table FK). `operatorType`'s existing `'operator_type'` category confirmed accurate, left as-is. `ReferenceDataTable.tsx`'s generated hint text reworded from `Fixed list of values ('X') managed in Lookup Values` to `Values come from Lookup Values, filtered to the 'X' category` — states the source table and the filter explicitly instead of implying it.
  - **`referenceData.ts` mock**: `lookup_value`'s metadata column is `categoryId: foreign_key -> lookup_category`; `lookup_category` mock seed has 10 rows (`REPORTING_CLASSIFICATION_TYPE`, `operator_type`, `instrument_type`, `storage_agreement_type`, `transport_agreement_type`, `price_adjustment_type`, `demurrage_basis`, `gl_account_type`, `rin_transaction_type`, `rin_obligation_status` — `book_type`/`commodity_type` were never in this mock array to begin with, since the mock's `lookup_value` rowSeed never modeled them). New `commodity_type` `PARENT_LOOKUP_TABLES` entry (11 rows, same ids/order as the real table) — `book_type` already existed there from an earlier session, untouched. `book.bookType`/`book.commodityType` in the bespoke `book` entity mock (`etrmHandlers.ts`) were never lookup_value-backed there in the first place (plain string/number literals) — no mock changes needed for those beyond the new dedicated-table entries existing. `registrySeed` gained rows for `lookup_category` and `commodity_type` (auto-derived, no manual edit needed for the latter); `MasterDataHub.tsx` gained matching cards for both.
  - Verified: byte-diffed the two `85_lookup_category.sql` copies (identical) after every edit round; `tsc -b --noEmit` clean.
- **V81–V84 — closed out the remaining static-data-reference review (the ~26-entry orphan list from V80's sweep) with real schema, not just GUI/registry fixes.** User confirmed the full corrected scope after a targeted schema check (below) found most of the "20 missing tables" weren't missing at all. Result: 9 columns finished a half-done `lookup_value` conversion, 13 new dedicated FK tables got built, 3 mock-only entries turned out to be pure duplicates and were deleted instead of built.
  - **The scope correction (do this check before building 20 anything):** cross-referencing each of the ~26 mock-only `PARENT_LOOKUP_TABLES` entries against the real schema found: `crude_grade_type` (Brent/WTI/Forties…) duplicates `dbo.product`, which already has real `BRENT-CRUDE`/`WTI-CRUDE` rows; `power_load_type` (Baseload/Peak/Off-Peak) duplicates `dbo.load_shape_template`, already FK'd from `power_product_detail.default_load_shape_id`; `lng_price_basis` (JCC/HH/TTF/NBP) duplicates `dbo.price_index`, which already models benchmark indices the same way. All three deleted from the mock, no schema built for them. Separately, `gas_day_type` turned out to already be correctly wired (`dbo.period.gas_day_type_lookup_id`, done in V57) — just needed removing from the mock's fake-table list. `nomination_type` was left alone — its parent `dbo.nomination` table doesn't exist yet (matches the Hub's own `live: false`), same deferred-not-missing status as the already-documented `pricing_trigger_event_type`.
  - **V81** (`database/81_check_columns_lookup_value_wiring.sql`): 7 columns already had their `lookup_value` category rows seeded in real SQL (`trade.instrument_type`, `trade_storage_agreement_detail.storage_agreement_type`, `trade_transport_agreement_detail.transport_agreement_type` — all V44; `trade_order_price_adjustment.adjustment_type`, `trade_order.demurrage_basis` — V46; `rin_transaction.transaction_type`, `rin_obligation.status` — V38) but the consuming column itself was never actually converted from CHECK+VARCHAR — same V77 staging-column pattern (add INT column, backfill by code match, drop CHECK column, rename, add FK), just finishing conversions that were already half-started.
  - **V82** (7 tables, Credit & Collateral): `margin_agreement_type`/`valuation_frequency_type`/`governing_law_type` (from `margin_agreement`'s 3 CHECK columns), `credit_limit_type`/`credit_limit_status_type` (from `credit_limit`), `lc_type`/`lc_status_type` (from `letter_of_credit` — note V35 drops and rebuilds V5's original `letter_of_credit` table from scratch, so the CHECK constraints to convert live in `35_credit_margin_lc.sql`, not the dead V5 definition still sitting in `05_financial_operational_md.sql`; checked which one actually survives before touching either). All single-parent, no existing `lookup_value` rows, built as dedicated tables (V17 shape) per explicit instruction, not `lookup_value` categories.
  - **V83** (4 tables, Carbon & Environmental): `emission_scheme_type`, `carbon_registry_type`, `environmental_product_type`, `emission_obligation_status` — from `emission_scheme`/`carbon_registry`/`environmental_product`/`emission_obligation` (V36). These four had no CHECK constraint at all, just a plain comment (`-- COMPLIANCE | VOLUNTARY`) — less validated than any other column touched this session.
  - **V84** (2 tables + 1 wiring fix): `uom_type` (from `unit_of_measure.uom_category`) and `metal_shape` (from `metal_brand.metal_form`, V68) — **built against the real CHECK values, not the mock's guess**: the mock had invented `VOLUME/WEIGHT/ENERGY/POWER/QUANTITY/DISTANCE` for UoM types and a different 9-value set for metal shapes; the real constraints are `VOLUME/WEIGHT/ENERGY/POWER/TEMPERATURE/COUNT/OTHER` and `CATHODE/CATHODE_FULL_PLATE/INGOT/WIRE_ROD/PIG/BAR/GRANULES/BRIQUETTE/SLAB/OTHER` respectively — used the real ones. `gl_account_type` turned out to already be seeded as a `lookup_value` category directly inside `37_gl_account.sql` itself — wired `gl_account.account_type` to it instead of building a 3rd new table.
  - **Frontend**: `referenceData.ts`'s `PARENT_LOOKUP_TABLES` rebuilt to match — the 9 lookup_value-routed columns' rows moved into the shared `lookup_value` mock array (lookupId 12–73); the 13 dedicated tables rebuilt with real PKs/values (most already matched what was already written, `metal_shape`/`uom_type` rewritten with the real values above); `crude_grade_type`/`power_load_type`/`lng_price_basis` deleted outright. `registrySeed` needed **no manual edits** — it's auto-derived from `PARENT_LOOKUP_TABLES.map(...)`, so keeping a table in that array is sufficient to register it. `MasterDataHub.tsx` got 13 new cards in their correct existing groups (Credit & Collateral ×7, Carbon & Environmental ×4, Products & Markets ×1, Finance & Settlement ×1).
  - **The "build an API" part turned out to be free**: `ReferenceDataMetadataService`'s own header comment says it plainly — "adding a Tier 2 table is a registry row, not new code" — it derives all column/FK/CHECK metadata from SQL Server's system catalogs (`INFORMATION_SCHEMA`, `sys.check_constraints`, `sys.foreign_keys`) at request time. All 13 new tables + the 9 rewired columns get real CRUD through the existing generic `ReferenceDataController`/`ReferenceDataCrudService` with zero Java changes, purely from the `master_data_table_registry` INSERT rows in V82–V84.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean), `mvn clean compile` (clean, confirms V81–V84 didn't reintroduce anything the Lombok-removal fix depended on), byte-diffed all 4 migration copies (identical), and headless Chrome across one table from each new group (Margin Agreement Types, UoM Types, Emission Scheme Types, Metal Physical Forms) — all render real seeded data through the actual Static Data screen, correctly grouped in the sidebar tree; confirmed `crude_grade_type`/`power_load_type` no longer appear anywhere in the Hub search.
