- **Fixed `etrm-backend`'s compile break for real, in place — root cause was never actually diagnosed before this session, just labeled "pre-existing, unrelated" three times.** User asked to review Static Data (Tier 2) table references and I raised, unprompted, that `ReferenceDataController.java` couldn't compile — something I'd previously dismissed as pre-existing/out-of-scope without actually diagnosing it. Traced it properly this time:
- **Fixed `etrm-backend`'s compile break for real, in place — root cause was never actually diagnosed before this session, just labeled "pre-existing, unrelated" three times.** User asked to review Static Data (Tier 2) table references and I raised, unprompted, that `ReferenceDataController.java` couldn't compile — something I'd previously dismissed as pre-existing/out-of-scope without actually diagnosing it. Traced it properly this time:
  - **Root cause 1 (the real one): Lombok's annotation processor is broken on this environment's JDK (26.x) under any explicit compiler version flag.** `MasterDataTableRegistry.java` used `@Getter @Setter` (the *only* file in the entire backend using Lombok — every other JPA entity already has plain hand-written accessors). Confirmed via direct `javac` reproduction, not guessed: with `--release N` (any N), or `-source N -target N` (any N, including N matching the JDK's own native major version), Lombok's processor runs with no error/warning but silently emits none of its generated members — call sites like `entry.getTableName()` then fail as "cannot find symbol" even though the declaring class "compiles" clean. Only fully unflagged, fully native compilation avoided it, and Maven's compiler plugin can't be made to omit a version flag entirely (blank `maven.compiler.source/target/release` falls back to the plugin's own ancient 1.3/1.1 defaults, which modern javac outright refuses). Fix: removed Lombok entirely — rewrote `MasterDataTableRegistry.java` with plain getters/setters matching every other entity's existing style, dropped the `lombok` dependency and its `spring-boot-maven-plugin` exclude from `pom.xml`. Deterministic, permanent, and consistent with the codebase's own established convention — no compiler flag workarounds needed or left behind.
  - **Root cause 2 (genuinely separate, unrelated to Lombok): `ContactRepository`/`AddressRepository` were just missing a method declaration.** `CounterpartyController.java` calls `contactRepository.findByEntityTypeAndEntityId(EntityType, Long)` and the address equivalent — `BankAccountRepository` (same package, same polymorphic pattern) already declares this exact derived-query method; `ContactRepository`/`AddressRepository` simply never had it added. One-line fix on each interface, matching `BankAccountRepository`'s existing signature exactly.
  - `mvn clean compile` now returns 0 errors — confirmed clean, not just "no new errors relative to a broken baseline" like earlier in this session.
  - Attempted `mvn spring-boot:run -Dspring-boot.run.profiles=dev` (there's a real H2 in-memory dev profile, `application-dev.yml`, that was previously assumed unusable) to get genuine runtime verification instead of compile-only — hit a **separate, unrelated ceiling**: `spring-boot-maven-plugin:3.3.5`'s bundled ASM can't read Java 25 major-version (69) classfiles ("Unsupported class file major version 69"), since Spring Boot 3.3.5 predates Java 25. Did not chase this further — out of scope for what was asked (the compile fix), and downgrading `java.version` back to 21 or upgrading Spring Boot itself are both real options for whoever picks this up, not something to guess at without asking first.
  - `java.version` was externally bumped from 21 → 25 in `pom.xml` (and `README.md` synced to match) partway through this investigation, not by me — left as-is per instruction; it's compatible with the Lombok fix (the fix works regardless of `java.version`'s value, since it removes the flag-dependent failure mode entirely rather than tuning around it).
- **Full-session re-verification pass (no code change) — confirmed everything above actually works end-to-end, and found 2 new pre-existing rough edges while probing error paths.** User asked for a full review of the session's work. Drove the real UI (not just `tsc`/`mvn compile`) through the multi-role assign/approve flow, the name-denormalization, and the new search/filters — all confirmed working via headless Chrome (see `/private/tmp/.../scratchpad/verify/` for screenshots, not preserved past the session). Two findings surfaced by deliberately triggering the *error* path (a duplicate-role 409), not present on the happy path:
  1. **The duplicate-role error shows the wrong message and the button appears stuck loading for ~3 seconds even though the backend responds in <50ms.** Root cause: `admin/roles/api.ts`'s `json()` helper throws a plain `Error(text)` instead of a `ProblemDetail`-shaped object, so every `onError: (e: ProblemDetail) => message.error(e.detail ?? e.title ?? 'fallback')` in `admin/roles/hooks.ts` always hits the generic fallback text — the specific "User already has this role assignment." the backend correctly returns is dead on arrival. Compounding it: TanStack Query v5 awaits `onError` before clearing a mutation's `isPending`, and antd v5's `message.error()` returns a promise that only resolves after its 3-second toast auto-dismisses — so the triggering button visibly "hangs" for ~3s after the request already failed. This is an app-wide pattern (same `onError` shape used by every mutation in this file, and likely others), not unique to the assign-role feature — just never exercised end-to-end before now. Not fixed this session; flagged for a follow-up pass.
  2. **Credit Limits' Credit Analyst dropdown shows redundant-looking labels** — `"System Administrator (System Administrator)"`, `"Risk Manager (Risk Manager)"` — because those two seed users' `fullName` happens to equal their role's `roleName`. Not a logic bug (filtering is correct), just an unguarded label format inherited from before this session's `roles.some()` rewrite. Low severity.
  
  Also created `.claude/skills/verify/SKILL.md` (repo root) capturing the launch/drive recipe for future sessions — dev server port isolation, the ag-grid pinned-column multi-DOM-node gotcha, the `forceRender` hidden-modal-selector-collision gotcha, and the antd-message/TanStack-Query interaction above, so the next session doesn't have to rediscover any of this from scratch.
- **Added search + filter to both tables on `/admin/roles` (Roles tab, User Assignments tab) — user flagged that paginated data needs this as a general rule, not just for this page.** Both tabs were plain antd `Table` with `pagination={{ pageSize: 15 }}` and no way to narrow results — first plain-`Table` (non-`SmartGrid`) page in the codebase to get this treatment, since `Input.Search`/client-side-filter wasn't an existing pattern anywhere else to copy (`SmartGrid`'s ag-grid pages get a "Quick search…" box for free via `quickFilterText`; plain-`Table` pages didn't have an equivalent). Added: a free-text `Input` above each table (Roles: matches `roleCode`/`roleName`/`description`; Assignments: matches `fullName`/`username`/`roleName`/`roleCode`), filtering `dataSource` client-side via `useMemo`; plus native antd column `filters`/`onFilter` on the Type and Status columns (Roles) and Status column (Assignments) — no extra state needed for those, antd Table handles them natively once `filters` is set. Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome: searching "trader" on Roles correctly matched both `TRADER` and `CRUDE_TRADER`; searching "chen" on User Assignments correctly narrowed to just Sarah Chen's row. **General rule for future pages, not just this one: any paginated table needs search/filter — check for this as part of building or reviewing a list view, the same way the two "basics" above should have been checked.**
- **Fixed: Roles & Permissions' "User Assignments" tab showed a bare numeric `User ID` column, no name — real UX gap, frontend + backend both fixed.** User flagged this directly. `UserRoleAssignment` (frontend `admin/roles/types.ts`) gained `username`/`fullName`, denormalized the same way `roleName`/`roleCode` already were: hand-seeded on the 9 static `assignmentsSeed` rows (`mocks/rbacData.ts`, mirroring `systemUsersStore`) and looked up live in `rbacHandlers.ts`'s and `etrmHandlers.ts`'s assignment-creation handlers (both places a new assignment gets built). `RolesPage.tsx`'s assignment table's `User ID` column replaced with a `User` column showing full name + `(username)` underneath. Mirrored on the real backend the same session-long convention established: new `AssignmentResponse` DTO (`rbac/AssignmentResponse.java`, denormalizes `username`/`fullName` via `AppUserRepository`) — `RbacController`'s 5 assignment endpoints (`listAllAssignments`/`listUserAssignments`/`assignRole`/`approveAssignment`/`rejectAssignment`) now return it instead of the raw JPA entity; `assignRole` also gained a real "does this user exist" check it was missing (previously would silently create an assignment for a nonexistent `userId`, matching the theme of the FK gap fixed below — nothing enforced the relationship at the application layer either). Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean), headless Chrome (assigned Credit Analyst to Alice Smith through the modal — new row correctly showed "Alice Smith (a.smith)", not blank or a raw ID), and `mvn -o compile` (no new errors beyond the pre-existing unrelated ones noted above).
- **Fixed in place (V20, no new migration): `dbo.user_role_assignment.user_id` was missing its `FOREIGN KEY` entirely.** The column only ever had a comment — `-- FK → system_user.user_id` — no real constraint, and `system_user` was never a real table name (the actual one is `dbo.app_user`, from V1). Nothing stopped an assignment row pointing at a `user_id` that doesn't exist. This survived two full passes over this exact table earlier in the session (the RBAC rebuild and the V79 backend fix) and only surfaced on a third pass, prompted by a direct user question about which table connects `app_user` and `user_role` — user called out that this should have been caught earlier. Added `CONSTRAINT fk_ura_user FOREIGN KEY (user_id) REFERENCES dbo.app_user(user_id)` directly to V20's `CREATE TABLE`, removed the stale comment (matching this same file's existing precedent of fixing structural gaps in place rather than patching forward — see its own header comment about the V1/V20 duplicate-table bug). No seed data anywhere inserts into `user_role_assignment` (`dev-seed.sql` only seeds `app_user`), so nothing to backfill or clean up first. No live SQL Server instance available in this environment to actually run Flyway against, so verified structurally (full `CREATE TABLE` re-read, byte-identical diff between the two migration copies) rather than by executing the migration.
- **V79 — `dbo.app_user.role` dropped; the real Spring Boot backend had the exact same disconnected-role bug the frontend mock just had fixed (entry below), except live in the DB.** After fixing the frontend, user asked "what about db?" — checked whether the real backend (`etrm-backend`, not just the MSW mocks) had the same problem, and it did, independently: `V21__address_contact_rbac_user_profile.sql` had bolted a flat `role VARCHAR(30)` directly onto `dbo.app_user` — no FK, no CHECK, added right after V20 had already built the real RBAC tables — and `SystemUserController` read/wrote that string directly, never once touching `UserRoleAssignmentRepository`. Not a live security hole (`AuthController` never reads `app_user.role` for authorization — every login gets a flat `ROLE_USER` today, per its own comment that real RBAC "waits on the separate role table"), but a second, drifted source of truth for the same concept. Fixed to match: **V79** (`database/79_app_user_role_column_removed.sql` / backend copy) backfills a real `ACTIVE` `user_role_assignment` row for any `app_user` with the old `role = 'ADMIN'` string (the only value V21 ever actually seeded) before dropping the column outright. `AppUser.java`'s `role` field/getter/setter removed. `SystemUserController` rewritten: injects `UserRoleRepository`/`UserRoleAssignmentRepository`, returns a new `SystemUserResponse` DTO (`roles: List<RoleSummary>`, denormalized from `assignmentRepo.findByUserIdAndIsActiveTrue()`, filtered to ACTIVE/PENDING_APPROVAL — mirrors the frontend's `SystemUserRoleSummary` exactly) instead of the raw `AppUser` entity; `createUser` takes an optional `roleId` and requests the user's first role through the identical `PENDING_APPROVAL`-assignment logic `RbacController.assignRole` uses (not a bypass); `updateUser` no longer touches roles at all — that goes through `RbacController`'s assignment endpoints, same governance as the frontend enforces. Verified the touched files compile clean in isolation (`mvn -o compile` fails module-wide on unrelated pre-existing errors — see the CRITICAL note above — confirmed via `git stash` that this backend module was already broken before this session touched anything).
- **Fixed: a user could not actually be assigned more than one role, despite the schema already supporting it.** User asked to check whether multiple roles per user worked and fix it cleanly. `dbo.user_role_assignment`'s uniqueness constraint is on `(user_id, role_id)`, not `user_id` alone — the data model was always correct — but two gaps in the frontend built during the previous entry's RBAC fix made it unreachable in practice: (1) `useAssignRole()` (`admin/roles/hooks.ts`) was fully wired to `POST /users/:userId/role-assignments` but never called from anywhere in the UI — there was no "assign an additional role" action at all, only the one-role-at-creation flow and revoke; (2) `SystemUser` denormalized only a single "current" assignment (`currentAssignment()` in `etrmHandlers.ts` picked the first ACTIVE, falling back to first PENDING, and discarded the rest) — even a user who somehow held two active roles would only ever show one, everywhere. Fixed both: `SystemUser.roleId/roleCode/roleName/assignmentStatus` replaced with `roles: SystemUserRoleSummary[]` (every ACTIVE/PENDING_APPROVAL assignment, not just one), `denormalizeSystemUser` now maps all of a user's live assignment rows instead of picking one; added an "Assign Role" button + modal on Roles & Permissions → User Assignments (`RolesPage.tsx`) that calls the previously-dead `useAssignRole` hook; the Users grid's Role column and the edit drawer's role display both now render every role as a tag (with a Pending suffix per assignment, not per user); `CreditLimitsPage.tsx`'s analyst-picker filter updated from a single `roleCode` check to `roles.some(...)`. Frontend-only, no migration — the schema needed no change. Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome: assigned Read-Only Viewer to `j.doe` (who already held Trader) through the new modal, approved it, and confirmed both the Users grid and the edit drawer showed "Trader" + "Read-Only Viewer" simultaneously; re-requesting the same role for the same user still correctly 409s.
- **User Management review, part 2 — found and fixed a real architectural bug: the Users page's "Role" field was a second, disconnected role system from the real RBAC (`user_role`/`user_role_assignment`) reviewed in the entry below.** User asked to review the Users page (`/admin/users`), since access_level's home in role creation prompted a closer look. Found the actual bug rather than chasing a red herring first:
  - **Ruled out first:** a `rc-util`/antd "There may be circular references" console warning fires on a few `SmartGrid`-based create drawers (Desks, System Users — not Brokers, Payment Terms, Legal Entity). Bisected it down (removed the Role field, removed `useFormDraft`, removed `hint()` tooltips — warning persisted through all of them) without finding the exact prop; no visible functional symptom found anywhere (forms render and save correctly), so treated as the same class of benign pre-existing noise as this app's documented antd deprecation warnings, not the real bug — flagged, not chased further.
  - **The real bug:** `SystemUser.role` (`src/features/admin/system-users/types.ts`) was a flat, hardcoded 6-value string (`USER_ROLES`) with **zero connection to the real RBAC system** built in V20/verified by RolesPage.tsx — `dbo.app_user` has no `role` column at all; a user's actual role has only ever lived in `user_role_assignment`. The two systems had already drifted: 2 seed users (`s.chen`, `m.webb`) had `role: 'CREDIT_ANALYST'`, a value in neither the hardcoded list nor the real `user_role` table — confirmed visually, their edit drawer showed the raw unmatched string sitting in the Role dropdown, not a real option. Consequence: a custom role created via Roles & Permissions could never be assigned to a user from the Users page at all, since that page could only ever offer its 6 hardcoded strings.
  - User chose the real fix over a quick patch: removed `SystemUser.role`/`USER_ROLES` entirely. `SystemUser` now carries `roleId`/`roleCode`/`roleName`/`assignmentStatus`, denormalized live from `user_role_assignment` (mocks/rbacData.ts's `assignmentsStore`) — the same single source of truth Roles & Permissions' "User Assignments" tab already manages, not a second copy. `mocks/rbacHandlers.ts`'s previously-private `roles`/`roleFunctions`/`assignments` arrays moved to `rbacData.ts` as shared exported state (`rolesStore`/`roleFunctionsStore`/`assignmentsStore`) so `etrmHandlers.ts`'s new `admin/users` handlers read and write the identical live data — same shadow-store lesson as `legalEntityStore` vs `legalEntitiesRef` (§0 above).
  - Added a real `CREDIT_ANALYST` role (`roleId: 8`, SYSTEM, APPROVED, read-only counterparty/master-data/position grants) to close the gap `s.chen`/`m.webb` exposed — `credit_limit.credit_analyst_user_id` (a pre-existing field on `CreditLimitsPage.tsx`) already filtered system users by this exact role code, confirming it's a real, consumed concept, not an invented one. Rebuilt `assignmentsSeed` to cover all 9 system users (the old 4-row seed only covered users 1-4, and its role mappings didn't even match those users' old fake `role` field — e.g. old userId 4 was mapped to OPERATIONS in the assignment seed but `RISK_MANAGER` in the fake field — another symptom of the two systems never having been cross-checked).
  - **New user creation now requests a role through the exact same pending-approval path** as Roles & Permissions' own assignment flow (`POST /admin/users` creates the user, then — if a role was picked — creates a `PENDING_APPROVAL` `user_role_assignment` for them via the identical logic `POST /users/:userId/role-assignments` already uses, not a bypass). Editing an existing user's role is deliberately **not** exposed inline anymore — the Role field is disabled on edit with a hint pointing at Roles & Permissions → User Assignments, so a role change goes through the same request/approve governance as any other assignment rather than being silently overwritten.
  - **Found and fixed a second real bug while verifying the round-trip, not before shipping it:** approving/rejecting/revoking an assignment on Roles & Permissions only ever invalidated the `role-assignments` query key, never `system-users` — so the Users grid kept showing a role as "Pending" after it had actually been approved, until its own 5-minute `staleTime` lapsed or a manual refresh. Confirmed via headless Chrome: created a user requesting Trader, saw it flagged Pending on both the Users grid and the User Assignments tab, approved it there, and the Users grid still said Pending on SPA-internal navigation back — the approve PATCH itself returned 200 correctly, so the bug was purely a missing cache invalidation, not the mutation. Fixed by having all four assignment mutations (`useAssignRole`/`useApproveAssignment`/`useRejectAssignment`/`useRevokeAssignment`) invalidate both query keys; re-verified the same round trip and the Users grid updated immediately.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome end to end: all 9 seeded users show correct real role names (System Administrator/Trader×2/Risk Manager/Compliance/Operations [Pending, the intentional worked example]/Read-Only Viewer/Credit Analyst×2); created a new user requesting Trader — appeared Pending on both Users and User Assignments; approved it there — Users grid reflected Active immediately without a manual refresh.
- **Reviewed all 6 remaining CHECK constraints in the User Management domain (RBAC + field permissions); all 6 stay CHECK — no migration.** Followed up on the earlier CHECK-constraint-audit discussion: for `user_role.role_type`/`status`, `role_function.access_level`, `user_role_assignment.status`, `object_lock_rule.locked_to`, and `field_permission_rule.field_permission`, checked each against actual frontend code (the only place real logic exists in this prototype — `etrm-backend` has no authorization enforcement yet) instead of guessing from the column name or category label:
  - **`user_role.status` / `user_role_assignment.status`** — real exhaustive state machines. `RolesPage.tsx` branches on every value (`status === 'PENDING_APPROVAL'`, `'DRAFT'`, `'ACTIVE'`, …) to show/hide Approve/Reject/Edit/Revoke actions. A value added via an admin picklist with no matching branch would get stuck showing no valid action at all. **Left as CHECK.**
  - **`user_role.role_type`** — `RolesPage.tsx` branches on `roleType === 'SYSTEM'` to lock editing and show a lock icon. Lower risk than the status columns (a new value degrades gracefully — it just wouldn't get lock protection) but it's a structural flag, not a business picklist. **Left as CHECK.**
  - **`object_lock_rule.locked_to`** and **`field_permission_rule.field_permission`** — both feed the real, actively-used field-permission enforcement engine (`useFieldPermissions.ts`'s `canEdit`/`canView`/`isHidden`, gating every `<PermissionField>` across the app's capture forms). The highest-risk pair of the six — converting either would let an admin add a value the enforcement engine's exhaustive 3-way check has no branch for. **Left as CHECK.**
  - **`role_function.access_level`** — confirmed zero enforcement code anywhere in the app; `RolesPage.tsx` only stores and displays it via a Read/Read+Write checkbox matrix, no authorization gate reads it — by the same test applied to the other five, this one was safe to convert. **Built as a `lookup_value` FK (staging migration, `configLookups.ts` extended for shared-table categories, `FunctionMatrix` resolving ids dynamically) and verified working end-to-end, then reverted at the user's explicit direction** — kept as CHECK alongside the other five rather than being the one exception, so User Management's six columns read as one consistent, deliberate decision instead of five kept + one converted for a reason (no live authorization logic yet) that doesn't obviously read as a reason from the UI alone. Nothing about the CHECK constraint or the `READ`/`READ_WRITE` UI changed as a result — this is purely "stayed as it already was."
  - Found and fixed a real, unrelated bug while reading `user_role`'s schema to scope this review: `V1__master_data_foundation.sql` and `V20__rbac_roles_functions.sql` both do `CREATE TABLE dbo.user_role`, with V20 never dropping V1's version first — V1's is a leftover flat user_id+role_code CHECK assignment table (conceptually superseded by V20's own `user_role_assignment`), and V20 redefines the same table name from scratch with an unrelated shape (`role_id`/`role_type`/`status`). Would fail outright on a real from-scratch deploy. Fixed in place by adding `IF OBJECT_ID('dbo.user_role','U') IS NOT NULL DROP TABLE dbo.user_role;` at the top of V20 (both `database/20_...sql` and the backend `V20__...sql`, kept byte-identical) — same "fix the actual migration that needs it" precedent as V55's desk CHECK bug. This fix is real and stayed in, independent of the access_level revert above.
  - **Built the missing "User Management" Master Data Hub group** — `System Users` and `User Roles` (previously buried under "Organization & Users") moved here; `Field Permissions` (built earlier, routed at `/admin/field-permissions`, but never had a Hub entry at all) added.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) after the revert too — no leftover references to the numeric `AccessLevel`/`ACCESS_LEVEL` lookup group anywhere.
- **V78 frontend rewiring — completed the follow-up flagged in the V78 entry below (converted all 12 parent-lookup-table columns' consuming pages/types/mocks from string enums to numeric FK ids), plus found and fixed 3 real bugs while verifying it.** The V78 SQL cutover was backend-only; this pass did the matching frontend work across `payment-terms`, `netting-agreements`, `storage`, `products`, `tier1/counterparty` (+ its `Addresses`/`BankAccounts`/`Contacts`/`TaxRegistrations` sub-sections), `tier1/legal-entity`, and `trade` (`TradeBlotter.tsx`'s `tradeType`): each converted type (`ContactRole`, `AddressType`, `BankAccountType`, `PaymentMethod`, `SettlementType`, `StorageType`, `NettingAgreementType`, `TaxType`, `EntityType`, `CpType`, `KycStatus`, `TradeType`) is now `number`, mock seed data reseeded with the matching numeric id, and every consuming `<Select>`/grid column resolves its label via `useCustomConfigOptions()` (`configLookups.ts`, extended with `GROUP_TO_PK` so the generic `/reference-data/{table}` fetch can pull the right numeric PK column per lookup group) against the 12 real `PARENT_LOOKUP_TABLES` rows already seeded in `mocks/referenceData.ts`.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome (Playwright) across all 8 changed routes — and the verification pass itself surfaced 3 real, pre-existing bugs, none of them latent in the V78 diff itself:
    1. **MSW route collision hid the entire Netting Agreements grid** (`counterparties/netting-agreements`) behind a permanent "No records found." `counterpartyHandlers.ts`'s `GET /counterparties/:id` (registered before `etrmHandlers.ts` in `browser.ts`) matches *any* single path segment, so `/counterparties/netting-agreements` was being treated as a request for counterparty id `"netting-agreements"` — always a 404, never reaching the correct `crudHandlers('counterparties/netting-agreements', ...)` handler registered later. Same latent collision affected `/counterparties/commercial-terms` and `/counterparties/gtc-agreements` too (untouched by V78 itself, but broken by the same pre-existing route bug) — confirmed fixed by the same change via a follow-up headless-browser check (both now return their 2 seeded rows, zero bad responses). Fixed generically, not special-cased: constrained the three id-based counterparty handlers (`GET`/`PUT`/`PATCH .../deactivate`) to `:id(\d+)` (path-to-regexp digit constraint) so they only match numeric ids.
    2. **`LegalEntityListPage` and `CounterpartyListPage`'s "Type" grid columns permanently showed "—"** — both used ag-grid's `valueFormatter` to resolve an async-loaded lookup label (`entityTypeOptions`/`cpTypeOptions`), but `valueFormatter`'s result is computed once at initial cell render and never recomputed once the lookup query resolves later — confirmed by instrumenting the formatter: it was still seeing an empty options array on every subsequent grid refresh even minutes after the underlying query had `status: 'success'`. The pattern that already works elsewhere in this app for the identical async-lookup-label shape is `cellRenderer` (ProductsPage's Settlement column, TradeBlotter's Type column, and — right next to the broken one — `CounterpartyListPage`'s own `kycStatus` column). Converted both broken columns from `valueFormatter` to `cellRenderer`.
    3. **`LegalEntityListPage`'s own ad-hoc `legal_entity_type` lookup query was silently getting the wrong data shape** — it used React Query key `['lookup', 'legal_entity_type']`, which is the *exact* key `useCustomConfigOptions('LEGAL_ENTITY_TYPE')` already owns (consumed by the always-mounted `LegalEntityFormDrawer` sibling). React Query dedupes purely by key regardless of each call site's own `queryFn`, so whichever query actually won the fetch race silently supplied its `{label, value}` `ConfigOption[]` shape to *both* consumers — breaking the list page's own code, which expected raw `ReferenceDataRow[]` (`legalEntityTypeId`/`typeName`/`typeCode`). This is why bug #2's `cellRenderer` fix alone wasn't sufficient for this page (had to fix both). Gave the list page's raw fetch a distinct key (`['legal-entity-type-rows']`).
  - After all three fixes: Netting Agreements grid shows both seed rows; Legal Entities' Type column shows "Trading Company"/"Subsidiary"/"Branch"; Counterparty's Type column shows "Producer" etc.; Payment Terms shows "Wire Transfer"; Storage shows "Tank Farm"/"Gas Storage"/"Salt Cavern"/"LNG Tank"/"Warehouse"; Products shows "Physical" settlement tags; Trade Blotter shows "Physical" trade-type tags; Counterparty form's Addresses/Contacts/Bank Accounts/Tax Registrations sub-tabs all resolve their type labels correctly (these use antd `Table`'s `render` prop, not ag-grid, so were never subject to bug #2). Zero console errors across all 8 pages beyond pre-existing antd deprecation warnings already noted elsewhere in this doc; zero unexpected network 4xx after the route-collision fix.
- **V78 — finished V17's deferred parent-lookup-table cutover for 12 of its original 13 pairs. Backend-only; frontend not yet updated (see below).** After V77, user asked why several "type" columns that already have a dedicated Static Data table still aren't FK'd to it. Investigated rather than guessed: found `V17__parent_lookup_tables.sql` (June 2026) had already built this correctly as an explicit two-phase plan — its own header states it added 13 parent lookup tables + FK columns, backfilled them, but deliberately kept the original CHECK+VARCHAR columns "for backward-compat," to be dropped "in a future migration once all application code has been migrated to use the FK columns." That follow-up never happened for 12 of the 13 — only `book.book_type` was ever finished, and via a *different* migration (V55, pointing at `lookup_value` rather than V17's own dedicated `book_type` table). The other 12 sat as orphaned, unused FK columns next to their still-live originals ever since — confirmed concretely for `storage_facility.storage_facility_type_id` by checking the frontend, which has zero knowledge of it (`StorageFacility.storageType` is still a plain string union matching the old `facility_type` CHECK).
  - Verified before writing anything: every parent table's seed data already exactly matches its child column's live CHECK value list (spot-checked all 12 against V1/V9/V47) — `storage_facility_type` in particular was already kept in sync by V47's own remap step, so no reseeding was needed, only the cutover itself.
  - `V78` completes it for: `contact.contact_role`, `address.address_type`, `bank_account.account_type`, `payment_term.payment_method`, `product.settlement_type`, `storage_facility.facility_type`, `netting_agreement.agreement_type`, `tax_registration.tax_type`, `legal_entity.entity_type`, `counterparty.cp_type`, `counterparty.kyc_status`, `trade.trade_type`, `trade.settlement_type` — each: backfill any straggler rows, drop the old CHECK + column, rename the orphaned FK column into the *original bare column name* (matching V55/V63/V77's established convention — no `_id` suffix survives), re-apply `NOT NULL`. Found and fixed 3 real blocking dependencies along the way (the same class of bug V57 hit once with `period.commodity_type`): `ix_contact_entity`/`ix_address_entity`/`ix_bank_acct_entity` (composite indexes including the dropped column), `ix_cp_type`/`ix_cp_kyc` (direct indexes on `counterparty`), and `uq_netting`/`uq_tax_reg` (UNIQUE constraints including the dropped column) — all dropped and recreated around the change. `legal_entity`/`counterparty`/`trade` are SQL Server temporal tables (per V17's own note); `SYSTEM_VERSIONING` toggled off/around each change with the corresponding `_history` table kept in step, matching V17's own handling.
  - **Deliberately backend-only this pass** — these are 13 columns across 10 tables including the core `trade` and `counterparty` entities, and each needs its own frontend rewiring (type change, FK-driven `<Select>`, mock reseed) same as the earlier 9-table batch. Frontend currently still expects the old string-enum shape for all of these (e.g. `trade.tradeType: 'PHYSICAL'`) — doesn't break the running app today since the frontend is 100% MSW-mock-driven and never calls the real backend, but the divergence is real and now larger. Flagged for a follow-up pass, not built this session.
  - **Also produced but not yet acted on:** a full audit of every enum-style CHECK constraint in the schema (194 columns not referenced elsewhere as an FK, after excluding ones on tables that are themselves already dedicated type/reference tables) — published as a searchable artifact for review. Caught and fixed 3 real bugs in the extraction script while building it (missed multi-column `DROP COLUMN` lists, CREATE TABLE body-boundary bleed across tables, a dead-migration-history false positive on `kyc_status`) — worth remembering if this list is revisited, since it's a text-scan derivation, not a live schema introspection. Most of the 194 are transactional/workflow status fields (`trade_pricing_schedule`'s 9 fixing/dispute/schedule states, `credit_limit.status`, etc.), not master data — user has not yet decided which (if any) subset beyond this V78 batch to convert.
  - Verified via careful manual cross-checking of every constraint/index/UNIQUE dependency before writing the SQL (no live DB available to test against in this environment) — did not run `tsc -b` (no frontend touched this pass).
- **V77 — `transport_operator.operator_type` converted CHECK → `lookup_value` FK, plus a new generic capability: `foreignKeyCategory`-scoped lookup_value FKs on any Static Data table.** User asked why `operator_type` was a CHECK constraint instead of going through the same `lookup_value` mechanism already used for `commodity_type`/`book_type`/`load_type`/`gas_day_type`/`classification_type`/`instrument_type`/etc. (V55/V57/V63). Answered with the actual distinguishing factor found by checking the schema, not asserted: `mot_type`/`location_type`/`inspection_type` get their own dedicated tables because *other* tables FK against them (and `mot_type` specifically carries its own business-rule columns — `requires_physical_asset`/`requires_routing` — that `lookup_value`'s flat shape can't hold); `operator_type` is single-parent (nothing else in the schema references it) and flat, making it a genuine candidate either way. User chose to convert it.
  - `V77` seeds 8 rows under `lookup_value.category = 'operator_type'` and converts the column via the established staging-column-and-rename pattern (V55/V63): add `operator_type_new INT NULL` → backfill by joining old value to `lookup_value.code` → drop the old CHECK + column → rename into place → `NOT NULL` + FK.
  - **This surfaced a real gap in the generic Tier 2 mechanism**: `lookup_value` holds every small picklist in the schema in one shared row set, so a `foreign_key` column pointing at it needs to be scoped to one category — but `ReferenceDataTable.tsx`'s FK-fetching only ever keyed `fkOptions` by table name, meaning a naive `foreignKeyTable: 'lookup_value'` would have mixed `operator_type` rows with `REPORTING_CLASSIFICATION_TYPE` rows (the only other `lookup_value` consumer so far, V63) into one dropdown. Fixed properly rather than special-cased: added `ColumnMetadata.foreignKeyCategory` (`types/referenceData.ts`, `col()` helper in `mocks/referenceData.ts`), and reworked `ReferenceDataTable.tsx`'s FK machinery to key `fkOptions` by table+category (`fkKeyFor()`) while still fetching each distinct table only once (categories are filtered client-side after the shared fetch, not a second network call) — reusable the next time any table needs a scoped `lookup_value` FK, not just this one.
  - Also fixed two other real bugs in the same generic mechanism while in there (see entry below, done first chronologically this session but documented together since both touch `ReferenceDataTable.tsx`): the enum-`<Select>` missing-placeholder bug, and country fields being raw free text everywhere.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome: Transport Operators grid resolves `SHIPPING_LINE — Shipping Line` / `RAIL_OPERATOR — Rail Operator` / `HAULIER — Haulier` correctly; edit form's Operator Type dropdown shows exactly the 8 `operator_type` rows (not `REPORTING_CLASSIFICATION_TYPE` mixed in); Lookup Values Static Data page shows both categories cleanly separated with correct sort order; zero console errors.
- **Fixed two real bugs in the generic Static Data mechanism (`ReferenceDataTable.tsx`, drives every `/static-data/:tableName` page) — found via the Transport Operators page while reviewing where Rail Cars' `operatorId` FK resolves to. No migration, frontend-only.**
  - **Enum-kind `<Select>` had no `placeholder`** (`fieldControl`'s `'enum'` case) — user asked "where is oper type" because Transport Operators' Operator Type field rendered as a blank, unlabeled dropdown (every other field type — FK, boolean, date — had a placeholder or visible default; enum was the one silent gap). Added `placeholder`/`showSearch` matching the `foreign_key` case's existing pattern.
  - **Country fields across every Static Data table were raw free-text, unlinked to the real `country` reference entity** — same systemic gap flagged (and fixed only for Rail Cars) in the previous entry. Fixed properly this time, generically, for every table at once: `ISO_3166_COLS` (`countryCode`/`jurisdictionCode`/`incorporationCountry` — already existed as a validation-only allowlist) now also drives which columns render as a country `<Select>`, keyed by column **name**, not per-table config — no per-table edits needed in `referenceData.ts`. `country` itself can't go through the generic `/reference-data/:table` FK mechanism (that mechanism assumes a numeric auto-increment PK; `country`'s PK is the ISO string code) — rather than duplicate country data into a second mock store to force-fit it (the exact `legalEntityStore`-vs-`legalEntitiesRef` shadow-store bug already documented as a past incident in this doc), `ReferenceDataTable.tsx` now fetches from the real `useCountries()` hook once and reuses it by column name everywhere.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome on two unrelated tables to confirm the fix is genuinely generic, not special-cased: Transport Operators (Operator Type dropdown now shows all 8 values with a placeholder; Country search-filtered "United" → GB/US/AE correctly; full save round-trip of a new `TEST-OP` row resolved "JP — Japan" in the grid) and Balancing Authorities (an unrelated table with its own `countryCode` column — country names resolved correctly with zero additional code, confirming the fix applies app-wide from one change).
- **V76 — Rail Cars page review: dropped free-text `approved_commodities`, wired the real (previously unbuilt) `mot_asset_product_approval` table, fixed country to a proper `Select`, added `build_year`/`gross_rail_load_lbs`.** User asked to review the Rail Cars page and settle "commodity or product?" for the car's `approved_commodities` field (`VARCHAR(500)` CSV, no FK — a dead-end free-text field), plus "link country correctly" and check for other gaps via research.
  - **Commodity vs. product — the schema already had the answer.** `dbo.mot_asset_product_approval` (V4) is a polymorphic PRODUCT-level approval table (`asset_type IN VESSEL,TRUCK,RAILCAR,CONTAINER,TANK`, with `approval_status`/`effective_from`/`effective_to`/`regulatory_ref`) that had **zero frontend wiring anywhere** — same "genuinely missing concept" pattern as `pipeline_point`/`mot_asset_product_approval`'s siblings found earlier. Asked the user whether to patch the flat CSV field or wire the real table properly; chose the real table. `V76` drops `railcar.approved_commodities` (superseded, not left as dead legacy) and the frontend gets a new "Approved Products" sub-drawer (`ApprovedProductsDrawer` in `RailcarsPage.tsx`, opened via a new grid action icon) backed by real CRUD — `railcars/types.ts` gets `RailcarProductApproval`/`RailcarProductApprovalInput`, `api.ts`/`hooks.ts` get the sub-resource calls (`/logistics/railcars/:id/product-approvals[/:id]`), mock gets `railcarProductApprovalsStore` + `computeAssetApproval()` denormalizing `productName` from `referenceRowSeed.product`. This is the first (of five possible) `mot_asset_product_approval` asset types wired — the same pattern is reusable for vessel/truck/container/tank later, not built this session.
  - **Country — found the same systemic gap as everywhere else in this app.** `features/reference/countries` (`useCountries()`, backed by a real `country` reference table with names/region/FATF/sanctions status) already exists, but every page with a country field — including Railcars — used a raw free-text 2-char `<Input>` instead of a `<Select>` sourced from it. Fixed for Railcars only (scope-contained to what was asked, not a sweep across every other page that has the same issue — Trucks/Locations/Holiday Calendars/etc. all still use raw text). `countryName` added to `Railcar` type, denormalized in the mock's `computeRailcar()`, shown as its own grid column.
  - **Researched real-world railcar data (AAR Umler Data Specification Manual)** — a full UMLER record runs 50+ mechanical/dimensional fields, deliberately not matched 1:1 (this app models logistics assets at ETRM-relevant granularity, not full mechanical engineering detail — same restraint as vessels/trucks). Two fields judged genuinely missing by parity with how this app already models the closest comparable assets: `build_year` (vessel already has `buildYear`; matters for tank-car compliance — older DOT-111s being phased out of crude/ethanol service under post-2015 PHMSA rules) and `gross_rail_load_lbs` (the actual AAR/FRA weight-class figure — 263,000/286,000/315,000 lbs — that determines which track a car can even run on; truck's analogous `gvwTonnes` already exists). Both added as plain nullable columns (no FK, no CHECK — matches `commodity_family.family_type`-style "don't over-constrain a descriptive figure" precedent).
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome: grid shows GRL/Built/Country columns correctly (286,000 / 2018 / United States); Approved Products drawer resolves both seeded approvals (Ethanol, Heating Oil) by product name; Edit drawer's Country field is a proper searchable `Select` pre-filled "US — United States"; zero console errors throughout.
- **V75 — added `effective_from`/`effective_to` (DATE) to `dbo.pipeline_cycle`.** User asked where a cycle's "start and end dates" were, pointing out this shouldn't just be a tariff thing. Clarified the two different date/time concepts already on the table before changing anything: `effective_start`/`effective_end` are `TIME` — the daily delivery window's clock time (e.g. WD1 delivers 06:00→05:00 next day) — not a calendar validity period for the cycle *rule*. `pipeline_tariff` already versions its rate rows with `effective_from`/`effective_to` (`DATE`); `pipeline_cycle` had no equivalent, so a cycle definition change (e.g. the real FERC Order 809/587-W deadline shift found via research two entries ago) could only overwrite the row in place. Added the same nullable `DATE` pair (`NULL` = always in force / no expiry, matching `pipeline_tariff`'s convention). Frontend: new `effectiveFrom`/`effectiveTo` on `PipelineCycle`/`PipelineCycleInput` (`types.ts`), a separate `DATE_FIELDS` `AppDatePicker` pair in `PipelineCyclesPage.tsx`'s drawer (distinct from the existing `TIME_FIELDS` `TimePicker`s — same Valid-From/Valid-To-must-be-after-From validation pattern as `PipelineTariffsPage.tsx`), and two new grid columns. Seeded WD1–3 with `effectiveFrom: '2020-06-01'` (the real FERC order date) and the WTI `D+1` cycle with `'2024-01-01'` (matching Capline's tariff row), all `effectiveTo: null`.
  - **Also surfaced, not built:** looking for where a deal would consume a cycle's dates, found the `TRANSPORT_AGREEMENT` `instrumentType` (V44) has a backing table (`trade_transport_agreement_detail`, with a plain-text `pipeline_code`, no `pipeline_cycle_id` FK) but **no form panel in `TradeBlotter.tsx` at all** — unlike `oilDetail`/`freightDetail`, which do render. Deriving a deal's delivery window from a cycle's validity dates would mean building that missing panel first (and adding a `pipeline_cycle_id` FK to the detail table) — flagged for the user to scope explicitly rather than assumed, since it's a Trade Blotter change, not a master-data one.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome: grid shows "2020-06-01" / "–" (Valid From/To) for the gas cycles and "2024-01-01" / "–" for the WTI cycle; Edit drawer round-trips both correctly; zero console errors.
- **V74 — added nullable `product_id` to `dbo.pipeline_cycle`.** User pushed back on the earlier `pipeline_cycle` build ("where is product link to cycle?" / "you can't have this work for all products"), arguing a cycle shouldn't apply identically to every product on a pipeline. Researched real practice before changing schema (FERC tariff filings for Colonial Pipeline and Explorer Pipeline, both real multi-product refined-products pipelines): cycle *deadlines* are defined per pipeline/segment and shared across whatever product batch is nominated into that slot — there's no per-product deadline variance within a single cycle in real tariffs. So the ask wasn't "deadlines differ by product" but rather the same optional-scope shape `pipeline_tariff.product_id` already uses (`NULL` = all products, non-NULL = this specific cycle instance is dedicated to one product — e.g. a pipeline running a separate cycle exclusively for one crude grade). `ALTER TABLE dbo.pipeline_cycle ADD product_id INT NULL` + FK to `dbo.product` + `ix_pc_product` index (`database/74_...sql` / `V74__pipeline_cycle_product_scope.sql`, byte-identical, confirmed via `diff`).
  - Frontend: `PipelineCycle.productId`/`productName` added to `types.ts`; new "Product (blank = all products on this pipeline)" `<Select allowClear>` in `PipelineCyclesPage.tsx`'s drawer (sourced from `useTableRows('product')`, same pattern as `PipelineTariffsPage.tsx`); new grid column showing the product code/name or "All products". Mock: `computePipelineCycle()` now also denormalizes `productName` from `referenceRowSeed.product`; reseeded the 4 existing rows — the 3 Interconnector UK gas cycles stay `productId: null` (single-commodity pipeline, product-agnostic), Capline's `D+1` cycle set to `productId: 2` (WTI) with an updated name/notes demonstrating the product-specific case.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome: grid shows "All products" for the 3 gas cycles and "West Texas Inte…" for the WTI cycle; opening that row's Edit drawer correctly pre-selects "WTI-CRUDE — West Texas Intermediate" in the new Product field; zero console errors.
- **Built real CRUD + bulk Excel upload for individual holiday dates (`dbo.holiday`) — the annual-extension gap flagged (and deferred) in the previous entry.** User asked for both a manual "add one" page and a bulk-upload feature. While building, found the frontend's `CalendarHoliday` type had drifted from the real DB schema: it carried invented `isPartialDay`/`endTime` fields that don't exist on `dbo.holiday` (V1) — the real table has `is_settlement_holiday`/`is_trading_holiday` (both `BIT NOT NULL DEFAULT 1`). Fixed the type to match the DB (`isSettlementHoliday`/`isTradingHoliday`) rather than building new UI atop fictional columns; remapped the two existing "early close" seed rows (Christmas Eve, New Year's Eve) to `isSettlementHoliday: true, isTradingHoliday: false` (settlement closes, trading still occurs) as the closest real-world reading the two actual booleans support.
  - Previously this sub-resource was 100% read-only/mocked (`GET /holiday-calendars/:id/holidays` only, static seed data, no create/delete anywhere). Added real POST/DELETE/bulk-POST mock handlers (`etrmHandlers.ts`) that mutate the per-calendar `holidayDates` store and keep the parent calendar's denormalized `holidayCount` in sync on every add/delete/bulk-import.
  - Bulk upload follows the exact `LegalEntityListPage`/`excelTemplate.ts`/`excelUpload.ts` precedent (the only existing bulk-import pattern in the app): new `excelTemplateHolidays.ts` (exceljs template generator, scoped to one calendar since the calendar is fixed by the drawer context, not a spreadsheet column), `excelUploadHolidays.ts` (parses + validates date format and required name, **rejects** — not upserts — duplicate dates both against the calendar's existing holidays and within the same batch, mirroring the DB's `uq_holiday_date (calendar_id, holiday_date)` constraint), and `HolidayUploadReviewModal.tsx` (Ready-to-import / Rejected tabs, same shape as `LegalEntityUploadReviewModal.tsx`).
  - Rebuilt the holiday-viewing `HolidayDrawer` (`HolidayCalendarsPage.tsx`) from a static two-table (this-year/next-year) read-only view into one sorted, editable table: Template/Upload/Add Holiday buttons in the drawer header, a small `AddHolidayModal` for manual entry (date, name, two switches), and a per-row delete (`Popconfirm` → hard `DELETE`, not deactivate — `dbo.holiday` has no `is_active` column, so a real delete is the correct operation here, not an invented soft-delete).
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome end to end: opened LON calendar's holiday drawer, added "St. Patrick's Day" manually (toast, row appended correctly sorted), built and uploaded a 2-row `.xlsx` via the real file input (review modal showed both rows passing validation), imported them (toast "Imported 2 holidays", both rows appeared), deleted one (toast "Holiday removed", row gone) — zero functional console errors (only a pre-existing unrelated antd Tooltip deprecation warning). Also caught and fixed a real bug surfaced during this same pass: the `AddHolidayModal` used the deprecated antd `destroyOnClose` prop (this codebase's convention, confirmed via grep across 7+ other modals/drawers, is `destroyOnHidden`).
- **Built the missing `pipeline_cycle` frontend page — no new migration, table already existed in V4 with zero frontend representation.** User asked whether pipeline cycles had been added and wanted an "auto-extend every year" button. Researched before building (real-world NAESB US gas-pipeline nomination standards and UK UNC within-day cycles) and found `pipeline_cycle`'s columns (`nomination_deadline`/`confirmation_deadline`/`scheduling_deadline`/`effective_start`/`effective_end` as `TIME`, `applies_to_days`) model a **standing rule**, not a per-year instance — real pipelines file these once and rarely change them (e.g. FERC Order 809/587-W), so there's nothing year-bound on this table to "extend." The genuinely annual artifact in this domain is `dbo.holiday` (individual holiday dates, calendar_id FK'd from `pipeline_cycle`) — that table exists in V1 but has **zero backend/frontend wiring today** (holiday calendars are 100% MSW-mocked, seeded only through 2026, no roll-forward feature anywhere in the codebase). Flagged this to the user via AskUserQuestion; they chose to scope this session to just the `pipeline_cycle` page and defer the holiday roll-forward idea.
  - Built same pattern as the other 6 logistics pages this doc already documents: `types.ts`/`api.ts`/`hooks.ts`/`PipelineCyclesPage.tsx` under `features/logistics/pipeline-cycles/`, `computePipelineCycle()` denormalizing `pipelineName` (from `pipelinesStore`) and `calendarName` (from `holidayCalendarsStore`, via the `calendar_id` FK to `holiday_calendar`), `AppRouter.tsx` route `/logistics/pipeline-cycles`, `MasterDataHub.tsx` flip to `live: true`. `TimePicker format="HH:mm"` for the five `TIME` columns (matches `PeriodsPage.tsx`'s existing pattern for `startTimeUtc`/`endTimeUtc`).
  - Seeded 4 realistic rows: 3 `INTRADAY` WD1/WD2/WD3 cycles on Interconnector UK (matching the DB migration's own NBP-style comment) plus 1 `DAILY` D+1 cycle on Capline Crude Pipeline.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and headless Chrome: grid renders all 4 seed rows with resolved pipeline names; New Cycle drawer opens with all fields incl. time pickers and the holiday-calendar select; filled and saved a new `M1`/`DAILY` cycle end-to-end — toast fired, new row appeared with denormalized pipeline name, zero console errors.
- **Bidirectional Market ↔ Product linking, plus fixed a real FK-as-raw-number gap on the Markets page.** User flagged that the Trade Blotter's Market select being filtered only by broad `commodityType` (see entry below) isn't the correct scoping at all. **Deferred, per user's explicit request ("let's fix this later") — noting the corrected design here so it isn't lost:** the Market select should be scoped **purely by the `market_product` link for the selected `productId`** — no `commodityType`-based filtering at all (the commodity filter added in the entry below should be *removed*, not kept as a fallback). Concretely: `marketOptionsFor` in `TradeBlotter.tsx` (currently filters `Market.commodityType === commodityType`) should instead look up `market_product` rows for the leg's `productId` (mirroring `useProductMarkets`/the `marketProductsStore` join used on `ProductsPage.tsx`'s Markets tab) and only offer those markets. Open question for when this is picked up: what to show when no product is selected yet on the leg (empty list vs. all markets vs. disabled field until a product is chosen) — decide then, don't guess now.
  - Separately, user asked for Markets↔Products to be linkable from either page (previously: Markets → Market Products drawer already had an "add product" form, Products → Markets tab was read-only and told the user to "manage from Markets"). Implemented both directions properly:
  - **Fixed a real, pre-existing gap while touching the Markets page's existing "Link Product" form** (`MarketsPage.tsx`'s `MarketProductsDrawer`): `productId` was a raw `InputNumber` asking the admin to type a numeric product ID from memory — the same class of bug already fixed elsewhere in the app for Static Data FK columns (V59). Replaced with a searchable `<Select>` sourced from `useProducts()`.
  - Also fixed a latent mock-only bug this surfaced: the `POST /markets/:id/products` handler never denormalized `productCode`/`productName` onto the new row (only the hand-seeded rows had them baked in) — any product linked through the existing form was silently missing its display name. Fixed by looking up the product in `productsStore` by `productId` at write time.
  - **Added the reverse direction on `ProductsPage.tsx`'s Markets tab** (previously view-only): a new "Link Market" button + inline form (mirrors the Markets-side form: market select, ticker, lot size, LTD/FND offsets, price precision), backed by a new `useLinkMarketToProduct(productId)` hook (`products/hooks.ts`) that calls the *same* `marketsApi.addProduct(marketId, ...)` endpoint the Markets page uses — both pages write through the identical `market_product` bridge row, so linking from either side updates the same record (no new backend/mock endpoint needed, since `GET /products/:id/markets` already dynamically joins `marketProductsStore` on every read).
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean), a full production build, and headless Chrome: Markets → ICE_BRENT → Link Product now shows a proper searchable product dropdown (not a bare number field); Products → CBOT-CORN → Markets → Link Market → picked ICE_TTF → toast "Market linked." → the new row appeared immediately in the product's own Markets tab with CCY/status resolved correctly.
- **Follow-up audit + fix: three more `TradeBlotter.tsx` selects had the same unfiltered-by-commodity bug as the UoM fix below, and the same fix pattern applied.** After the UoM fix, asked whether the same class of bug existed elsewhere; an Explore-agent audit of every `<Select>` in `TradeBlotter.tsx` confirmed three more real gaps, in priority order (all frontend-only, no migration):
  - **Market select** (`marketId`) — `Market.commodityType` is already a direct field on the entity; was building `markets` into options completely unfiltered. Added `marketOptionsFor(commodityType)` (exact match on `Market.commodityType`).
  - **Product select** (`productId`, both the leg/order drawer and the trade-item drawer) — `Product.commodityId` plus the existing `resolveCommodityType()` resolver (already used by `ProductsPage.tsx` for the same purpose) were never applied in `TradeBlotter.tsx`. Added `productOptionsFor(commodityType)`, using a new `COMMODITY_TRADE_TO_BROAD` map since the `commodity` master table only has 5 broad buckets (OIL/POWER/GAS/AGRICULTURAL/METALS) while trades use 9 (`CommodityTypeTrade`) — LNG products are filed under the GAS bucket in this mock (no separate LNG commodity row exists; `JKM-LNG`'s `commodityId` resolves to GAS), so `LNG` maps to `'GAS'` in the lookup; `FREIGHT`/`RINS`/`ENVIRONMENTAL` are deliberately absent from the map (confirmed via their seeded orders, which all have `productId: null` and use `freightDetail`/`rinDetail`/`environmentalDetail` instead — these commodity types don't reference `dbo.product` at all, so an empty, still-optional product list for them is correct, not a bug).
  - **Location-based selects** (`locationOpts`, shared across oil load/discharge ports, LNG terminals, metals warehouses, freight ports, and the generic delivery-location field) — `Location.commodityType: CommodityType | null` exists specifically for this (`null` = cross-commodity port like Rotterdam) but was never read. Added `locationOptionsFor(commodityType)`, replacing the single static `locationOpts` memo with a per-commodity function (same shape as `uomOptionsFor`).
  - Deliberately left `pricingRuleId` alone — `PricingRule` has no commodity/product field at all, and unlike the other three, it's not obvious real rules should be scoped this way (some formula rules may legitimately be commodity-agnostic); flagged for a future product decision rather than guessed at.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean), a full production build, and headless Chrome: an OIL trade's leg drawer now shows only oil products/markets/ports (`BRENT-CRUDE`/`WTI-CRUDE`/etc., `ICE_BRENT`/`NYMEX_WTI`/`OTC_NS_CRUDE`, `SULLOM-VOE`/`RAS-TANURA`/`CUSHING-OK`/`ROTTERDAM` — correctly excluding `NBP-UK`/`FREEPORT-LNG`/`LME-WAREHOUSE`); GAS and METALS trades likewise show only their own scoped products/markets (e.g. METALS → `LME_COPPER`/`LME_ALUMINIUM` only).
- **Fixed the Trade Blotter's quantity UoM dropdown showing every unit of measure regardless of the trade's commodity — frontend-only fix, no migration needed.** User flagged that the leg/order and trade-item quantity UoM selects (`TradeBlotter.tsx`) offered all 19 `unit_of_measure` mock rows (e.g. TROY_OZ, BUSHEL, GWH all showing up on an OIL leg) even though the real backend schema already models this: `dbo.unit_of_measure.commodity_type` (V55-refactored to an FK on `lookup_value`) scopes each UoM row to a commodity, with `NULL` meaning cross-commodity. The frontend mock's `Uom` type only had a free-text `commodityHint` (e.g. `'Natural gas (US), LNG'`) with no structured field to filter on — that was the actual root cause, not the dropdown code itself. Fix: added `Uom.commodityTypes: CommodityType[] | null` (`features/reference/uom/types.ts`, `null` = universal/cross-commodity, matching the DB's own convention; array rather than the single-nullable shape `UomConversion.commodityType` uses, since real-world units like MWH are legitimately valid for both POWER and GAS — a single value would have forced an artificial pick), populated all 19 seed rows in `etrmHandlers.ts` from their existing `commodityHint` text (e.g. MWH → `['POWER','GAS']`, MT → `null` since it's used across all physical commodities, BBL → `['OIL']`), and added a `uomOptionsFor(commodityType)` filter in `TradeBlotter.tsx` (replacing the single unfiltered `uomOpts` memo) wired into both the leg/order drawer (via `orderCommodity`, which already existed as a prop but was never used for this) and the trade-item drawer (via `selectedTrade?.commodityType`, since `TradeItem`/`TradeOrder` don't carry their own commodity field independent of the parent trade).
  - Also built the actual admin surface for this on `UomPage.tsx` (`/reference/uom`, the "Units of Measure" Static Data page): a new "Allowed Commodities" grid column (tag list, or "All" when null) and an `<Select mode="multiple">` form field so master-data admins can edit which commodities each unit applies to, rather than this being a hardcoded, un-editable mapping.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean), a full production build, and headless Chrome: opening "New Leg" on an existing GAS trade (TRD-2026-00003) shows only `MT, MWH, MMBTU, THERM, M3, SCFD, GJ, SCM, MMSCM` in the UoM dropdown (previously all 19); the same drawer on an OIL trade (TRD-2026-00001) shows only `BBL, MT, GAL, LTR, CBM`; the Units of Measure admin page's MWH row correctly shows/edits `POWER, GAS` in a new "Allowed Commodities" column and form field.

  - **Discovered and flagged rather than silently designed: `nomination` and `delivery_instruction` have zero SQL schema anywhere** (`grep -rln "dbo.nomination\b\|dbo.delivery_instruction\b" database/*.sql` returns nothing) — qualitatively different from every other backlog item, which all had real backend intent to build from. Asked the user rather than inventing new schema (consistent with this session's own "research/verify before schema" lesson); user chose to skip both for now. These remain the only two `live: false` items left in the entire 4-group backlog and need a schema-design pass (not just frontend work) before they can be built.

- **Second full "entity page" group: Credit & Collateral (`bank_guarantee`, `insurance_policy`, `margin_account`, `collateral`) — no new migration needed, all four tables already existed in `05_financial_operational_md.sql` with no registry-table involvement (they're full entity pages, not Static Data).** Same pattern as the Counterparty Agreements group: `types.ts`/`api.ts`/`hooks.ts`/`Page.tsx` per entity, mock store + `computeXxx()` denormalization handler pair before `crudHandlers()`, `AppRouter.tsx` route, `MasterDataHub.tsx` flip to `live: true`.

- **V72 — first full "entity page" group from `MasterDataHub.tsx`'s `live: false` backlog: Counterparty Agreements (`credit_term`, `netting_agreement`, `cp_commercial_terms`, `cp_gtc_agreement`).** User approved building out all 4 backlog groups (~21 entities); started with the smallest. - **V71 — `collateral_type`, `event_category`/`event_type`, `external_system` registered as Static Data.** Continuing the V70 review, five candidate tables had been deliberately excluded from `MasterDataHub.tsx`'s plan (`event_category`, `event_type`, `collateral_type`, `interest_rate_index` [built in V70], `pricing_trigger_event_type`, `external_system`) — investigated why each was left out rather than assuming they were overlooked. - **V70 — whole-project master-data review: registered the first batch of genuine Static Data registry orphans (`insurance_provider`, `interest_rate_index`, `regulatory_report_type`, `transport_operator`), fixed a real `lookup_value` backend/frontend registry mismatch, and corrected stale `MasterDataHub.tsx` entries.** User asked for a full project review of what master data is still missing. Three parallel Explore-agent audits covered: (1) a mechanical sweep of every `CREATE TABLE` in `database/*.sql` against every `master_data_table_registry` INSERT, surfacing ~26 candidate orphans; (2) genuine gaps in Oil/Gas/Freight/Carbon/RINs; (3) genuine gaps in Counterparty/Credit/Contracts/Finance/Admin. Before implementing anything, cross-checked the candidate-orphan list against the actual frontend (`find` for dedicated feature pages, and `MasterDataHub.tsx`'s existing `live: true/false` backlog, which turned out to be a far more authoritative source than the SQL-only sweep) — this eliminated the large majority as false positives: `unit_of_measure`, `holiday_calendar`, `exchange`, `price_source`, `mot_type`, `location_type`, `pricing_type`, `inspection_type`, `transport_document_type`, `base_date_event_type`, `business_day_convention_type`, `gl_account`, `carbon_registry`, `emission_scheme`, `environmental_product`, `rin_fuel_category` all already have either a dedicated feature page or a working frontend mock entry (`PARENT_LOOKUP_TABLES`) — only the real backend SQL registry was missing rows for them, which doesn't affect the actual running prototype (100% MSW-mock-driven today). Narrowed to 4 genuine, previously-unbuilt-anywhere tables, all of which independently already appeared in `MasterDataHub.tsx`'s curated `live: false` backlog (confirming they were planned, not overlooked): `insurance_provider`, `interest_rate_index`, `regulatory_report_type`, `transport_operator`. Registered all four (V70, real backend SQL) and built full frontend `TABLE_DEFS`/`registrySeed`/`rowSeed` entries with real seed data drawn from each table's actual SQL `INSERT` statements where available. Added lightweight `counterparty` id/code/name mirror entries (same FK-resolution-only pattern as `product`/`storage_facility` from V65/V66) since `insurance_provider.counterparty_id` and `transport_operator.counterparty_id` needed it.
  - Also fixed a real discrepancy found along the way: V63 added `lookup_value` to the frontend mock's `registrySeed` but never actually inserted the corresponding row into the real backend SQL's `master_data_table_registry` — prototype and intended real schema had quietly diverged.

- **V69 — `commodity_grade_standard` rescoped from `commodity_family_id` to `product_id`; wired into the Trade Blotter to auto-populate price adjustments.** User asked, after V67 shipped: is a grade schedule per commodity or per product, and can the actual delivered grade be captured in the blotter to drive pricing? Researched real practice: CBOT's own rulebook (Chapter 10 Corn, Chapter 14 Wheat) publishes a **separate** grade/class differential schedule per listed contract — Corn's cents-per-bushel schedule is not Wheat's, even though both list under the same GRAINS `commodity_family`. V67's family-level scope was therefore wrong — it implied Corn and Wheat share one schedule. Rescoped the FK to `product_id` (ALTER, backfilled against CBOT-CORN, dropped the old FK/column, matching the established ALTER-not-DROP+CREATE convention). Also researched crude oil's equivalent (pipeline "quality bank" adjustments, computed per-cargo from actual assay vs. reference — RBN Energy/Allocation Specialists LLC methodology) and confirmed that per-trade capture mechanism already exists here (`trade_order_price_adjustment`, V46, `adjustment_type` already includes QUALITY_PREMIUM/QUALITY_DISCOUNT/ASSAY) — what was missing was linking the two. Added a nullable `grade_standard_id` FK on `trade_order_price_adjustment` (NULL for manual/assay-computed adjustments, populated when derived from a published grade standard) and a new `GradeDeliveredSelect` in `TradeBlotter.tsx`'s Price Adjustments section: picking a grade for the order's product auto-adds a price-adjustment row (type/value/currency/UoM from the grade standard, `gradeStandardId` traced via a hidden `Form.Item` matching the existing `tradeId`/`orderId` hidden-field pattern) while manual entry remains fully available for cargo/assay-based adjustments that have no published schedule.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean); V69 migration pair byte-identical; no constraint-name collisions.
- **V65–V68 — LNG/Power/Agri/Metals master-data review, researched against real industry structure (GIIGNL LNG terminology, ISO/RTO power market design, USDA grain grading, LME warehouse/brand/warrant conventions) and implemented to fit the existing generic patterns.** User asked to review these four commodity classes' master data specifically and "link them correctly that works for single source of GUI" — i.e. everything should surface through the one generic Tier 2 Static Data screen, not a bespoke one-off UI per table. An Explore-agent audit established ground truth first (what already exists vs. what's genuinely thin), then each gap was closed:
  - **V65 — Power registry orphans (no new schema).** Power turned out to be the most mature of the four (V11/V12/V51: balancing authorities, transmission zones, interconnectors, generation assets, load shapes, transmission rights) but only 3 of 8 real tables were ever registered in `master_data_table_registry` — `interconnector`, `generation_asset`, `power_product_detail`, and `transmission_right_type` had real schemas and seed data but were invisible in the Static Data UI. Registered all four. Deliberately did NOT register `trade_transmission_right_detail` — it's a 1:1 *trade* extension (same family as `trade_swap_detail`/`trade_option_detail`), correctly managed inline from the Trade Blotter, not master data; registering it would have been the same category error in the other direction.
  - **Found and fixed a real, pre-existing frontend bug while wiring this up**: the mock's `transmission_right_type` was a "simple lookup" entry (`PARENT_LOOKUP_TABLES`) with data (FTR/PTR/ATR) that didn't even match the real V12-seeded codes (FTR/CRR/TCC), and the real schema is richer (FK to balancing_authority, two enum columns) than the simple lookup shape supports. Replaced it with a full `TABLE_DEFS` entry matching the real schema and real seed data.
  - **V66 — `lng_terminal_detail`**: new 1:1 extension of `storage_facility` (only populated for `LNG_TANK` rows) — regas send-out capacity (import) or liquefaction nameplate MTPA (export), storage tank/berth count, and min/max cargo-lot size. `storage_facility` itself had no terminal-level capacity concept beyond a single generic `capacity` field.
  - **V67 — `commodity_grade_standard`**: new table for named grade tiers (e.g. USDA No. 2 Yellow Corn) with a flat price adjustment vs. the contract par grade — the genuinely missing piece in Agri master data (quality was already well covered generically via `product_spec_template`/`spec_parameter`, but there was no actual *grade* concept, just loose parameter values). Linked from `commodity_family`, not `product`, since a grade standard is a market-level convention. Deliberately kept separate from the per-parameter spec system to avoid duplicating it.
  - **V68 — `metal_brand`**: new table for an LME-style approved brand register (producer + metal form: cathode/ingot/wire rod/etc., country of origin, approval/delisting date) — replaces the previous boolean-only `LME_BRAND` spec flag, which couldn't represent the real mechanism (a specific producer's brand on a specific form is what's actually deliverable/warrantable, not just "has an LME brand: yes/no").
  - **Cross-store FK-resolution gap found and worked around consistently**: several new FK columns point at tables (`product`, `storage_facility`) that have their own dedicated feature pages with separate mock stores, not present in the generic Static Data mock's `rowSeed` — the same gap `transmission_zone.location_id` had already silently accepted by omission. Added lightweight id/code/name-only mirror entries for `product` and `storage_facility` (metadata + rows, but deliberately **not** added to `registrySeed`, so they resolve FK labels correctly without creating a duplicate products/storage-facilities tab — the dedicated pages remain the single source of truth for editing those records).
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean) and a full audit of all four new migration files: byte-identical `database/`↔backend pairs, no constraint/index name collisions against the rest of `database/`.
- **Silent-mutation-failure sweep + RolesPage header/loading fix, continuing the GUI audit's punch list.** Added the standard `onError: (e: ProblemDetail) => message.error(...)` pattern (matching `organization/desks/hooks.ts`'s established shape) to every mutation that was missing it: `features/trade/hooks.ts` (all 8 trade/trade-order/trade-item mutations — the busiest module in the app, previously failed completely silently on save/cancel/confirm/delete errors), `admin/roles/hooks.ts` (9 mutations — role CRUD/submit/approve/reject + assignment approve/reject/revoke), and the four one-line reference-data hook files (`reference/currencies`, `reference/incoterms`, `reference/countries`, `reference/uom`).
  - `RolesPage.tsx`: swapped its ad-hoc `<Title>`/`<Text>` header for the shared `PageHeader` component (`moduleGroup="admin"`, matching the pattern used by all 51 other page files); added the missing `loading` prop to the User Assignments tab's table (previously flashed an empty table on load while the Roles tab correctly showed a spinner).
  - Investigated the audit's "several tables lack a custom empty state" finding (`TradeBlotterPage`, `CarbonRegistriesPage`, `LocationsPage`, `RinTransactionsPage`, `ExchangesPage`) and found it was **not actually a gap** — all five use the shared `SmartGrid` component, which already applies a uniform `overlayNoRowsTemplate` ("No records found") to every grid via `AgGridReact`, so they're already consistent with each other; no fix needed.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean).
- **Fixed money/date validation gaps in Credit & Risk pages, found via a targeted GUI/validation audit.** User asked for a broader review of missing field validation and UI polish; two Explore-agent audits (validation gaps, GUI/UX consistency) surfaced a prioritized list — user chose to fix the money/date validation gaps first (highest risk since it's financial/risk data). Fixed:
  - `CreditLimitsPage.tsx` — `limitAmount`, `usedAmount`, `collateralOffset`, `tempUpliftAmount`, and the sub-limit list's `subLimitAmount`/`usedAmount` now reject negative values (`min={0}` + a matching Form rule); `effectiveDate`/`expiryDate` now cross-validate (expiry can't be before effective).
  - `MarginAgreementsPage.tsx` — `thresholdAmount`, `cpThresholdAmount`, `mtaAmount`, `roundingAmount`, `independentAmount` all get `min={0}`; `effectiveDate`/`expiryDate` cross-validated the same way.
  - `LettersOfCreditPage.tsx` — `lcAmount`, `drawdownAmount`, `issuedAmount`, `presentationDeadlineDays`, `autoRenewalDays` all get `min={0}`; `issueDate`/`expiryDate` cross-validated. Deliberately did NOT cap `drawdownAmount`/`issuedAmount` against `lcAmount` — the field's own hint text says revolving LCs can have `issuedAmount` exceed face value, so a hard cap would be a wrong constraint.
  - `VesselsPage.tsx` — `guaranteedBoilOffRatePctPerDay` had a `step` but no bounds at all (same bug class as the `versionYear` fix); added `min={0} max={5}` (realistic LNG boil-off range).
  - TS gotcha hit and fixed: adding a literal `min={0}` to a plain (non-generic) `InputNumber` that also has a custom `parser` returning `number` caused TS to infer the component's value type as the literal `0` instead of `number`, conflicting with the parser's return type. Fixed with `min={0 as number}` on the affected instances (in `LettersOfCreditPage.tsx`/`MarginAgreementsPage.tsx`) rather than adding an explicit `<InputNumber<number>>` generic everywhere, to keep the diff minimal.
  - Audit also surfaced (not yet fixed, deferred by user choice): Trade Blotter's ~8 order mutations have zero error feedback (`features/trade/hooks.ts` has no `onError`/`message.error` anywhere); several tables lack custom empty states (`TradeBlotterPage`, `CarbonRegistriesPage`, `LocationsPage`, `RinTransactionsPage`, `ExchangesPage`); `RolesPage.tsx` uses an ad-hoc header instead of the shared `PageHeader` and has an inconsistent `loading` prop between its two tabs' tables. Phone number fields have no format validation anywhere in the app (systemic, not a single-file gap) — noted but not fixed.
  - Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean).
- **Added missing numeric-range validation for year-like Static Data fields, then upgraded the input to a year-picker calendar.** User flagged `incoterm.versionYear` as unvalidated — the generic Tier 2 form rendered it as a bare `InputNumber` with no bounds, so a user could save `-5`, `3.7`, or `99999` as an Incoterms version year. Added a generic rule (matching the existing `isoRules`/`isCodeColumn` pattern, not a one-off for this table): any `number`-kind column whose name ends in "Year" (`isYearColumn` — catches `versionYear`, and any future `*Year` column added to Static Data without further code changes) gets `min=1900`, `max=currentYear+5`, integer-only, enforced both live and as a submit-time Form rule (`yearRules()`), plus a hint showing the valid range. User then asked for a calendar picker for the same field — replaced the constrained `InputNumber` with antd's `DatePicker` in `picker="year"` mode (a year-grid calendar, not a full date calendar), `disabledDate` enforcing the same min/max bounds; since the stored value is a plain number (e.g. `2020`) not a dayjs object, the `Form.Item` gets conditional `getValueProps`/`normalize` (number ↔ `dayjs(..., 'YYYY')`) only for year columns — the grid/list view is unaffected since it reads the raw stored row value, not the form's display transform. Checked dedicated (non-generic) pages with year fields for the same gap — `TradeBlotter.tsx`'s `rinDetail.vintageYear`/`environmentalDetail.vintageYear` and `RinTransactionsPage.tsx`'s `vintageYear` (a constrained dropdown, not free entry) already had `min`/`max` bounds, so `incoterm.versionYear` was the one real gap; left as plain bounded `InputNumber`/`Select` there rather than converting to a calendar too, since that wasn't asked for. Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean).
- **Field hints added everywhere they were missing.** First pass added generic, metadata-derived hints (`columnHint()`) to the Tier 2 Static Data admin form (`ReferenceDataTable.tsx`), the one form driven purely by DB-derived metadata rather than hand-written fields. Second pass (user: "still missing for some") audited every remaining dedicated feature form for the `hint()`/`FieldHint` tooltip pattern used across ~30 other pages and found it missing entirely from: `DeskFormDrawer.tsx`, `BookFormDrawer.tsx`, `LegalEntityFormDrawer.tsx`, `GuaranteeFormDrawer.tsx`, `CounterpartyFormPage.tsx`, and all four counterparty child-record sections (`BankAccountsSection`, `TaxRegistrationsSection`, `ContactsSection`, `AddressesSection`) — added hand-authored ETRM-domain hints to the non-obvious fields in each (e.g. LEI Code, parent-company toggles, book type distinctions, guarantor/principal/beneficiary roles, IBAN/SWIFT, KYC status). `GuaranteeFormDrawer.tsx`'s `RoleField` sub-component needed a small structural change (new `hintText` prop, wraps its plain-string `Typography.Text` label with `hint()`) since its label isn't a `Form.Item` label. Only `LoginPage.tsx` (not a domain form) and `ChildRecordSection.tsx` (generic wrapper — renders no labels of its own) remain without hints, correctly. Verified via `tsc -b --noEmit` (clean).
- **Full front/back/SQL/docs review pass — 4 real bugs found and fixed, none by guessing, all via targeted Explore-agent audits + manual verification:**
